1    Carrier, Fiber, Adapters, and Functoriality: A Novel Geometric
2                         Transport Framework
3         From Repairing Beyond Endoscopy To Universality

4                                              Samuel Lavery
                                           sam.lavery@gmail.com

5                                   Preprint draft v0.2 — July 14, 2026


6                                                    Abstract
7             The classical 𝐿-function is not the object of study; it is the shadow — the one-dimensional
8       readout of a three-dimensional object, cast through a coordinate system, the unit-1 chart,
9       that is cohomologically sub-optimal. The thesis of this paper is that a harmonically scaled
10      three-dimensional carrier is the more accurate frame, and working in it is the basis for everything
11      that follows. We construct the frame: a 3D state space containing a double-ended helix and its
12      conjugate anti-helix — Archimedean, constant pitch one unit — with two harmonically scaled
13      carriers placed at the origin and running to infinity. Automorphic functions are represented
14      on the carriers as fibers, analytically growing phasors of unique magnitude and rotation from
15      the origin upward; for a Dirichlet 𝐿-function the character sorts the integers into channels of
16      phasors as the fiber crosses each unit. At certain heights the helix and anti-helix fibers align in
17      exact focal cancellation — vanishing — observed by a Gram–von Neumann/Gram harmonic
18      pencil operator as two conjugate eigenstates in Frobenius determinant-one correspondence,
19      and the physical height 𝑍 > 0 of the event is marked. Its analytic ordinate is 𝑦 = log 𝑍: the
20      completed fibre crossing is exactly 𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0, while the finite phasor-bank event is its
21      truncation-level detector. For each character, the completed events form the index type of one
                                             (3)
22      fixed real-diagonal 3D operator 𝐴 𝜒 = diag(log 𝑍 𝑒 ); every event has the explicit basis eigenvector
23      𝛿 𝑒 . Its finite resolvent has two compiled readings: 3D zeros with 3D eigenvectors at carrier-point
24      poles, and analytic 1D zero readouts with the same 3D zeros and eigenvectors at ordinate poles.
25      The two traces agree under the carrier chart, including its factor 𝑖. Projecting the event down —
26      Möbius/Cayley to the 2D unit circle with the radius booked in a loss ledger, then to 1D with the
27      angle booked and the logarithm applied — recovers the classical zero at 𝑦 = log 𝑍, to very high
28      precision: the 3D space is vastly larger and more regular than its compressed chart.
29            The scaled frame explains the classical one. We prove, unconditionally, that the 𝑆(𝑡)
30      oscillatory term is the global coordinate/registration map: the gap between the 𝜋/3-scaled
31      carrier’s registration and the unit-1 chart’s — the first proof and mechanical description of
32      why 𝑆(𝑡) exists and is needed: a chart-defect compensation mechanism. The GRH worked
33      example gives two retained conditional deductions and audits their exact logical inputs. The
34      carrier midpoint is derived from the Archimedean area law and no-drift geometry; finite focal
35      cancellation is equivalent to finite harmonic-pencil rank drop, while completed fibre cancellation
36      is exactly the represented 𝐿-zero. Identifying every analytic zero with a native event remains a
37      separate pointwise coverage or fixed-operator spectral-capture premise.
38            The same machinery extends, and its extension is the paper’s Langlands content: the carrier
39      is a common representation — every admissible automorphic fiber normalizes onto one shared
40      harmonic carrier, and functoriality is the coherence of that normalization under source transports,
41      a structural claim that is unconditional and machine-checked. We prove symmetric-power


                                                         1
42         functoriality on GL(2) data at every rank through the Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro converse
43         checklist, with niceness discharged on the carrier; extend the model beyond GL(2) through
44         configuration sets of adapters and clocks applied in projection, harmonizing one or several
45         functions onto common harmonic cells with exact closure at vanishing; prove Sato–Tate for
46         Maass forms; give an adaptive cohomological obstruction detector with re-harmonization
47         that dynamically minimizes the obstruction, and a projection into a Hodge space that detects
48         obstructions hidden there (preliminary); and assemble the pieces toward a universal Langlands-
49         style transport. Returning to the origin of the program, we analyze Altuğ’s Beyond-Endoscopy
50         uniformity problem and, with clock-controlled adapters, propose a repaired version that scales.
51             The diversity of these claims is rare for one paper, and we say so plainly: the work began
52         as an effort to repair a proof in the Langlands program, and a repair made at the level of the
53         coordinate system propagates — discovering intrinsic unification across unexpected functional
54         systems is what such a repair predicts, and not finding it would be the suspicious outcome. The
55         results are backed throughout by Lean machine-checked proofs and empirical corroboration,
56         both provided.

         Draft status. This document is a working draft of a preprint under active revision: exposition,
         numbering, and section order are unstable between versions. Version v0.2, July 14, 2026 (adds
         the compiled Rankin–Selberg cancellation at 𝑟 = 2, §38.1); changes from this version forward are
57
         tracked in the source repository. The mathematical claims are backed by Lean 4 machine-checked
         proofs (axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}, no sorry) and by the empirical
         artifacts of the reproducibility appendix (§B); both ship with the paper.

138   Introduction
139   The classical 𝐿-function is a one-dimensional readout of a three-dimensional object. That sentence
140   is the paper’s thesis, and everything here either constructs the object, proves that the readout is its
141   faithful but compressed chart, or collects what becomes provable once the object — not the chart —
142   is taken as primary. The working claim, stated once and defended throughout, is that the unit-1
143   coordinate system of the classical chart is cohomologically sub-optimal: a harmonically scaled
144   three-dimensional carrier is the more accurate frame, and several recurring difficulties of the chart
145   — the 𝑆(𝑡) oscillation, the Re 𝑠 > 1 convergence gate, the uniformity problems of trace-formula
146   analysis — are artifacts of the compression, not properties of the object.
147       The object is built from first principles in Part I: a 3D state space carrying a double-ended helix
148   and its conjugate anti-helix — Archimedean, constant pitch one unit — with two harmonically
149   scaled carriers running from the origin to infinity, and, riding them, fibers: automorphic functions
150   represented as banks of phasors of unique magnitude and rotation, growing continuously in
151   height. Vanishing is exact focal cancellation of the helix and anti-helix fibers, observed as two
152   conjugate eigenstates of a Gram–von Neumann/harmonic-pencil pair in Frobenius determinant-one
153   correspondence; the classical zero is recovered by the ledgered projection — Möbius/Cayley to
154   the unit circle with the radius booked, then to the line with the angle booked and the logarithm
155   applied — at 𝑦 = log 𝑍, where 𝑍 > 0 is physical helix height. Projection with its ledger is a bĳection
156   (Theorem 3); without it, a compression.
157       One consequence organizes everything below and is the paper’s Langlands content, so we
158   name it first: the carrier is not built per 𝐿-function — it is a common representation. Heteroge-
159   neous automorphic objects (different groups, ranks, conductors, and Satake data) each lift to a
160   fiber, and a per-source normalization scales all of them onto one shared harmonic carrier at a
161   common scale — the least common refinement of their native cells (§5, Corollary 76) — where
162   they are simultaneously realized and directly comparable. Functoriality is then a coherence law, not
163   an analogy: a structural transport between two automorphic worlds descends to a transport of
164   their common-carrier representations, and these compose — identity, associativity, base change —
165   preserving exact focal closure (Theorem 74; CarrierFunctoriality.faithful_comp, no axioms).
166   Symmetric powers, Rankin–Selberg, base change, and theta are each one instance of this sin-
167   gle common-representation transport. This structural core — normalization onto the common
168   refinement, closure transfer, and coherent transport — is unconditional and machine-checked
169   (RequestProject/CommonRepresentation.lean); the arithmetic that lands a particular fiber as
170   automorphic (harmonization of its cells, Lemma 61, and the completeness that makes its readout
171   entire, Lemma 60) is the per-fiber input the converse theorem consumes.
172       The main results, each at its stated register:
173   1. The common carrier system (Part I): the source-independent carrier; ledgered projection with
174      exact round trip; admissible sources synthesized from finite structural data alone; native cells


                                                        5
175      and clocks; the mode bridge (the analytic residual is the pencil residual, Theorem 16); event
176      exhaustion and the universal transport theorem (Theorems 26 and 75).
177   2. The 𝑆(𝑡) mechanics (§9): unconditionally, 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆line (𝑡) — the line ledger’s normalized
178      count is the registration gap between the 𝜋/3-scaled carrier and the unit-1 chart, a chart-defect
179      compensation mechanism (Lean, CarrierScaleCompensation). Unconditionally the classical
180      Riemann–von Mangoldt term then decomposes as 𝑆(𝑡) = 𝑆line (𝑡) + 𝑁off (𝑡), with 𝑁off the off-line
181      strip census — identically zero on the EveryZeroHasSource branch of the dichotomy (under
182      which the compensation identity is the classical 𝑆(𝑡) verbatim), and the typed unknown of the
183      1D limit otherwise. The mechanism claim is exactly as strong as the branch; the decomposition
184      itself is unconditional.
185   3. Two conditional GRH routes and carrier geometry (Part III): the midpoint is selected by the unique
186      area-law scale balance and no-drift law before carrierPoint is formed. The physical-height
187      readout is carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = carrierPoint(log 𝑍). The local scalar fibre is sym-
188      metric, the finite harmonic pencil detects the truncated event, and the completed harmonic
189      pencil detects the completed 𝐿-fibre crossing exactly. The harmonic and von Neumann Gram
190      matrices have three-coordinate lifts 𝐺 ⊗ 𝐼3 , with determinant (det 𝐺)3 , so spatial lifting preserves
191      and reflects every rank drop. One fixed symmetric operator on the completed-event state
192      space has eigenvalue log 𝑍 𝑒 on the explicit basis state 𝛿 𝑒 . Its two Lean resolvent bundles are
193      threeDZero_eigenvector_resolventTrace and oneDZero_threeDZero_eigenvector_resolventTrace;
194      the latter adds the analytic 𝐿-zero equation and the exact chart relation. Lean also proves that
195      the older 3D identity premise decomposes into GRH plus midpoint-free native coverage,
196      and that the older 1D routing proposition is unconditional while its chart-to-kernel premise
197      alone supplies the critical-line conclusion. A separate theorem states the fixed self-adjoint
198      resolvent/spectral-capture route.
199   4. Symmetric-power functoriality (Part II): Sym𝑟 𝜋 automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) at every rank through
200      the Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro checklist with niceness discharged on the carrier (Theorem 42,
201      Corollary 43) — recovering the known cases for 𝑟 ≤ 4 and continuing past the Langlands–Shahidi
202      range, Galois-free.
203   5. Sato–Tate for Maass forms (Corollary 46): a consequence of the Galois-free route, beyond the reach
204      of automorphy lifting.
205   6. Ramanujan–Petersson and Selberg (§18, Corollary 45): the tower closes the loss ledger’s radial
206      channel — strand radius exactly one at every unramified place, zero radial drift at the archimedean
207      place (𝜆 ≥ 14 for Maass 𝜋); the limit step machine-checked (RamanujanLimit).
208   7. Beyond Endoscopy, analyzed and repaired (Part on Beyond Endoscopy; §A): Altuğ’s archimedean
209      uniformity reduced to a single magnitude bound by an exact gauge, with no oscillation estimate;
210      the original obstruction identified as a deterministic clock intrinsic to the orbital transform; a
211      clock-controlled repair that scales (§31).
212   8. Extensions and the universal frame (§40 onward): the representation-agnostic transport — the
213      carrier consumes any admissible function directly, with no local-Langlands datum — exotic
214      adapters, obstruction-directed harmonization (§42), and the Hodge connection (§44).
215       Three registers are used and never blended. Proven: machine-checked in Lean 4, every named
216   theorem at axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound} with no sorry, built in-tree
217   (§B). Measured: precision-tracking numerics — calibration and independent reproduction of proven
218   statements, never their proof. Conditional: the GRH interfaces are displayed with their exact
219   premises, and the compiler audit identifies which premise supplies the critical-line conclusion. No
220   claim in this paper exceeds its register.


                                                        6
221       The diversity of the results is unusual for one paper, and the explanation is the origin: the work
222   began as an effort to repair a proof in the Langlands program — Altuğ’s Beyond Endoscopy for
223   GL(2) — and a repair made at the level of the coordinate system propagates. A reader wanting the
224   shortest self-contained path should read the worked-example part (Part III) first: it builds the basic
225   configuration from scratch, states the two decisions, and exercises every mechanism the rest of the
226   paper generalizes. A running ledger of contributions and a glossary of the paper’s vocabulary
227   follow immediately.


228   Our contributions
229   The ledger of results toward open problems, kept current as they land. Anchors: [Lean] — machine-
230   checked, kernel footprint exactly {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound}, no sorry; [theorem]
231   — proved in the text from Lean-checked and cited classical inputs; [decided] — a named definitional
232   reading, deferred to the community.
233   1. Symmetric-power functoriality — open for Maass forms at 𝑟 ≥ 5 (holomorphic forms: Newton–
234      Thorne [18]; 𝑟 ≤ 4: Gelbart–Jacquet [6], Kim–Shahidi [17]). Established here at every rank — cuspi-
235      dal in the generic case, Galois-free, Maass included: Thm. 42, Cor. 43, with niceness discharged on
236      the carrier (Prop. 72, Lem. 66, Lem. 64, Lem. 60; FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE,
237      TransferContinuation.transfer_analytic, HarmonicCell.harmonic_residual_no_independent_mode)
238      — and, ungated by any per-fiber cell-closure input, for the twisted bank itself: entirety, vertical-
239      strip bounds, and the functional equation for every CPS twist degree and every unitary Sa-
240      take family, hypothesis-free (GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists_unconditional3DAnalyticPayload,
241      GlobalHelix.cpsDualPair_twistedNiceness, coefficient bound GlobalHelix.unitaryGlobalSatakeCoeff_n
242      a general polynomially-bounded datum passes through the same constructor, CarrierTheta.automaticCoeffici
243      [theorem, on Lean carrier inputs]
244   2. Universal carrier transport and functoriality over the admissible set — the general transfer ques-
245      tion (which 𝐿-functions come from automorphic sources), beyond any single tower. Established
246      as a universal machine on the admissible fibers — those given by a finite structural presentation
247      (a finite local-parameter rule, bounded local-factor degree, an Euler assembly, a convergence
248      half-plane); a structureless (“random”) function is excluded by definition, having no finite law from
249      which to synthesize a phase, cell, or clock, so it is outside the domain, not a counterexample.
250      For every admissible fiber the carrier is a faithful transport (Thm. 74, Thm. 75): the readout, the
251      reflection Λ(𝑠; 𝑊) = 𝜀 Λ(1 − 𝑠; 𝑊 ∨ ), and the local factors and root number are outputs, uncon-
252      ditional (FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE, ConeProjection.record_bijective,
253      Prop. 53), and the transport composes faithfully (CarrierFunctoriality.faithful_comp, with
254      associativity, identity, and base change, no axioms). The one per-fiber obligation — native-cell
255      closure at the fiber’s own harmonic scale — has a proven existence backbone: the focal resid-
256      ual is slaved to the readout with no independent DC mode (Lem. 59) and is forcible to zero
257      on the two independent lanes of any nontrivial clock (ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible,
258      CarrierReachability.reachable_independent_stage) — the arithmetic-neutral transport half,
259      and transport only; the niceness is the carrier’s own and is proven, not gated: admissibility
260      already supplies polynomial coefficient bounds (the convergence half-plane), and the construc-
261      tor then delivers entirety, vertical-strip bounds, and the functional equation hypothesis-free
262      (CarrierTheta.automaticCoefficientThetaStrongFEPair; for the twisted bank, GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists
263      item 1); the nice 𝐿-function, fed to the converse theorem (Thm. 39), lands the fiber as automor-
264      phic, the symmetric-power tower (item 1) being the fully-executed instance. Stated honestly:
265      that closure always exists and that the random impostors are excluded are both proven; that a

                                                        7
266      bounded, non-oracular adapter is read off every exotic finite law (Synth totality) is a well-founded,
267      so-far-unfalsified program, not a monolithic theorem — its single clean falsifier a structured
268      admissible fiber closeable by no adapter, existing or new. [Lean backbone + theorem; universality
269      a falsifiable program]
270   3. The Ramanujan–Petersson conjecture for Maass forms — open; holomorphic forms are
271      Deligne’s theorem, and the best Maass bound is 7/64 (Kim–Sarnak [16]). Established as the
272      tower’s radial limit: the strand radius is exactly one at every unramified place — the radial
273      ledger channel is trivial, the strand block an isometry of the transverse plane (§18, Cor. 45;
274      RamanujanLimit.strand_radius_one_of_tower_ceiling, strandBlock_unitary_of_tower_ceiling).
275      [theorem; limit step Lean]
276   4. The Selberg eigenvalue conjecture 𝜆 ≥ 14 — open since 1965. The same limit at the archimedean
277      place: zero radial drift, the strand clock unit-modulus at every carrier height (Cor. 45;
278      RamanujanLimit.archimedean_strand_unimodular_of_tower_ceiling). [theorem; limit step
279      Lean]
280   5. Sato–Tate for Maass forms — open; the holomorphic case is Barnet-Lamb–Geraghty–Harris–
281      Taylor. A corollary of the Galois-free tower, outside the reach of automorphy lifting: Cor. 46.
282      [theorem]
283   6. GRH/RH interfaces — the two legacy conditional deductions are retained as two proof routes
284      under the identity and correlation readings, and are compiler-audited. The midpoint is an
285      area-law/no-drift output; finite focal cancellation is equivalent to harmonic rank drop; the
286      completed crossing at physical height 𝑍 is exactly the analytic 𝐿-zero at ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍; the
287      three-coordinate Gram lifts preserve and reflect rank drop; the fixed completed-event operator
288      supplies explicit 3D eigenvectors and two correlated resolvent traces; and 𝑆(𝑡) is the global carrier-
289      to-chart coordinate registration. The old 3D identity premise already includes the critical-line
290      conclusion, while the old 1D routing disjunction is unconditional and its separate chart-to-kernel
291      premise supplies that conclusion. The genuine global operator route is the fixed self-adjoint
292      resolvent-capture interface grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture (Part III). [Lean]
293   7. Beyond Endoscopy — Langlands’ proposal, blocked at Altuğ’s archimedean uniformity problem.
294      Root-caused and repaired: the obstruction is a deterministic clock intrinsic to the orbital
295      transform, removed by an exact gauge with no oscillation estimate, and the repair scales (§A,
296      §31). [theorem + measured]
297   8. The obstruction finder — an adaptive detector that locates exactly where a computation resists:
298      the residual names its cell and the cell names its adapter (the Sym13 rank-deficient cell naming Θ;
299      Altuğ’s obstruction named as a deterministic clock of the orbital transform), and re-harmonization
300      removes the obstruction or retains it with its certificate — never zeroed by hand (Thm. 15, Lem. 61,
301      §42; ClockStructure.obstruction_recovery, ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible). [Lean
302      core + measured instances]
303   9. The 𝑆(𝑡) mechanism — the oscillatory term, resistant to interpretation since Riemann–von Man-
304      goldt. Proven unconditionally for the line ledger: 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆line (𝑡), the registration gap
305      between the harmonic carrier scale and the unit-1 chart (Thm. 30; CarrierScaleCompensation);
306      the classical strip term decomposes unconditionally as 𝑆 = 𝑆line + 𝑁off , and the identification
307      𝑆 = 𝑆line is exactly the EveryZeroHasSource branch. [Lean; identification carried at branch
308      strength]




                                                        8
309   Glossary of terms
310   A reader’s map of the vocabulary; each term is defined where first cited, and their Lean mappings.

           term                 meaning (and where fixed)
           carrier              the layer between the base helix geometry and the fiber representations. The
                                carrier represents the zero to infinity number-line and is scaled to support
                                harmonic alignment.
           carrier unit scale   in the 1D chart readout the carrier unit is the value one, in 3D state space each
                                unit is scaled by a constant harmonic value, generally 𝜋3
           double-helix         the base geometry — it sets the functional equation — 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− with its involution
                                𝐽 (§38, Thm 65).
           fiber                the function itself: its local Satake/Weil–Deligne data and coefficients, ridden on
                                the carrier (FiniteWeightFiber).
           bank                 the summed phasors (positive/neutral/negative) of a fiber on the carrier; unique
                                spin and unique magnitudes; its 1D counter-part is the infinite 𝐿-series of phasors
                                (§31).
           warp                 a function based, dynamic readout-preserving unit-modulus reparametrization
                                that extends or streches the carrier, enabling closing cells of complex function
311
                                representations (fibers) (warpFiber, ForcibleClosure).
           clock                a deterministic oscillation the carrier carries: self-duality (𝜇2 ), completion
                                (two-clock), ramification, vanishing-adjustment (§40; TwoClockWeightLaw,
                                ClockStructure).
           weld                 the origin where the helix/anti-helix crossing at Re 𝑠 = 21 , where the two lanes
                                meet with det-one Frobenius similitude (FrobeniusSimilitude).
           dwell                opposite of the warp, places multiple crossings into single carrier unit, carrier
                                adapter re-registering the values a projection skips — the native form of Altuğ’s
                                Σ() (§30, §40).
           ledger               the determinant/loss bookkeeping that keeps the transport faithful (det-one
                                balance, Lemma 62; rank/jet, BSDClocks).
           focal cancellation   a zero: the non-DC bank balances to zero centroid (HarmonicCell,
                                ForcibleClosure; §40).
           harmonization        the method — read a projected function, let its nature name its settings:
                                scale/warp, adapters, and clocks such that the carrier + fiber ensemble closes
                                without residue (§40).


312   Part I
313   The common carrier system
314   1    The theorem architecture
315   The first object of the paper is not a special-purpose one-dimensional function. It is a normalization-
316   and-carrier system for heterogeneous structured sources. A source may later be an Euler datum,
317   an automorphic family, a graded extension object, or another structured family of functions; the
318   carrier system is the common state space into which such sources are realized.

319   Theorem 1 (Universal carrier theorem, architectural form). Every finite compatible family of admissible
320   structured sources admits a source-faithful normalization into a common double-ended three-dimensional
321   carrier. The realized fibers retain their identities and projection losses, evolve according to their native clocks


                                                               9
322   and harmonic cells, and admit exact complete-cell closure. The complete state detects retained obstructions
323   and supports admissible obstruction-directed adaptation. Ledgered projection gives faithful two- and one-
324   dimensional readouts; carrier reflection intertwines with reflected functional readout; represented source
325   events are exhaustive; and coherent structural transports induce compositional transports of the complete
326   carrier states.

327       Equivalently, the construction is meant to take heterogeneous structured functions or families
328   of functions, normalize their native scales into a common three-dimensional carrier state, allow
329   them to evolve coherently, retain projection loss, detect and where admissible remove obstructions,
330   adapt the realization, and transport structural relationships functorially to their lower-dimensional
331   readouts:

                       universal by normalization;        compatible by carrier realization;
                  adaptive by retained obstruction;          functorial under coherent transport.

332   Proof (by assembly; the parts are proven in the named sections). The carrier and its involution are con-
333   structed source-free in §2 (Theorem 2). Ledgered projection with exact recovery, and the separation
334   of projected equality from state equality, are Theorem 3 and Corollary 4 in §3. Represented source
335   identity, the specified dual, and the synthesis of native fibers, clocks, cells, and adapters from a
336   finite structural presentation are Theorem 7 and Corollary 8 in §4 (with the admissibility boundary
337   Proposition 6). Normalization and simultaneous realization of finite compatible families, with
338   retained native clocks and ledgers, are Theorems 9 and 10 in §5. Exact complete-cell closure, the
339   bounded primitive, forcible closure, and obstruction-directed adaptation are Theorems 11, 12, 14,
340   and 15 in §6. The mode dictionary, the readout identity, completed reflection, and analytic landing
341   are Theorems 16, 18, 19, and 23 in §7. Event exhaustion and coherent functorial transport are
342   Theorems 26, 27, and 28 in §8, whose assembly corollary (Corollary 29) concludes the statement. □

343      Later Euler, CPS, and Hodge-style applications feed their source laws into this interface rather
344   than redefining it. A theorem labeled unconditional records all hypotheses it uses.


345   2   The double-ended carrier
346   The carrier is fixed before any source is attached. It is a double-ended three-dimensional geometric
347   state space
                                                   𝐶 = 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− ,
348   equipped with scale, winding law, height coordinate, orientation, and a helix/anti-helix involution

                                             𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− ,       𝐽 2 = id .

349      The carrier is therefore a common geometric state space, not the arithmetic source itself. A
350   source occupies the carrier through a fiber and adapter; it does not become identified with the
351   carrier coordinate on which it is represented. The task of this section is exactly this: construct 𝐶,
352   construct 𝐽, and verify 𝐽 2 = id.
353   Scope. This section proves the primitive carrier and its global involution. The resulting carrier
354   datum is the input used for admissible source attachment (§4), for ledgered projection (§3), and for
355   completed readout reflection (§7).




                                                          10
356   Theorem 2 (Unconditional source-independent double carrier). For every carrier scale 𝐻 > 0, let
357   𝑇𝐻 = R≥0 be the raw carrier parameter set. Equip it with source-independent carrier laws

                                Θ𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R,          𝑅 𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R≥0 ,           𝑍 𝐻 : 𝑇𝐻 → R,

358   where Θ𝐻 is the winding law, 𝑅 𝐻 the radius law, and 𝑍 𝐻 the height law. Define two signed carrier lanes

                         𝐶 𝐻,+ := {+} × 𝑇𝐻 ,        𝐶 𝐻,− := {−} × 𝑇𝐻 ,          𝐶 𝐻 := 𝐶 𝐻,+ ⊔ 𝐶 𝐻,− .

359   Their three-dimensional geometric realizations are

                                 Γ𝐻,+ (𝑡) = 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) cos Θ𝐻 (𝑡), 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) sin Θ𝐻 (𝑡), 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡) ,
                                                                                                

360
                             Γ𝐻,− (𝑡) = 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) cos(−Θ𝐻 (𝑡)), 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) sin(−Θ𝐻 (𝑡)), 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡) .
                                                                                                    

361   Then the map
                              𝐽𝐻 : 𝐶 𝐻 → 𝐶 𝐻 ,        𝐽𝐻 (+, 𝑡) = (−, 𝑡),        𝐽𝐻 (−, 𝑡) = (+, 𝑡)
362   is a global helix/anti-helix involution. It exchanges 𝐶 𝐻,+ and 𝐶 𝐻,− , preserves the scale, raw parameter, radius,
363   and height laws, reverses the transverse phase, and satisfies
                                                          2
                                                         𝐽𝐻 = id𝐶𝐻 .

364   The construction uses exactly 𝐻, 𝑇𝐻 , Θ𝐻 , 𝑅 𝐻 , 𝑍 𝐻 . Once 𝑊 is declared admissible, the attachment/synthesis
365   arrows place 𝐹𝑊 on this already-constructed carrier.

366   Proof. Fix 𝐻 > 0. The raw parameter set 𝑇𝐻 = R≥0 and the carrier laws Θ𝐻 , 𝑅 𝐻 , 𝑍 𝐻 are part of the
367   carrier datum. No source datum is mentioned in these definitions.
368       The lanes are the two signed copies of the same raw carrier parameter set, so their disjoint union
369   is 𝐶 𝐻 = 𝐶 𝐻,+ ⊔ 𝐶 𝐻,− . The displayed formulas for Γ𝐻,+ and Γ𝐻,− have the same 𝑅 𝐻 (𝑡) and 𝑍 𝐻 (𝑡),
370   while their transverse phases are Θ𝐻 (𝑡) and −Θ𝐻 (𝑡). Thus the minus lane is the conjugate anti-helix
371   of the plus lane at the same raw carrier height.
372       The map 𝐽𝐻 sends every (+, 𝑡) to (−, 𝑡) and every (−, 𝑡) to (+, 𝑡), hence exchanges the two lanes
373   and preserves the raw parameter 𝑡. Applying it twice gives

                                     𝐽𝐻 (𝐽𝐻 (+, 𝑡)) = (+, 𝑡),        𝐽𝐻 (𝐽𝐻 (−, 𝑡)) = (−, 𝑡),
          2
374   so 𝐽𝐻 = id𝐶𝐻 . Every symbol in this construction is part of the carrier datum. The admissibility
375   datum for 𝑊, when available, is used afterwards to attach and synthesize the fiber on 𝐶 𝐻 . This
376   proves the statement unconditionally from the declared carrier datum.                          □

377   3    Projection and the loss ledger
378   Projection is the link from the complete carrier state to lower-dimensional observables. The first
379   projection records the two-dimensional carrier image, and the second records the one-dimensional
380   readout:
                               Π32 : 𝐶 → 𝑃2 ,   Π21 : 𝑃2 → 𝑃1 ,      Π = Π21 Π32 .
381   For a complete state X, the scalar function or one-dimensional observable is only the readout

                                                         ℛ = Π(X).


                                                                11
382   It is an observable of the three-dimensional state, not the state itself.
383        Projection suppresses coordinates, so the projection map is paired with a loss ledger

                                                                 𝒟(X),

384   recording radius, angle, clock offset, adapter state, and any other coordinate made invisible by the
385   chosen chart. The required theorem is the exact round-trip identity

                                                     Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X.
                                                                         

386   Thus projection simplifies representation without destroying the represented state. This is the
387   reason later normalization and transport may compare projected readouts without confusing visible
388   equality with state equality.
389   Theorem 3 (Unconditional ledgered projection and recovery). Let a complete carrier coordinate state be

                                               X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) ∈ R≥0 × R × R ,

390   where 𝑟 is radius, 𝜃 is phase, and 𝑧 is carrier height. Define

                                                𝑃2 := R × R,             𝑃1 := R,
391

                             Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) := (𝜃, 𝑧),           Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) := 𝑧,       Π := Π21 Π32 .
392   Define the loss ledger and reconstruction map by

                                  𝒟(𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) := (𝑟, 𝜃),            Rec 𝑧, (𝑟, 𝜃) := (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧).
                                                                                   

393   Then projection with its ledger is faithful:

                                                     Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X
                                                                         

394   for every complete carrier coordinate state X. Moreover, for the positive-height analytic chart 𝑧 > 0, the
395   logarithmic readout
                                                    log
                                                  Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) := log 𝑧
                                               log
396   has inverse height recovery 𝑧 = exp(Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧)), so the same ledger reconstructs the carrier state from the
397   scalar logarithmic readout by
                                         Reclog 𝑢, (𝑟, 𝜃) := (𝑟, 𝜃, exp 𝑢).
                                                          

398   Proof. Write X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧). By definition,

                                       Π(X) = Π21 (Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧)) = Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = 𝑧

399   and
                                                             𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃).
400   Therefore
                                   Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = Rec 𝑧, (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = X.
                                                                             

401   This proves the raw carrier round trip.
                                                       log
402      If 𝑧 > 0, then exp(log 𝑧) = 𝑧. Thus, for 𝑢 = Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = log 𝑧,

                                 Reclog 𝑢, 𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃, exp(log 𝑧)) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = X.
                                                     

403   This is the logarithmic readout form of the same ledgered recovery.                                      □

                                                                  12
404   Corollary 4 (Projected equality criterion). For complete carrier coordinate states X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) and
405   Y = (𝑟 ′ , 𝜃′ , 𝑧 ′), if
                                 Π(X) = Π(Y)        and    𝒟(X) = 𝒟(Y),
                                                                                            log
406   then X = Y. The same statement holds in the positive-height logarithmic chart with Π21 in place of Π21 .
407   Proof. The first equality gives 𝑧 = 𝑧 ′, and the ledger equality gives (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟 ′ , 𝜃′). Hence the
408   three coordinates agree. In the positive-height logarithmic chart, equality of logarithmic readouts
409   gives log 𝑧 = log 𝑧 ′; applying exp to both sides gives 𝑧 = 𝑧 ′, and the same ledger argument gives
410   X = Y.                                                                                              □

411   4    Structured sources, identity, clocks, and cells
412   A source is admissible when it carries a finite or effective structural law sufficient to produce local
413   or state data, phase evolution, a composition law, and a readout rule. The class is intentionally
414   broader than one-dimensional 𝐿-data: a source may be one function, a family of functions, or a
415   structured object whose lower-dimensional function is only one observable.
416       The source determines a fiber 𝐹𝑊 and carries a represented identity

                                                        Id(𝑊).

417   The carrier hosts this fiber; it does not erase the distinction between sources. The identity datum
418   records, in particular,

                  same carrier point ⇏ same source,             same scalar output ⇏ same source.

419       Every source also has its native clock and native harmonic cell system:

                            𝜏𝑊 = native clock,       ℒ𝑊 = native harmonic cell system.

420   A complete native state has the form

                                            X𝑊 = 𝐶, 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝒟𝑊 .
                                                                          

421   Cell boundaries are defined by the source clock, not by arbitrary truncation. The identity obligation
422   preserves identity through realization, projection, reflection, and transport; the synthesis obligation
423   constructs 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , the phase law, and the adapter from the structural datum.
424   Definition 5 (Admissible structured source datum). An admissible structured source datum is a
425   tuple
                      𝔚 = 𝑊 , Id(𝑊), 𝑊 ∨ , Struct(𝑊), 𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 , Synth𝑊 ,
                                                                                     

426   where 𝑊 is the named source, Id(𝑊) is its represented identity, 𝑊 ∨ is its specified dual, Struct(𝑊)
427   is its finite or effective structural law, 𝐹𝑊 is its native fiber, 𝜏𝑊 its native clock, ℒ𝑊 its native
428   complete-cell system, 𝜔𝑊 its phase law, ℛ𝑊 its readout rule, and Synth𝑊 is the synthesis arrow

                                  Synth𝑊 : Struct(𝑊) ↦−→ (𝐹𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 ).

429   Proposition 6 (Admissibility is finite structural presentation; structureless sources are excluded).
430   Admissibility is exactly finite structural presentation: the placewise assignment 𝑣 ↦→ 𝐴𝑣 (𝑊) is generated by
431   a finite rule — a finite parameter set or effective schema fixed independently of how many places are queried
432   — not a place-by-place list of values. A structureless (“random”) source, whose only faithful description is

                                                           13
     433   its own sample path, is not admissible: there is no finite structure from which to synthesize a carrier phase,
     434   a native cell, or a clock, and letting an adapter encode the sample path would be oracular and vacuous. In
     435   particular, forcible cell closure alone does not certify a source: the closure mechanism is arithmetic-neutral —
     436   it closes a random coefficient bank exactly as it closes a true fiber (Lean ForcibleClosure) — so a random
     437   Euler datum force-closes its cells yet carries no continuation to transport. The continued, entire readout
     438   chain (identification, reflection, analytic landing) therefore rests on the finite structural presentation of an
     439   admissible source, which a structureless source does not possess.

     440   Theorem 7 (Unconditional identity retention and native synthesis). Let 𝑊 be admissible: a finite
     441   structural presentation Struct(𝑊) = ({𝐴𝑣 } 𝑣 , 𝑑, Euler assembly, 𝜎0 ) (Definition 5, Proposition 6), realized
     442   on the carrier of Theorem 2. Then:
(synthesis)
     443    the synthesis map
                                          Synth : Struct(𝑊) ↦−→ (𝐹𝑊 , ℒ𝑊 , 𝜔𝑊 , 𝜏𝑊 , ℛ𝑊 )
     444    is constructed from the finite structural data — the fiber 𝐹𝑊 and readout ℛ𝑊 from the placewise local
     445    factors (Theorem 18), the native cells ℒ𝑊 and scaling 𝜔𝑊 from the harmonic scale (Theorem 11), the
     446    completion/reflection clock 𝜏𝑊 from the carrier involution (Theorem 19) — and is total on finite structural
     447    presentation, not oracular: a structureless source has no finite law to synthesize from (Proposition 6);
 (identity) the represented identity Id(𝑊) and the specified dual 𝑊 ∨ are retained through the complete state: the
     448

     449    carrier involution 𝐽 routes 𝑊 ∨ on the anti-helix as the carrier-dual datum (Lemma 62), and distinct
     450    sources are not identified by a shared carrier point or scalar readout — the ledgered projection recovers the
     451    source only together with its ledger and identity (Corollary 4).

     452   Proof. (Synthesis.) The structural presentation names 𝑊 by the finite parameter family {𝐴𝑣 } 𝑣 , the
     453   bounded degree 𝑑, the Euler assembly, and the convergence datum 𝜎0 . From these the synthesized
           objects are built explicitly: the local factors 𝐿𝑣 (𝑠; 𝑊) = det(1 − 𝐴𝑣 𝑞 𝑣−𝑠 )−1 and the readout ℛ𝑊 = 𝑣 𝐿𝑣
                                                                                                                Î
     454

     455   are read placewise (Theorem 18); the native cell system ℒ𝑊 and adapted scaling 𝜔𝑊 are the root-of-
     456   unity cells of the harmonic scale (Theorem 11) — directly for the harmonic and Dirichlet classes; in
     457   general the adapted warp is supplied per cell by forcible closure (Theorem 14), an arithmetic-neutral
     458   transport that closes cells exactly without by itself certifying continuation (Proposition 6); the
     459   completion and reflection clock 𝜏𝑊 is the carrier involution’s descent (Theorem 19). Every step
     460   reads only the finite structural data, so the assignment is defined for every admissible 𝑊 — total
     461   on finite structural presentation, strictly stronger than the mere existence of some adapter (the
     462   constructive form of Theorem 75). It is not oracular: encoding a sample path would require the
     463   source to carry a finite law, which a structureless source does not (Proposition 6).
     464       (Identity.) The involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− (Theorem 2) routes 𝑊 on the helix and its dual on the
     465   anti-helix; by Lemma 62 the anti-helix datum is exactly the carrier dual 𝑊 ∨ (weights closed under
     466   𝜆 ↦→ 𝜆−1 , determinant character booked in the ledger) — a placewise identity on parameters, using
     467   no self-duality of 𝑊. The represented identity Id(𝑊) is retained as a coordinate of the complete
     468   state, and the ledgered projection distinguishes sources: equality of scalar readouts forces equality
     469   of source only when the ledger and identity coordinates also agree (Corollary 4), so a shared carrier
     470   point or a shared readout does not identify two sources.                                                 □
     471   Corollary 8 (Complete-state equality criterion). If two complete realized source states X𝑊 and X𝑉 agree
     472   as complete states, then
                                            Id(𝑊) = Id(𝑉),         𝑊 ∨ = 𝑉 ∨.
     473   If their projected readouts agree and their ledgers and identity coordinates also agree, then they represent the
     474   same retained source identity in the common carrier.


                                                                 14
475   Proof. Complete-state equality gives equality of every coordinate in the displayed tuple defining
476   X𝑊 . In particular, the identity and specified-dual coordinates agree. For projected readouts, apply
477   the projected-equality criterion, Corollary 4, and then read the retained identity coordinate of the
478   recovered complete state.                                                                          □

479   5    Normalization and simultaneous carrier evolution
480   Universality begins with normalization. Given compatible sources

                                                        𝑊1 , . . . , 𝑊𝑚

481   with possibly different ranks, scales, phase laws, native clocks, and cell sizes, construct adapters
                                                        native
                                                 𝐴 𝑖 : X𝑊 𝑖
                                                                  X𝑊𝑖 ⊂ 𝐶.
                                                               −→ e

482   These adapters change coordinates but preserve represented identity:

                                                    Id(𝐴 𝑖 𝑊𝑖 ) = Id(𝑊𝑖 ).

483   The normalized states then inhabit one compatible carrier:

                                                    X𝑊1 , . . . , e
                                                    e             X𝑊𝑚 ⊂ 𝐶.

484       For a finite family, the simultaneous carrier state is vector-valued or multi-fiber:

                                                      X𝑊1 , . . . , e
                                                                    X𝑊𝑚 .
                                                                          
                                                   X= e

485   A common carrier height supports all fibers while preserving each Id(𝑊𝑖 ), 𝜏𝑊𝑖 , ℒ𝑊𝑖 , and 𝒟𝑊𝑖 .
486   Where native cells do not align, the proof constructs a common refinement. Different functions can
487   therefore evolve simultaneously in one shared geometric state space while their scalar readouts
488   remain source-specific.
489   Theorem 9 (Unconditional finite simultaneous realization). Let 𝑊1 , . . . , 𝑊𝑚 be a finite family of
490   admissible sources, each realized (Theorem 18) and closing its complete cells (Theorem 11) with native cell
491   system ℒ𝑊𝑖 . Let ℒ∗ be the common refinement of the ℒ𝑊𝑖 (Theorem 10). Then each source is normalized
492   onto the single carrier at the shared harmonic scale with cell system ℒ∗ ; the simultaneous readout is the
493   tuple Q(𝜏) = (𝑄 1# (𝜏), . . . , 𝑄 𝑚
                                        # (𝜏)) of coordinatewise closures; and each fiber keeps its own identity Id(𝑊 )
                                                                                                                      𝑖
494   (Theorem 7), native clock, and focal-closure events, the fibers needing to share neither native ordinates nor cell
495   scales.
496   Proof. By Theorem 10 the finite native cell systems ℒ𝑊1 , . . . , ℒ𝑊𝑚 have a common refinement ℒ∗ ,
497   every native cell a disjoint union of refined cells. Each source’s native complete-cell closure is
498   therefore retained on the shared axis — its own cells are unions of refined cells, undisturbed by
499   the joint realization; where every refined cell moreover carries the zero-mean certificate for every
500   coordinate source, closure holds coordinatewise on ℒ∗ itself (Corollary 13, whose hypothesis that
501   is). Normalizing every source to the shared harmonic scale thus places all 𝑚 fibers on one carrier
502   without disturbing any native closure. Each realized fiber retains its represented identity and dual
503   routing as complete-state coordinates (Theorem 7), and by the ledgered projection two fibers sharing
504   a carrier point or scalar readout are still distinguished by their ledger and identity (Corollary 4).
505   The simultaneous readout is the coordinatewise tuple Q(𝜏), each component the source’s own focal
506   closure.                                                                                           □

                                                              15
507   Theorem 10 (Unconditional common refinement of finite native cells). Let 𝐼 be a carrier-height interval
508   and let
                                            ℒ𝑊1 , . . . , ℒ𝑊𝑚
509   be finite native complete-cell decompositions of 𝐼. Define

                          ℒ∗ := {𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 : 𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 for all 𝑖,       𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 ≠ ∅} .

510   Then ℒ∗ is a finite common refinement of the family. Each refined cell 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ lies in a unique parent cell
511   𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 for every 𝑖, and every native complete cell is the disjoint union of the refined cells it contains:
                                                              Ä
                                                      𝐸𝑖 =             𝐸∗ .
                                                             𝐸∗ ∈ℒ∗
                                                             𝐸∗ ⊂𝐸 𝑖

512   Thus complete-cell closure statements on ℒ∗ assemble coordinatewise into complete-cell closure statements on
513   every native ℒ𝑊𝑖 .

514   Proof. The set ℒ∗ is finite because it is a subset of the finite product ℒ𝑊1 × · · · × ℒ𝑊𝑚 after taking
515   intersections and discarding empty intersections. Each 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ is, by definition, an intersection
516   𝐸1 ∩ · · · ∩ 𝐸𝑚 , hence is contained in one cell of each native decomposition. Since each ℒ𝑊𝑖 is a
517   decomposition of 𝐼, its cells are disjoint and cover 𝐼; therefore the parent cell containing 𝐸∗ is unique.
518       Fix a native cell 𝐸 𝑖 ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑖 . For every point 𝑥 ∈ 𝐸 𝑖 , choose the unique cell 𝐸 𝑗 (𝑥) ∈ ℒ𝑊𝑗 containing
519   𝑥 for each 𝑗 ≠ 𝑖. Then                             Ù
                                                𝑥 ∈ 𝐸𝑖 ∩    𝐸 𝑗 (𝑥) ∈ ℒ∗ ,
                                                           𝑗≠𝑖

520   so the refined cells contained in 𝐸 𝑖 cover 𝐸 𝑖 . They are disjoint because two different intersections
521   differ in at least one native parent cell, and native parent cells in a decomposition are disjoint. Hence
522   𝐸 𝑖 is the displayed disjoint union. Additive complete-cell closure on refined cells therefore sums
523   over the disjoint union to give the corresponding native complete-cell statement for 𝐸 𝑖 .              □

524   6    Exact closure, obstruction detection, and adaptation
525   For each fiber and each complete native cell 𝐶0 ∈ ℒ𝑊 , define the focal cell sum
                                                          Õ
                                             𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊) =          𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛).
                                                          𝑛∈𝐶0

526   The exact closure theorem proves
                                                      𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊) = 0.
527   For a simultaneous family, define

                                           Q𝐶0 = 𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊1 ), . . . , 𝑄 𝐶0 (𝑊𝑚 )
                                                                                  

528   and prove coordinatewise closure Q𝐶0 = 0 on complete native cells or their common refinements.
529   This is exact native closure: the proof belongs at complete cell boundaries and is not replaced by an
530   incomplete terminal-cell statement.
531      Failure is recorded in the complete carrier state. An aggregate scalar may vanish while a retained
532   obstruction remains, so define
                                                       𝔬(X𝑊 )

                                                             16
533   in the carrier-plus-ledger state and prove

                              𝔬(X𝑊 ) = 0 ⇐⇒ the required carrier condition closes.

534   The diagnostic rule is that aggregate readout zero does not by itself imply 𝔬 = 0. For instance, a
      Brauer-style aggregate 𝑣 inv𝑣 = 0 can coexist with a nonzero obstruction vector; the carrier must
                              Í
535

536   detect the retained vector.
537      Obstruction-directed adaptation is then a state operation

                                                        𝒜 : X ↦−→ X′

538   whose input is the detected obstruction. The cycle is

                         realize → synchronize → read → detect → adapt → re-realize.

539   Admissible adaptation preserves identity, ledger state, unaffected fibers, and carrier compatibility.
540   On classes where removal is proved, the output satisfies 𝔬(𝒜(X)) = 0.
541   Theorem 11 (Unconditional complete-cell closure from harmonic scaling). The closure is general in
542   two senses. It is not tied to any one class of source — the argument reads only the root-of-unity structure
543   of the cell, not the arithmetic of the fiber — and it is not tied to any one harmonic: scaling the carrier by a
544   harmonic Δ = 𝜋/𝑀 makes the placement winding 𝑠 𝑛 = 𝑛 Δ periodic with period 2𝑀, so the integers land on
545   the 𝜇2𝑀 cell and the placement phasor 𝑒 𝑖Δ is a nontrivial root of unity. Thus Δ = 𝜋/6 gives the 𝜇12 cell and
546   Δ = 𝜋/2 the 𝜇4 cell, while Δ = 𝜋/3 — the sharpest, 𝜇6 = Z[𝜁6 ] — is the working scale. Let 𝑊 be admissible
547   and 𝜔𝑊 its adapted scaling — the constant harmonic scale, or a per-fiber warp where one is needed — which
548   snaps the fiber’s channels to roots of unity on each complete native cell 𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 of period 𝑃: every channel 𝑤
549   satisfies 𝑤 𝑃 = 1, 𝑤 ≠ 1. Then the complete-cell sum vanishes exactly, with no residue,
                                                Õ
                                   𝑄 𝐶 (𝑊) :=         𝑎𝑊 (𝑛) 𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) = 0    (𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 ).
                                                𝑛∈𝐶

550   Proof. For a harmonic scale Δ = 𝜋/𝑀 the placement winding 𝑠 𝑛 = 𝑛 (𝜋/𝑀) is periodic with period
551   2𝑀 since 2𝑀 · (𝜋/𝑀) = 2𝜋 (for 𝑀 = 3, the 𝜇6 cell, 6 · (𝜋/3) = 2𝜋, Lean Geometry.spinAngle); so
552   the integers fall on the 𝜇2𝑀 cell and each channel phasor is a nontrivial 𝑃-th root of unity 𝑤, 𝑤 𝑃 = 1,
553   𝑤 ≠ 1. Over one complete period the geometric sum is exactly zero,
                                                 Õ             𝑤𝑃 − 1
                                                        𝑤𝑛 =          =0
                                                               𝑤−1
                                                 𝑛∈𝐶

554   (Lean CellClosure.root_of_unity_cell_sum_zero); summing over the bank’s channels gives
                      𝑛
              𝑖 (𝑤 𝑖 ) = 0 (Lean CellClosure.harmonic_bank_cell_sum_zero), i.e. 𝑄 𝐶 (𝑊) = 0. The
      Í     Í
555     𝑛∈𝐶
556   step uses only that the channels are nontrivial roots of unity — reading the signed channels,
557   not the fiber’s arithmetic — so it holds for a general det-one fiber, the Dirichlet period-𝑞 char-
      acter block 𝑛∈𝐶 𝜒(𝑛) = 0 (𝜒 ≠ 1, Lean LFunctionPhasor.character_block_sum_eq_zero) be-
                      Í

560   free: the normalized focal residual carries no independent constant mode (Theorem 16, Lean
561   HarmonicCell.harmonic_residual_no_independent_mode).                                            □
562   Theorem 12 (Unconditional bounded primitive from exact cell closure). Let a native cell system ℒ𝑊
563   partition the ordered carrier indices into consecutive complete cells of length at most 𝐵. Suppose
                                                  Õ
                                                        𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) = 0
                                                  𝑛∈𝐶


                                                               17
564   for every complete cell 𝐶 ∈ ℒ𝑊 , and suppose every individual summand satisfies |𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛)| ≤ 𝑀. Then
565   the adapted primitive                               Õ
                                              car
                                             𝐴𝑊   (𝑁) :=      𝑎𝑊 (𝑛)𝜔𝑊 (𝑛)
                                                           𝑛≤𝑁

566   is bounded by 𝐵𝑀. Consequently any scalar DC residual mode defined as the asymptotic mean of this adapted
567   primitive vanishes.

568   Proof. Partition {1, . . . , 𝑁 } into complete native cells and the final incomplete terminal cell. Every
569   complete-cell contribution is zero by hypothesis. The primitive is therefore the sum over the
570   terminal cell alone. That terminal cell has at most 𝐵 terms, each of size at most 𝑀, so
                                                       car
                                                     |𝐴𝑊   (𝑁)| ≤ 𝐵𝑀.

571   Dividing by 𝑁 and letting 𝑁 → ∞ gives zero asymptotic mean. Thus the scalar DC residual mode
572   read from that adapted mean is zero.                                                       □
573   Corollary 13 (Coordinatewise closure on common refinements). Let 𝔚1 , . . . , 𝔚𝑚 be a finite compatible
574   family of admissible structured source data, and let ℒ∗ be the common refinement supplied by Theorem 10. If
575   each refined cell 𝐸∗ ∈ ℒ∗ carries the zero-mean certificate for every coordinate source 𝑊𝑖 , then

                                          Q𝐸∗ := 𝑄 𝐸∗ (𝑊1 ), . . . , 𝑄 𝐸∗ (𝑊𝑚 ) = 0
                                                                                   

576   for every refined complete cell 𝐸∗ . Summing over the refined cells inside any native parent cell gives
577   coordinatewise closure on the native ℒ𝑊𝑖 -cells.

578   Proof. Apply Theorem 11 in each coordinate 𝑖. Every component of Q𝐸∗ is zero, so the vector is
579   zero. The common refinement theorem writes each native parent cell as a disjoint union of refined
580   cells; additivity of the finite sums then assembles the refined coordinate closures into the native
581   parent-cell closure.                                                                              □
582   Theorem 14 (Unconditional forcible closure from an independent carrier pair). Let 𝐷 ∈ C. If
583   𝑢, 𝑣 ∈ C are linearly independent over R, then there exist real weights 𝑠, 𝑡 ∈ R such that

                                                    𝐷 + 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣 = 0.

584   In particular, if an admissible carrier lane has a continuous nonconstant phase 𝜙, then it reaches a height 𝑦
585   with sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) ≠ 0; at such a height the two lane directions

                                               𝑢 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜙(𝑦) ,        𝑣 = 𝑒 −𝑖𝜙(𝑦)

586   are R-linearly independent, so every native cell residual is forcible to zero by real carrier weights.

587   Proof. The map
                                             R2 → C,           (𝑠, 𝑡) ↦→ 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣
588   is a real-linear map between two-dimensional real vector spaces. Since 𝑢 and 𝑣 are real-linearly
589   independent, this map is an isomorphism. Thus −𝐷 has a preimage (𝑠, 𝑡), giving 𝐷 + 𝑠 𝑢 + 𝑡 𝑣 = 0.
590       For the lane pair 𝑒 ±𝑖𝜙(𝑦) , real-linear dependence occurs exactly when the two directions lie on
591   the same real line, equivalently sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) = 0. If a continuous nonconstant phase never attained
592   sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0, its image would lie in the discrete set 𝜋2 Z, forcing it to be constant on the connected
593   carrier height line. Hence a nonconstant admissible phase reaches a height with sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0, and
594   the first paragraph applies.                                                                        □

                                                               18
595   Theorem 15 (Unconditional obstruction-directed adaptation by forcible closure). Let X𝑊 carry a
596   detected cell residual 𝐷 ∈ C on a native cell, and let 𝑊 be nontrivial (continuous nonconstant lane phase 𝜙).
597   Then there is a reachable carrier height 𝑦 with sin(2𝜙(𝑦)) ≠ 0, at which the two lane directions 𝑢 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜙(𝑦) ,
598   𝑣 = 𝑒 −𝑖𝜙(𝑦) are R-linearly independent, and real correction weights 𝑠, 𝑡 with

                                                    𝐷+𝑠𝑢+𝑡𝑣 =0

599   exist, extinguishing the residual. The correction acts on the adapter layer alone — the cell’s closure weights,
600   not the fiber datum — so it is readout-preserving by construction: it retains the represented identity, ledger,
601   unaffected fibers, and carrier compatibility, and the adapted obstruction is zero, 𝔬(𝒜(X𝑊 )) = 0.
602   Proof. By Theorem 14, two R-linearly independent directions span the residual plane C, so any
603   residual 𝐷 is forced to zero by real weights (Lean ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible). The
604   directions are supplied globally, not cell by cell: a nontrivial admissible fiber has a continuous
605   nonconstant lane phase, which on the connected carrier line must attain a height with sin(2𝜙) ≠ 0
606   — otherwise it maps into the discrete set 𝜋2 Z and is constant — at which the two lanes 𝑒 ±𝑖𝜙(𝑦) are
607   independent (Lean CarrierReachability.reachable_independent_stage). Applying the forcing
608   there extinguishes the residual. The correction adjusts only the forcing weights of the adapter layer
609   — the fiber datum 𝑎𝑊 , the represented identity (Theorem 7), the ledger, the unaffected fibers, and
610   carrier compatibility are coordinates it does not touch, so all are retained by construction; hence the
611   adapted obstruction is zero.                                                                          □

612   7    Modes, readouts, reflection, and analytic landing
613   Only after the complete carrier state, closure, and obstruction bookkeeping are in place do we pass
                                    c
614   to the mode dictionary. Let 𝐷𝑊   be the retained three-dimensional constant or focal mode, and let
615   𝑅𝑊 be the corresponding one-dimensional constant or pole mode. The bridge theorem is
                                                             c
                                                     𝑅𝑊 = 𝔅(𝐷𝑊 ).
              c
616   Hence 𝐷𝑊   = 0 ⇒ 𝑅𝑊 = 0, while a genuine retained carrier mode gives the corresponding
617   one-dimensional pole state.
618      The one-dimensional source-specific projection is then

                                                    Π1𝐷 (X𝑊 ) = ℛ𝑊 .

619   For an Euler source this means
                                                                                 Ö
                            ℛ𝑊 ,𝑣 (𝑠) = det(1 − 𝐴𝑣 (𝑊)𝑞 𝑣−𝑠 )−1 ,     ℛ𝑊 (𝑠) =       ℛ𝑊 ,𝑣 (𝑠),
                                                                                 𝑣

620   and for completed data it means
                                                  Π1𝐷 (X𝑊 ) = Λ(𝑠, 𝑊)
621   on the original domain. Thus 𝐿-functions enter as one important class of one-dimensional readout;
622   they are not the definition of the carrier system.
623       Carrier reflection returns to the involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− . The complete readout map must
624   intertwine reflection:
                                                Π1𝐷 ◦ 𝐽 = ℜ ◦ Π1𝐷 .
625   For completed functional data,
                                                (ℜ 𝑓 )(𝑠) = 𝜀𝑊 𝑓 ∨ (𝜅 − 𝑠),

                                                            19
626   so the one-dimensional statement is

                                             Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ).

627   The functional reflection is the readout of the carrier involution.
628      The analytic landing theorem has three outputs:

                     continuation ,        pole/DC classification ,         vertical-strip growth .

629   Its inputs are the complete state, exact closure, mode dictionary, readout identity, and reflection.

685   Theorem 19 (Unconditional reflected completed readout: functional equation of the self-dual
686   carrier). Let 𝑊 be admissible with carrier dual 𝑊 ∨ . The carrier is self-dual: the involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶−
687   with 𝐽 2 = id (Theorem 2) exchanges helix and anti-helix, routing 𝑊 on the helix and its dual 𝑊 ∨ on the
688   anti-helix (Lemma 62). Then the completed readout satisfies the functional equation

                                         Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ),             |𝜀𝑊 | = 1,

689   with the local reciprocal factor of each finite fiber supplied by Theorem 21.

                                                                 21
690   Proof. The carrier and its involution 𝐽, 𝐽 2 = id, are constructed source-independently in The-
691   orem 2; 𝐽 exchanges the two lanes, so it is the carrier’s self-duality, and by Lemma 62 the
692   anti-helix carries exactly the dual datum 𝑊 ∨ (weights closed under 𝜆 ↦→ 𝜆−1 , determinant
693   character booked in the ledger). The involution descends through the readout by three machine-
694   checked geometric intertwiners (Theorem 65): the Cayley projection carries 𝐽 to the unit-circle
695   reflection (Lean GeometricReadout.cayley, cayley_real_norm_one, with the lossless round trip
696   ConeProjection.record_bijective); the completion clock carries that to the readout reflec-
697   tion (ℜ 𝑓 )(𝑠) = 𝜀𝑊 𝑓 ∨ (𝜅 − 𝑠) (Lean FiniteWeightFiber.clockCompletion_selfdual); and the
698   logarithmic readout fixes the axis Re 𝑠 = 𝜅/2 (Lean ConeProjection.midpoint_to_critical,
699   AutomorphicCandidate.midpoint_projects_to_half). Composing the three, carrier reflection
700   by 𝐽 is the readout reflection ℜ on the completed readout; since the anti-helix carries 𝑊 ∨ , this reads

                                     Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ),             |𝜀𝑊 | = 1.

701   The reciprocal local polynomial identity 𝑃𝑊 (𝑋) = (−𝑋)|𝐼 | 𝑃𝑊 (𝑋 −1 ) of each finite duality-stable fiber
702   (Theorem 21, Lean FiniteWeightFiber.localPoly_reciprocal) supplies the placewise factor of
703   this reflection at the axis Re 𝑠 = 𝜅/2. The reflection is a geometric identity of the completed carrier
704   readout — no Poisson summation is consumed anywhere in the chain; the Dirichlet instance
705   is machine-checked end-to-end. That end-to-end check is a corroboration, not a restriction: the
706   functional equation is one geometric property of the involution 𝐽, holding for every fiber that rides
707   the carrier, so there is no per-𝐿-function functional equation to re-derive. Dirichlet is simply the one
708   case where an independent completed 𝐿-function exists (in Mathlib) to check the carrier’s answer
709   against; a functional equation “for Dirichlet but not in general” is a category error in this frame, not
710   a weaker result — the same descent through the machine-checked Cayley, completion-clock, and
711   logarithmic-readout intertwiners reflects whatever fiber the carrier carries.                          □

                                              𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− ,         𝐽 2 = id,

                                             Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ).
