795   8   Exhaustion, coherent transport, and the universal theorem
796   Exhaustion asserts that represented source information is neither lost nor invented by carrier
797   realization or ledgered projection:

                              source state ↔ carrier state ↔ ledgered projected state.

798   For represented events,

                               𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(X𝑊 ) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ).

799   For zero events where applicable, the proof identifies the event with the corresponding closed
800   carrier condition, for example
                                                          #
                                       𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊       (𝜌) = 0.
801   The visible one-dimensional coordinate may suppress dimensions; the ledgered state remains
802   exhaustive.
803      Finally let
                                             𝑇 : 𝑊 → 𝑊′

                                                               25
804   be a structural source transport. The carrier construction induces

                                                    X(𝑇) : X𝑊 → X𝑊 ′ .

805   The transport theorem proves preservation and compatibility of identity, ledger state, cell structure,
806   closure, 𝐽, one-dimensional readout, and obstruction state, and proves composition:

                                                X(𝑇2 ◦ 𝑇1 ) = X(𝑇2 ) ◦ X(𝑇1 ).

807   Together with the previous sections, this is the proof content of Theorem 1. Later parts should
808   consume this theorem by instantiating the admissible source law: Euler/L-function sources, CPS
809   twisting families, and graded obstruction towers are inputs to the same carrier interface.

810   Theorem 26 (Unconditional ledgered event exhaustion). Let X𝑊 be a complete realized source state.
811   Because the ledgered projection is a bĳection — the fiber reconstructs from its retained height and loss ledger
812   (Theorem 3; Lean ConeProjection.record_bijective, reconstruct_record,
813   SourceHolonomy.projection_bijective_loss_ledger) — the represented source events, carrier
814   events, and ledgered projected events coincide:

                                𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(X𝑊 ) ⇐⇒ 𝑒 ∈ 𝐸(Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ),

815   so no event is lost by projection or invented by realization. For zero events, the represented vanishing coincides
816   with the closed carrier condition,
                                                                     #
                                                𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊         (𝜌) = 0,
817   the carrier focal closure vanishing exactly at the readout’s zeros (Lean ClosedForm.carrierZero_iff_L_zero,
818   FocalResidualVanishes.focal_residual_zero_iff_L_zero — the Dirichlet-instantiated form; the
819   general zero-event identification is placewise through the local identification of Theorem 18).

820   Proof. The ledgered projection X𝑊 ↦→ (Π(X𝑊 ), 𝒟𝑊 ) is a bĳection whose inverse is the reconstruction
821   map (Theorem 3; Lean record_bijective, reconstruct_record, projection_bijective_loss_ledger),
822   so it neither identifies distinct states nor omits any; the represented, carrier, and ledgered projected
823   event sets are therefore in bĳection, giving the three-way equivalence. For a zero-event datum, the car-
                           #
824   rier focal closure 𝑄𝑊   vanishes exactly when the readout vanishes (Lean carrierZero_iff_L_zero,
                                                                      #
825   focal_residual_zero_iff_L_zero), so 𝜌 ∈ 𝑍(𝑊) ⇐⇒ 𝑄𝑊                (𝜌) = 0.                             □
826   Theorem 27 (Unconditional coherent carrier transport). Call a carrier transport 𝑇 faithful for a closure
827   predicate Cl if Cl(𝑥) ⇒ Cl(𝑇𝑥). Then the identity transport is faithful; the composite of faithful transports
828   is faithful; composition is associative with the identity as two-sided unit; and the base-change transports
829   compose, bc𝑝 ◦ bc𝑞 = bc𝑝𝑞 , with bc1 = id. Hence coherent source transports induce carrier transports that
830   preserve closure and retained data and respect composition.

831   Proof. Each law is machine-checked in CarrierFunctoriality: the identity is faithful (faithful_id);
832   a composite of faithful transports is faithful (faithful_comp); composition is associative (comp_assoc)
833   with two-sided identity (id_comp, comp_id); and base change composes (bc_comp) with unit (bc_one).
834   The abstract closure-transport statement is Theorem 28; these are its verified instances.            □
835   Theorem 28 (Unconditional functorial closure transport). Let 𝒞 be a class of complete carrier states
836   equipped with a closure predicate Cl and retained datum predicate Ret. A transport 𝐹 : 𝑋 → 𝑌 is faithful
837   when
                                  Cl(𝑋) ⇒ Cl(𝐹(𝑋)),         Ret(𝑋) ⇒ Ret(𝐹(𝑋)).


                                                             26
838   Then the identity transport is faithful, and the composite of faithful transports is faithful. In particular, if
                                                           𝐹        𝐺
                                                        𝑋−
                                                         →𝑌−
                                                           →𝑍

839   are faithful carrier transports, then 𝐺 ◦ 𝐹 preserves closure and all retained Part I data named by Ret.

840   Proof. For the identity map, both implications are tautological:

                                        Cl(𝑋) ⇒ Cl(𝑋),              Ret(𝑋) ⇒ Ret(𝑋).

841   Now suppose 𝐹 and 𝐺 are faithful. If Cl(𝑋), then faithfulness of 𝐹 gives Cl(𝐹(𝑋)), and faithfulness
842   of 𝐺 gives Cl(𝐺(𝐹(𝑋))). The retained-datum implication is identical with Ret in place of Cl. Thus
843   𝐺 ◦ 𝐹 is faithful.                                                                               □
844   Corollary 29 (Part I assembly of the universal carrier theorem). For every finite compatible family of
845   admissible structured source data with the carrier, projection, source, synchronization, closure, obstruction,
846   readout, reflection, analytic, exhaustion, and transport datums specified in Part I, the conclusions of Theorem 1
847   hold.

848   Proof. The primitive double-ended carrier and involution are supplied by Theorem 2. Ledgered
849   projection and recovery are supplied by Theorem 3 and Corollary 4. Source identity and native
850   synthesis are supplied by Definition 5, Theorem 7, and Corollary 8. Finite simultaneous carrier real-
851   ization and common refinement are supplied by Theorems 9 and 10. Exact complete-cell closure and
852   obstruction-directed adaptation are supplied by Theorem 11, Theorem 12, Corollary 13, Theorem 14,
853   and Theorem 15. The retained-mode bridge, channel residual factorization, one-dimensional
854   readout identity, completed reflection, and analytic landing are supplied by Theorems 16, 17, 18, 19,
855   20, 21, 23, 24, and 25. Event exhaustion and coherent transport are supplied by Theorems 26, 27,
856   and 28. These are exactly the arrows named in Theorem 1.                                           □

857   9    The scale mismatch behind the 𝑆(𝑡) term

                     𝑆line (𝑡) is not a native oscillatory feature of the prime/harmonic system.

858   The native system is realized on the 𝜋/3-scaled harmonic carrier. The conventional analytic readout
859   uses a unit-1 coordinate system. These two carrier scalings represent the same arithmetic procession,
860   but they do not register the same crossings in the same coordinate units.
861        Typing convention, fixed before the theorem. Throughout this section 𝑁(𝑡) denotes the carrier’s event
862   count — the on-line ordinate census #{𝛾 ∈ (0, 𝑡] : 𝜁( 12 + 𝑖𝛾) = 0} (Lean: zeroEventCount) — and
863   𝑆line (𝑡) := 𝑁(𝑡) − 1 − 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋 its normalized form. The classical Riemann–von Mangoldt term is the
864   strip count’s normalization, 𝑆(𝑡) = 𝑁strip (𝑡) − 1 − 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋. The two ledgers are related unconditionally
865   by 𝑆(𝑡) = 𝑆line (𝑡) + 𝑁off (𝑡) with 𝑁off = 𝑁strip − 𝑁 ≥ 0 the off-line census; the identification 𝑆 = 𝑆line —
866   i.e. 𝑁off ≡ 0 — is exactly the EveryZeroHasSource branch of the standing dichotomy and is neither
867   assumed nor proven here. Every theorem of this section is a statement about the line ledger and is
868   unconditional as such; the register remark after the theorem states what does and does not transfer
869   to the classical term.




                                                               27
870   9.1    The theorem
871   Let 𝐹𝜁 denote the trivial-character arithmetic fiber and let X𝜁,𝐻 denote its realization on carrier
872   scale 𝐻, with the fiber law, local arithmetic data, phasor amplitudes, source identity, and crossing
873   criterion held fixed. Only the carrier scale is changed.

874   Theorem 30 (The 𝑆(𝑡) carrier-scale compensation theorem). With the registered counts of Definition 32:
875   (i) 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑁(𝑡): the native count is the arithmetic event count over the height ray;
                𝑡
876 (ii) 𝑁1 (𝑒 ) = 1 + 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋: the unit count is the DC residue plus the archimedean clock, with 𝜗 the Riemann–

877       Siegel theta, derived from the gauge, not inserted;
878 (iii) consequently

                                                                                             𝜗(𝑡)
                                𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆line (𝑡) , 𝑆line (𝑡) = 𝑁(𝑡) − 1 −      .
                                                                                              𝜋
879    Both 𝑁𝜋/3 and 𝑁1 are derived as cumulative carrier crossing counts; in particular 𝑁1 is not defined to be
880    the theta term. Every step is machine-checked in RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean
881    native_identification’, unit_identification, carrier_scale_compensation_S.

882   Remark 31 (Register: the classical 𝑆(𝑡)). What is proven above is unconditional for the line ledger.
883   For the classical strip term the unconditional statement is the decomposition

                                       𝑆(𝑡) = 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) + 𝑁off (𝑡),
                                                  |         {z         }
                                                  registration gap, proven

884   so the classical 𝑆(𝑡) acquires an unconditional two-part reading: a machine-checked chart-defect
885   compensation plus the off-line census. On the EveryZeroHasSource branch 𝑁off ≡ 0 and the
886   compensation identity is the classical 𝑆(𝑡) verbatim; off that branch 𝑁off is a nonnegative step
887   function supported on sourceless events — the typed unknown of the 1D limit, not a defect of the
888   3D representation. We do not claim the identification: the mechanism explanation of the classical
889   term is exactly as strong as the branch.

890      The proof occupies the rest of the section: part (i) in the native-𝜋/3 subsection, part (ii) in the
891   unit-1 subsection, part (iii) by subtraction; the induced event readout pinning every functor input is
892   derived in the discharged-arrows subsection.

893   9.2    Definitions of the two counts
894   Definition 32 (Scale-indexed registered count). For a carrier realization X𝜁,𝐻 , write

                  𝒞𝐻 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑧) = { 𝑐 : 𝑐 is a complete 𝐹𝜁 -closure in X𝜁,𝐻 through raw height 𝑧 }.

895   The cumulative crossing count at carrier scale 𝐻 is

                                                  𝑁𝐻 (𝑧) := #𝒞𝐻 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑧).

896   Thus
                               𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = #𝒞𝜋/3 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑒 𝑡 ),      𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = #𝒞1 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑒 𝑡 ).
897   Both counts start at the common origin, both are cumulative, and both use the same fiber law and
898   crossing predicate. The subscript records only the carrier scale used to register the same arithmetic
899   procession.

                                                              28
900       In Lean the scale-indexed cumulative count functor is installed as registeredCount: DC base
901   at the common origin, the chart’s continuous clock procession in 𝜋-cells, and the event count
902   weighted by the induced per-event contribution of the scale’s closure geometry (eventContribution;
903   derivation in the discharged-arrows subsection below) — every input pinned by a theorem. The
904   closure predicate is NativeClosure (the fiber’s 𝜂-accumulation) and the counts are nativeCount
905   and zeroEventCount.

906   9.3   Native 𝜋/3 chain
907   The native chain already present in the carrier framework is:

                                   𝐹𝜁 −→ X𝜁,𝜋/3 −→ 𝒞𝜋/3 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑒 𝑡 ) −→ 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ).

908   Its local pieces are the 𝜋/3 cell law

                                               cell(𝑛) = exp(𝑖𝑛𝜋/3),

909   the antipodal cancellation
                                              cell(𝑛) + cell(𝑛 + 3) = 0,
910   the helix pencil closure equivalence, and the exact height readout

                                              heightReadout(𝑒 𝛾 ) = 𝛾.

911   In Lean these correspond to the native cell and pencil statements in GeometricPhasorClosure.lean
912   and to the readout lemmas

               cell_antipodal_cancel,           helix_cancellation_logfree,             readout_exp

913   in GeometricReadout.lean.

914   Proof of Theorem 30(i). A complete closure of the fiber at ordinate 𝛾 is exactly an on-line zero
915   event: the fiber’s own 𝜂-accumulation closes at 𝛾 if and only if the readout vanishes there
916   (nativeClosure_iff_zero, via Faithful.continuous_model_zeta), and the height readout carries
917   raw height 𝑒 𝑡 to ordinate 𝑡 exactly (readout_exp). Here 𝑁(𝑡) is the zero-counting procession over
918   the 3D representation’s entire event space — the height ray, whose exhaustion is a theorem,
919   consumed not assumed (native_events_sourced, instantiating the proven threeD_exhaustive;
920   the height encoding is lossless, event_encoding_complete). Counting complete closures through
921   raw height 𝑒 𝑡 therefore counts exactly the arithmetic events through ordinate 𝑡: 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑁(𝑡)
922   (native_identification’). No 𝑆(𝑡) term is an additional state variable in X𝜁,𝜋/3 .                □

923   9.4   Unit-1 carrier chain
924   The unit-1 chain must be a parallel realization of the same fiber:

                                      𝐹𝜁 −→ X𝜁,1 −→ 𝒞1 (𝐹𝜁 ; 𝑒 𝑡 ) −→ 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ).

925   The required scalar readout identity is Theorem 30(ii): 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 1 + 𝜗(𝑡)/𝜋.

950   9.6    The arrows, discharged
951   Both arrows previously recorded here as unsupplied — the scale-indexed cumulative count functor
952   X𝜁,𝐻 −→ (𝑧 ↦→ 𝑁𝐻 (𝑧)) and the unit-1 derivation — are now proven in RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation
953   with no functor input inserted by hand:



                                                                     30
954   • Event channel. An event is a sign flip of the real native state; its mark is the half turn −1 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜋
955     (sign_flip_mark). A scale-𝐻 chart registers the mark only through a completed cell arc realizing
956     it, eventArcs 𝐻 = {𝑘 ≥ 1 : 𝑒 𝑖 𝑘𝐻 = −1}. At 𝜋/3 the wall is hit exactly once per closed six-cell
957     monodromy loop (pi3_wall_mem, from the antipodal identity; pi3_arcs_eq: the arcs are exactly
958     𝑘 ≡ 3 (mod 6)) — one registered event per completed native cell. At scale 1 no arc ever realizes
959     the mark (unit_arcs_empty). The induced per-event contribution (eventContribution) is 1 at
960     𝜋/3 and 0 at 1 by theorems, not by a gate.
961   • Clock channel. The native chart’s zero clock is derived, not assigned: every continuous clock its
962     readout factors through is constant on event-free stretches (native_clock_locally_constant,
963     from no_native_oscillation). The unit chart’s clock is 𝜗, the unique continuous gauge phase
964     (gauge_polar, theta_unique).
965   • DC base. The origin registration is the trivial-channel residue, value forced (dcResidue_spec,
966     dcResidue_unique).
967   The fundamental gap behind the theorem is prior to any analytic content: the native and unit
968   placements of the integer procession are incommensurable — the lattices {𝑘 𝜋/3} and {𝑚} meet
969   only at the origin (lattice_gap_fundamental); the unit carrier closes no cell (unit_never_closes)
970   and has no antipodal wall (unit_cell_no_antipodal). 𝑆(𝑡) is the accumulated readout of that
971   incommensurability; crossings are only the units of the native bookkeeping.

972   9.7   The general registration gap 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 and the harmonic family
973   The comparison generalizes to arbitrary scale pairs. With 𝑁𝐻 the canonical scale-𝐻 chart count
974   (NH; by NH_dichotomy the family contains exactly the two proven chart types, decided by the arc
975   geometry), define
                                  𝑆𝐻,𝐾 (𝑡) := 𝑁𝐻 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁𝐾 (𝑒 𝑡 ) (Sgap).
976   Proposition 34 (Coboundary laws). The registration gap is a coboundary of the per-scale potential:
977   𝑆𝐻,𝐻 = 0, 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 = −𝑆𝐾,𝐻 , and the cocycle law 𝑆𝐻,𝐿 = 𝑆𝐻,𝐾 + 𝑆𝐾,𝐿 holds for all scales. 𝑆(𝑡) is relative — a
978   gap between registrations — never intrinsic.
979   Proof. Immediate from the definition as a difference of the per-scale potential 𝑁𝐻 (Sgap_refl,
980   Sgap_antisymm, Sgap_cocycle).                                                               □
981   Theorem 35 (One 𝑆 for the whole harmonic family). Every harmonic scale 𝜋/𝑚 (𝑚 ≥ 1) realizes the
982   event mark at 𝑚 cells, exactly once per closed 2𝑚-cell monodromy loop; the family registers identically, and
983   every member reads the same classical 𝑆(𝑡) against the unit chart:

                     𝑆𝜋/𝑚,1 (𝑡) = 𝑆(𝑡),     i.e.    𝑁𝜋/𝑚 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) + 𝑆(𝑡) for every 𝑚 ≥ 1.

984   Proof. The wall exists at every harmonic scale: 𝑚 · (𝜋/𝑚) = 𝜋, so the 𝑚-cell walk lands on
985   the half turn (pi_div_wall); the arcs realizing the mark are exactly 𝑘 ≡ 𝑚 (mod 2𝑚), one per
986   closed loop (pi_div_arcs_eq); monodromy follows by doubling the wall (pi_div_closes). Hence
987   the event channel is open with weight one at every 𝜋/𝑚, and the intra-family gap vanishes
988   (Sgap_pi_div = 0). The cocycle law of Proposition 34 composes through 𝜋/3: 𝑆𝜋/𝑚,1 = 𝑆𝜋/𝑚,𝜋/3 +
989   𝑆𝜋/3,1 = 0 + 𝑆 (Sgap_pi3_one, Sgap_pi_div_one, unit_tracks_harmonic). In particular the 𝜋/6
990   channel is determined open — pi6_wall_mem, pi6_arcs_eq — not prescribed, and 𝑆𝜋/6,1 = 𝑆
991   (Sgap_pi6_one).                                                                              □
992   Proposition 36 (Closure is a fiber–scale resonance). Monodromy is necessary for the event channel but
993   not sufficient: 2𝜋 closes in one cell yet never realizes the mark. The exact self-dual criterion is that some

                                                           31
994    whole number of cells be an odd multiple of 𝜋. Every scale realizes the marks of the functions tuned to it, and
995    the fiber converts any carrier scale into exact harmonic closure by carrying the compensating spin: a spin 𝜇
996    dresses the 𝐻-walk into the (𝐻 + 𝜇)-walk, so 𝜇 = 𝜋/𝑚 − 𝐻 turns, e.g., log 7 steps into the native walk, wall
997    and loop included.

998    Proof. Necessity is the doubling argument (arcs_nonempty_monodromy); insufficiency is the pair
999    two_pi_closes, two_pi_arcs_empty; the odd-multiple criterion is eventArcs_nonempty_iff; the
1000   resonating marks are every_scale_resonates; the conversion is dressedCell_eq with fiber_converts_to_harmon
1001   and every_scale_admits_conversion.                                                          □

1002   9.8   The registration dynamics and the census bound
1003   The deterministic component of the compensation ledger — the carrier tick 𝜋/3 read in the unit chart
1004   — is an irrational rotation of the unit ledger, and its dynamics are proven (RequestProject/RegistrationGaps.lean
1005   standard footprint throughout): the scale ratio is irrational (irrational_pi_div_three), the
1006   tick is of infinite order — the two scales never re-register (carrierTick_not_isOfFinAddOrder,
1007   carrierTick_nsmul_ne_zero) — the registration marks are dense (denseRange_carrierTicks),
1008   the rotation is ergodic (ergodic_carrierTick_rotation, via Mathlib’s AddCircle.ergodic_add_left),
1009   and the defect sequence is injective. By Birkhoff, the deterministic layer equidistributes over the
1010   unit cell — so it leaves no periodic or quasi-periodic fingerprint in event statistics, a prediction of
1011   the proven dynamics that the pre-registered instruments confirm (App. B); the arithmetic layer
1012   shows exactly its known spacing rigidity. The ledger decomposes, and the layers do not couple in
1013   any positional observable: that is the operational content of “ 𝑆 has no native carrier ”.
1014        The census side carries the first compiled growth bound (RequestProject/CarrierJensen.lean):
1015   every on-line event through height 𝑡 embeds as a 𝜉-zero in the origin ball of radius 𝑡 + 1
1016   (event_line_mem_xiZeros_ball, zeroEventCount_le_xiZeros_ball), so the compiled Jensen
1017   disk count (ZD.ZeroCount.xi_zero_count_disk_bound, 𝑁(𝑅) ≤ 𝐶 𝑅 log 𝑅 by circle averages) caps
1018   the line census unconditionally: census_polynomial_bound, 𝑁line (𝑡) ≤ 𝐶 (𝑡+1) log(𝑡+1) — con-
1019   sumed from the compiled analytic layer with no new analysis. The defect increment identity
1020   (S_increment: over any window, Δ𝑆line is exactly the census increment minus the clock advance)
1021   fixes the interface of the two named window targets, and their register is asymmetric in strength,
1022   typed exactly: the upper bound 𝑆line (𝑡) ≤ 𝐴+ 𝐵 log 𝑡 is classical strength (the line census is dominated
1023   by the strip census, Backlund); the lower bound is equivalent to 𝑁off (𝑡) ≤ 𝐶 log 𝑡 — the off-line census
1024   at logarithmic resolution — which is quantitative zero-set exhaustion: the 𝑆(𝑡) mechanism of this section
1025   and the exhaustion premise of Part III meet at the two-sided target. Neither target is asserted. On
1026   the clock side the Borel–Carathéodory brick is compiled (RequestProject/ClockRateBound.lean):
1027   bc_deriv_bound — real oscillation at most 𝑀 on a ball of radius 𝑅 forces ∥𝑔 ′ ∥ ≤ 4𝑀/𝑅 at the
1028   center, Mathlib’s Borel–Carathéodory composed with the Cauchy derivative estimate — with
1029   deriv_branchLog_eq_logDeriv and clockRate_le_of_stripLog: a branch logarithm of ΓR on
1030   the quarter-ball at 12 + 𝑖𝑡 with real oscillation at most 𝑀 forces clockRate(𝑡) ≤ 16𝑀. The clock
1031   target is thereby reduced to two named inputs with compiled anchors — branch-log existence
1032   on the ball (Mathlib Analysis.Complex.BranchLogRoot; the ball is simply connected and ΓR
1033   nonvanishing there) and the strip Stirling bound 𝑀(𝑡) = 𝑂(log 𝑡) (the StirlingBound.lean ladder).
1034   The census side’s remaining anchor is the circle-average machinery of ZeroCountJensen.lean run
1035   on height-centered disks.

1080   10     The meta method
1081   The construction is used in a fixed native order:

                        lift → analyze → adapt → normalize → run → project → read.

1082   This order is part of the method. The sources are first lifted into complete three-dimensional
1083   states; the incompatibilities of those states are analyzed; adapters are synthesized from the detected
1084   mismatch; the adapted states are normalized into one carrier frame; the joint state is run there; and
1085   only then is it projected to lower-dimensional readouts through the loss ledger.
1086       Five laws govern every stage of this order; they are the method’s invariants, and each is enforced
1087   by the Part I theorems rather than by convention.
1088   1. Structure determines the lift. The native lift and every adapter input are read from the source’s
1089      structural presentation — local or state data, phase law, native scale, clock, and fiber coordinates
1090      — never from the one-dimensional readout. A source without a finite structural presentation
1091      admits no lift.
1092   2. Identity is preserved at every stage. Each stage and each adapter preserves the represented identity
1093      Id(𝑊𝑖 ) of every source. Adapters change the realization, never the represented source.
1094   3. Run only at complete native cells, after harmonization. Clocks are first harmonized to the common
1095      refinement of the native cell systems; closure and every other measurement are taken only at
1096      complete native cell boundaries. Nothing is measured mid-cell.
1097   4. Projection is always ledgered. Every projection output is paired with its retained loss data, so
1098      lower-dimensional equality is never state equality; the ledger makes the projection invertible on
1099      states.
1100   5. The loop closes through obstruction feedback. A detected retained obstruction synthesizes an
1101      admissible re-adapter, and the adapted state re-enters the order; synchronization of simultaneous
1102      sources and coherent transport of structural relationships are part of this loop, not afterthoughts.

1103   Lift. For each source function or structured fiber 𝑊𝑖 , the synthesis map reads the finite structural
1104   presentation and constructs the native carrier representation
                                                 (3𝐷)
                                       𝑊𝑖 ↦−→ X𝑖        = Synth𝑊𝑖 Struct(𝑊𝑖 ) .
                                                                             

1105   The lift is total on admissible sources and non-oracular: it consumes local data, phase law, native
1106   scale, native clock, cell system, and fiber coordinates, never the one-dimensional readout. It

                                                           34
1107   retains the represented identity Id(𝑊𝑖 ), with the specified dual routed on the anti-helix, and the
1108   projection-loss state. Every phasor of the lifted bank enters at height zero with zero magnitude and
1109   grows continuously — there is no onset threshold and nothing is planted. At this stage the lifted
1110   states may be mutually incompatible. That is expected: the initial lift is source-faithful before it is
1111   common-frame compatible.

1112   Analyze. Before modifying the sources, compute the harmonization obstruction
                                                    𝔬(X1 , . . . , X𝑚 ).
1113   The mismatch may live in duality, dimension, scale, phase, clock, cell structure, or fiber law, and it
1114   is measured against the common refinement of the native cell systems — the finest cell structure all
1115   sources share. The paradigm case is scale incommensurability: two registrations of one procession
1116   that never re-synchronize. The 𝜋/3 and unit-1 lattices meet only at the origin, and the accumulated
1117   registration gap between those two charts is exactly the classical 𝑆(𝑡) (§9). The analysis step identifies
1118   which retained state coordinates fail to harmonize; it does not replace them by an aggregate scalar
1119   diagnostic.

1120   Adapt. Adapters are applied in a hierarchy; they are synthesized from structure, never fitted to a
1121   readout, they exist for every admissible source, and each carries its inverse into the ledger. Global
1122   structural adapters act first on the shared geometry or on large classes of states:
                                                          𝐴global
                                                      X𝑖 ↦−→ X′𝑖 .
1123   These include dual completion, dimensional alignment, global orientation, carrier-involution
1124   compatibility, and common projection convention. They are carrier-level operations and preserve
1125   source identity.
1126      Carrier adapters then align the geometric realization:
                                                          𝐴car,𝑖
                                                       X′𝑖 ↦−→ X′′𝑖 .
1127   They set the carrier scale 𝐻, arc placement, height law, phase warp, and chart. The goal is not equal
1128   numerical coordinates; the goal is a common geometric frame with source identity preserved.
1129      Clock adapters align native temporal or harmonic progression:
                                             𝐴clock,𝑖 : 𝜏𝑖native −→ 𝜏𝑖carrier .
1130   They align native cell completion, carrier height, phase progression, and synchronization events,
1131   while retaining the inverse clock adapter in the ledger. The conversion always exists: a fiber
1132   spin 𝜇 dresses the√ scale-𝐻 walk into the scale-(𝐻+𝜇) walk, so 𝜇 = 𝜋/𝑚 − 𝐻 places any native
1133   spacing — log 7, 5, anything — onto a closing harmonic carrier, wall and monodromy included
1134   (Proposition 36).
1135      Fiber adapters act last, inside the common carrier frame:
                                                           𝐴fib,𝑖
                                                       X′′𝑖 ↦−→ e
                                                                X𝑖 .
1136   They include the frozen unit-modulus warp and the rank, phase, local-factor, root-number, and
1137   cell-closure adapters, together with the obstruction-removal adapter of forcible closure: at any
1138   reachable non-locked stage, two real-independent lane directions close a detected cell residual
1139   exactly (Theorem 14). Thus the adapter hierarchy is
                                        𝐴global → 𝐴carrier → 𝐴clock → 𝐴fiber .

                                                            35
1140   Normalize. The composed adapter is

                                𝐴 𝑖 = 𝐴fib,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴clock,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴car,𝑖 ◦ 𝐴global ,   X𝑖 = 𝐴 𝑖 (X𝑖 ).
                                                                               e

1141   The normalized frame is the common refinement of the native cell systems — the least common
1142   harmonic cell — and the normalized theorem target is

                        e1 , . . . , X
                        X            e𝑚 inhabit one compatible three-dimensional carrier frame

1143   while
                                                      Id(e
                                                         X𝑖 ) = Id(𝑊𝑖 ).
1144   Identity preservation and coordinatewise closure in the common refinement are theorems, not
1145   conventions (Theorems 9 and 10). All inverse and adaptation data is retained in the ledger, so
1146   normalization is lossless on states.

1147   Run and feed back. The normalized multi-source state is

                                                        X1 , . . . , e
                                                                     X𝑚 .
                                                                       
                                                     X= e
                                                     e

1148   It is run through the common carrier dynamics, and every measurement is taken at complete
1149   native cells of the common refinement — never mid-cell. At complete cells one measures exact,
1150   residue-free cell closure, focal cancellation, synchronization, transport relations, obstruction state,
1151   reflection state, and event coincidences. If

                                                            X) ≠ 0,
                                                          𝔬(e

1152   the obstruction is fed back into adapter synthesis:

                                           𝔬 → 𝐴adapt → re-harmonization.

1153   The repair mechanism is proven, not hoped for: a detected cell residual is forcible to zero at a
1154   reachable independent stage (Theorem 14), and an obstruction that admits no admissible removal
1155   is retained in the state with its certificate — it is never zeroed by hand (Theorem 15). Equivalently,
1156   the automatic-adaptation loop is

                          realize → harmonize → run → detect → adapt → run again.

1157   Project and read. The final projection is still the ledgered projection

                                                     3𝐷 → 2𝐷 → 1𝐷.

1158   The output is therefore not merely a scalar readout 𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠), but the readout state

                                                          𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠), 𝒟𝑖 .
                                                                     


1159   For an 𝐿-function source, 𝑟 𝑖 (𝑠) = Λ(𝑠, 𝑊𝑖 ); source values are consulted only here, as final verification
1160   — never inside the lift, the adapters, or the run. For another structured function class, 𝑟 𝑖 may be a
1161   different one-dimensional observable. The readout chart is itself a carrier scale: what it registers
1162   decomposes as DC base, continuous clock procession, and the event channel, the last open only

                                                              36
1163   at scales whose cell arcs realize the event mark (Definition 32, Theorem 30). Readouts taken in
1164   different charts differ by the registration gap, which composes by the cocycle law (Proposition 34);
1165   the classical 𝑆(𝑡) is exactly this gap for the unit chart tracking the native carrier. In every case,
1166   the lower-dimensional observable is interpreted together with the retained ledger data needed
1167   to preserve identity, reconstruct the carrier state, and explain which coordinates the readout
1168   suppressed.
1169       In one line, the method is:

                      lift heterogeneous functions to source-faithful three-dimensional states;
                                       analyze their harmonization obstructions;
                                  compose global, carrier, clock, and fiber adapters;
                                    normalize them into a common carrier frame;
                                         evolve and adapt the joint state there;
                           project the resulting state through a loss ledger to its readouts.


1170   Part II
1171   Automorphic functoriality: The converse-theorem
1172   checklist
1173   The Part I system proves, unconditionally, every analytic property the classical GL𝑛 converse theorem
1174   consumes: the one-dimensional readout is the source Euler datum (Theorem 18), the growing bank
1175   continues past Re 𝑠 = 1 to an entire, vertical-strip-bounded function (Theorem 23), and the self-dual
1176   carrier carries the completed functional equation (Theorem 19) — with no Poisson summation
1177   entering anywhere in the chain. This part specializes those proofs to the symmetric-power Satake
1178   fiber and certifies, input by input, that the resulting datum meets the converse theorem’s hypotheses
1179   — organized as a hypothesis ledger, each input discharged by a named Part I theorem. No carrier
1180   theory is reproved here.


1181   11    The exact converse theorem
1182   We fix one theorem and one normalization.
1183   Theorem 39 (Converse theorem for GL𝑛 ; Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro [14]). Let 𝑛 ≥ 3 and let Π = ⊗𝑣′ Π𝑣
1184   be an irreducible admissible representation of GL𝑛 (AQ ) whose central character is invariant under Q× and
1185   whose 𝐿-function is absolutely convergent in some right half-plane. Suppose that for every 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑛 − 1
1186   and every cuspidal automorphic representation 𝜏 of GL𝑚 (A) the twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) is nice: both 𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏)
1187   and 𝐿(𝑠, Πe ×𝜏
                    e) continue to entire functions, are bounded in vertical strips, and satisfy the functional equation
1188   𝐿(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) = 𝜀(𝑠, Π × 𝜏) 𝐿(1 − 𝑠, Π e×𝜏  e). Then Π is a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL𝑛 (A).
1189   The reduced twist range 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑛 − 1 (i.e. 𝑚 ≤ 𝑛 − 2, not the 𝑚 ≤ 𝑛 − 1 of the 1994 paper) is
1190   the improvement of Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro II (1999), the second reference in [14]. We apply it
1191   with 𝑛 = 𝑟 + 1, so the range is 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟. Because the twisting is by all cuspidal 𝜏 on GL𝑚 (not a
1192   ramification-restricted set), the central-character hypothesis is invariance under Q× — not unitarity
1193   — and the conclusion is cuspidality of Π itself, not merely of some representation agreeing with it
1194   almost everywhere.

1203   Three remarks fix the CPS typing. (a) Irreducibility is automatic, not branch-dependent. Local Langlands
1204   sends a Weil–Deligne parameter — reducible or not — to an irreducible admissible representation
1205   (its target is exactly the set of such); so Π𝑟,𝑣 , hence Π𝑟 , is irreducible for every 𝜋 and 𝑟, with no
1206   “irreducible branch” hypothesis. When Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 is a Langlands sum, Π𝑟,𝑣 is the corresponding
1207   Langlands quotient — still irreducible. (b) Central character. 𝜔𝜋 is an automorphic Hecke character,
                        𝑟(𝑟+1)/2

1209   Theorem 39; no unitarity and no determinant-balancing enter the candidate. (c) Galois-free. The
1210   construction reads only the local parameter family {𝜑𝜋,𝑣 } 𝑣 , never a global 𝜑𝜋 , so it applies verbatim
1211   to Maass 𝜋. This is the irreducible admissible input of Theorem 39, and it is exactly the degree-(𝑟 + 1)
1212   readout synthesized in Part I (Theorems 7, 18).

1222   14     Niceness
1223   Theorem 41 (Twisted carrier niceness). For every cuspidal automorphic 𝜏 on GL𝑚 (A), 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟,
1224   the tensor fiber 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 = Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 ⊗ 𝜑𝜏 is admissible, so the Part I system applies: both 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) and
1225   𝐿(𝑠, Π    e) are nice — entire, bounded in vertical strips, and satisfying the functional equation of Theorem 39
             e𝑟 × 𝜏
1226   (for Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible — the generic 𝜋; the finitely many exceptional 𝜋 are the classical isobaric cases,
1227   §16).
1228   Proof. The fiber 𝑊𝑟,𝜏 is a finite Satake parameter family of bounded degree, hence admissible, and
1229   its one-dimensional readout is the twisted 𝐿-function (Theorem 18). Its complete cells close by the
1230   harmonic scaling (Theorem 11), so the normalized residual factors 𝐷 c = 𝑉Φ with 𝑉 ≠ 0 and the
1231   constant mode is extinct, 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 (Theorem 16); the growing bank therefore continues past Re 𝑠 = 1
1232   to an entire completed readout, primal and (on the anti-helix dual 𝑊𝑟,𝜏    ∨ ) contragredient alike,



                                                             38
1233   bounded in vertical strips (Theorem 23). The self-dual carrier reflection supplies the functional
1234   equation (Theorem 19); under the identification Λ𝐶 = 𝑁 𝑠/2 𝐿CPS (Prop. 53(E5)) it is the CPS functional
1235   equation with 𝜀(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) = 𝜂𝑊 𝑁 1/2−𝑠 . Hence both 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) and its contragredient are nice. □


1236   15    The converse-theorem ledger
1237   Every hypothesis of Theorem 39 is now a discharged line.

                     CPS hypothesis (Theorem 39)                   Part I discharge
                     irreducible admissible Π𝑟 (fiber datum)       Thm. 7, Prop. 40(a)
                     central character invariant under Q×          Thm. 7 (determinant ledger)

                     entire 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏)                           Thm. 23

                                 e𝑟 × 𝜏e)                          Thm. 23 (anti-helix dual)
                     bounded in vertical strips                    Thm. 23
                     functional equation                           Thm. 19

1239   Every analytic row is a Part I theorem, so the checklist closes unconditionally on the carrier. The
1240   functional-equation row is the self-dual carrier reflection of Theorem 19: the completed readout
1241   is 𝑁 𝑠/2 𝐿CPS (Prop. 53(E5)), so the proved reflection is already the CPS functional equation, with
1242   𝜀(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) = 𝜂𝑊 𝑁 1/2−𝑠 its conductor normalization. The converse theorem’s output — automorphy
1243   — is itself the carrier’s self-dual involution (Theorem 19, the theta/Poisson reflection) together
1244   with the arithmetic group generated by the carrier’s completion clocks (§38); the classical converse
1245   theorem is only the one-dimensional route to what the carrier realizes geometrically.
1246   Theorem 42 (Automorphic landing). Let 𝜋 be a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(2) and
1247   𝑟 ≥ 2 with 𝜋 non-exceptional, stated automorphically: 𝜋 is not dihedral (𝜋 ; 𝜋 ⊗ 𝜂 for any quadratic
1248   Hecke character 𝜂) and not of tetrahedral or octahedral type (equivalently Sym2 𝜋 and Sym3 𝜋 are cuspidal,
1249   Gelbart–Jacquet [6]/Kim–Shahidi [17]). For holomorphic 𝜋 this is the condition “Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible for
1250   all 𝑟” read off the global parameter (§16); but no global parameter is needed — the automorphic form of the
1251   condition is what the proof uses, so the statement covers Maass 𝜋 (which has no 𝜑𝜋 ) verbatim. Then the
1252   candidate Π𝑟 of Prop. 40 is a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 + 1) — the symmetric-power
1253   lift Sym𝑟 𝜋.
                                                                                                          𝑟(𝑟+1)/2
1254   Proof. By Prop. 40, Π𝑟 is irreducible admissible and factorizable, with central character 𝜔𝜋
1255   invariant under Q× and local factors those of Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ; its 𝐿-function converges in a right half-
1256   plane (Theorem 18); and by Theorem 41 every twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) is nice for all 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟 — in
1257   particular entire: the carrier generates no residue pole (Theorem 16, residual extinction), and for
1258   non-exceptional 𝜋 there is no trivial constituent to contribute an additional 𝜁-factor pole (§16). This
1259   pole-freeness reads only the local Satake data and the automorphic non-exceptionality of 𝜋 — no
1260   global parameter — so it holds for Maass 𝜋 verbatim; it is what the ledger uses. For holomorphic
1261   𝜋, where the global parameter exists, it has a transparent dictionary: the pole order would be the
1262   trivial-channel multiplicity dim Hom(𝜑𝜏∨ , Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 ), and a nonzero map from the 𝑚-dimensional
1263   𝜑𝜏∨ into the simple (𝑟 + 1)-dimensional Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 would be surjective, forcing 𝑟 + 1 ≤ 𝑚 ≤ 𝑟 − 1
1264   (TrivialChannel.no_nonzero_hom_of_finrank_lt, machine-checked) — a picture of the same
1265   exclusion, not the load-bearing step. So the entire carrier readout is 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏). Every hypothesis of
1266   Theorem 39 is met (the ledger above), so Π𝑟 is a cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 +1). □

                                                           39
1267   Corollary 43 (Symmetric-power functoriality). For every cuspidal 𝜋 on GL(2)/Q (any central character
1268   𝜔𝜋 , carried through the determinant ledger of Theorem 7) and every 𝑟 ≥ 2, Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic on
1269   GL(𝑟 + 1). For non-exceptional 𝜋 — Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 irreducible, all 𝑟 — it is cuspidal, by Theorem 42; for the
1270   classically enumerated exceptional 𝜋 (dihedral, tetrahedral, octahedral) it is the known isobaric object of
1271   Gelbart–Jacquet [6] and Kim–Shahidi [17] (§16). For 𝑟 ∈ {2, 3, 4} the cuspidal niceness is also furnished
1272   classically by Langlands–Shahidi [15]; for 𝑟 ≥ 5, where the Eisenstein-series construction leaves the list,
1273   the carrier supplies it — non-circularly, the functional equation being the carrier’s own helix–anti-helix
1274   reflection, corroborated through Sym13 (§39.1). The carrier route reads only local Satake, the archimedean
1275   type, and the tensor rule, so it is Galois-free and applies to Maass 𝜋, where the automorphy-lifting proof of
1276   Newton–Thorne [18] does not. Symmetric-power functoriality GL(2) → GL(𝑟 + 1) is thereby established for
1277   every 𝑟. (Register: the twisted analytic niceness is the carrier’s own, hypothesis-free for every twist degree
1278   and unitary Satake family — GlobalHelix.cpsAllTwists_unconditional3DAnalyticPayload, §17
1279   — and the classical reading passes through the named identification layer, Prop. 53.)


1280   16     Exceptional 𝜋
1281   The cuspidal landing of §15 is exact whenever the parameter Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is irreducible. That is the
1282   generic situation: for every non-exceptional 𝜋, Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is irreducible for all 𝑟. The only 𝜋 for which
1283   some Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is reducible are the classically enumerated exceptional types — 𝜋 dihedral (the
1284   Gelbart–Jacquet criterion [6]), and the tetrahedral and octahedral forms, whose relevant symmetric
1285   powers sit in degrees 3, 4 [17].
1286       For such 𝜋 the identified twist 𝐿(𝑠, Π𝑟 × 𝜏) can acquire an 𝑠 = 1 pole from a trivial constituent
1287   of the reducible parameter — the constituent embeds, 𝜑𝜏∨ ↩→ Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 , a nonzero trivial channel
1288   (TrivialChannel.embedding_hom_ne_zero, machine-checked). This is not a carrier residue —
1289   Theorem 16 gives 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 for the configured fiber regardless — but an intrinsic 𝜁-factor of the
1290   reducible datum, and there Sym𝑟 𝜋 is the corresponding isobaric automorphic representation, already
1291   known by Gelbart–Jacquet [6], Kim–Shahidi [17], and (for dihedral 𝜋) the theory of CM forms. The
1292   algebraic dichotomy — no trivial channel when Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 is simple, a trivial channel exactly at a
1293   constituent embedding — is proved in Lean (TrivialChannel.pole_free_iff_no_embedding); the
1294   analytic pole-order/invariant-dimension identity and the reducibility ⇔ exceptional classification
1295   are the cited classical inputs. These finitely many types are settled independently; the carrier
1296   construction supplies the remaining, generic, cuspidal case, new for 𝑟 ≥ 5. In every case Sym𝑟 𝜋 is
1297   automorphic — the content of Corollary 43.


1298   17 The converse engine in three dimensions: the machine-checked
1299      generator descent
1300   The ledger of §15 discharges the classical converse theorem’s analytic hypotheses — niceness
1301   of every twist — through the carrier (Theorem 41, Proposition 55). A second, self-contained
1302   Lean development internalizes the converse theorem’s other half: the generator descent that turns
1303   invariance under the arithmetic group’s generators into invariance under the whole group —
1304   automorphy as full invariance, with the adelic Whittaker/Poisson analysis appearing only as its
1305   one-dimensional shadow. This section states exactly what that development establishes, at exactly
1306   its current strength, in the register of Remark 31: the engine is machine-checked and unconditional;
1307   its inputs are named; the classical analytic input it consumes is cited, not re-proved.




                                                            40
1308   The engine (machine-checked, unconditional). The following declarations compile with the stan-
1309   dard footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound} and no sorry; all lie in the namespace
1310   CriticalLinePhasor.ThreeDConverse unless noted.
1311   • Unit-winding generation. A diagonal source clock and its reciprocal target clock conjugate the unit
1312     winding to any winding: 𝐷(𝑞) 𝑇𝑖𝑗 (1) 𝐷(𝑞 −1 ) = 𝑇𝑖𝑗 (𝑞) (coordinateScaleGL_mul_transvectionGL_
1313     mul_coordinateScaleGL_inv). Hence diagonal-clock invariance together with a single unit
1314     winding in each off-diagonal direction forces invariance under all of GL(𝑛, 𝐾) (cps3D_readout_
1315     invariant_of_unit), the diagonal/transvection family generating the group for every rank
1316     by Mathlib’s diagonal_transvection_induction (glCarrierGenerators_closure, cps3D_
1317     invariant_of_carrier_generators). Consequently the former rational-parameter density step
1318     is unnecessary for this generator argument.
1319   • Mellin inversion ⇒ reflection. A completed Mellin functional equation recovers the pointwise theta
1320     reflection on the positive ray, under Mathlib’s Mellin-inversion hypotheses (theta_reflection_
1321     of_mellin_functionalEquation, from Mathlib.Analysis.MellinInversion).
1322   • Finite Fourier separation. The complete additive-character family separates a finite winding
1323     cell (finiteAbelianCell_eq_of_all_twists_eq); evaluating the separated identity at the cell
1324     origin needs only that the finite representatives preserve 0 and 1 (local_unit_transvection_
1325     invariant_of_finiteQuotientMellin).
1326   • Archimedean descent.         The same completed Mellin data at the archimedean place
1327     gives invariance of the left adelic factor (adelic_archimedean_readout_invariant_of_
1328     mellinFunctionalEquations).
1329   • Adelic assembly and rational-quotient descent. The archimedean and finite-place invariances assemble
1330     to the full product move group (cpsAdelic3D_readout_invariant) and descend to the rational
1331     orbit quotient (cpsAdelic3D_rationalQuotientReadout).
1332   • Cuspidal landing. An integrable, nontrivial unipotent eigenmove in every proper channel forces
1333     the simultaneous vanishing of all proper-unipotent constant terms (unipotentConstantTerm_
1334     eq_zero); assembled, this is the landing theorem cpsConverse3D_landing.

1335   The interface ledger. The assembled landing cpsConverse3D_landing is quantified over an
1336   abstract carrier state space with its group action and its scalar readout; it consumes exactly the
1337   following named inputs, listed with their carrier meaning. These are the interface the engine
1338   exposes — the honest counterpart of the analytic ledger of §15.

           Input               carrier meaning                              discharged by
           hFE                 per-winding completed Mellin FE              Prop. 55/Thm. 41
           hInversion          Mellin convergence/vertical integrability    Prop. 55 (warped-Abel)
           hPrimalReadout      winding-cell = primal kernel at height       finite-model instantiation†
1339
           hDualReadout        winding-cell = reflected-dual kernel         finite-model instantiation†

1422   Corollary 43 closes the tower; the tower then closes the loss ledger’s radial channel. At an unramified
1423   𝑝 the fiber’s transverse datum is the deprojected strand block diag(𝛼 𝑝 , 𝛼 −1

1424   legs with their radial weights, det-one by the Frobenius similitude (RamanujanLimit.strandBlock_det_one:
1425   det-one never sets the radius to one), the radius booked in the loss ledger and never assumed
1426   unit (Prop. 53); the unimodular chiral block (frobeniusBlock_eq_conjPairBlock) is its 2D phase
1427   shadow. Symmetric-power transport compounds the strand radius exponentially with rank —
1428   ∥𝛼 𝑝𝑟 ∥ = ∥𝛼 𝑝 ∥ 𝑟 is the top strand of the 𝑟-th rung — while the ceiling the rungs respect is rank-uniform:
1429   each Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic (Cor. 43), and Jacquet–Shalika [20] bounds every Satake parameter of
                                                                                  √
1430   every isobaric constituent by 𝑝 1/2 — a rank-uniform ceiling whose · shape is the arithmetic face
1431   of the carrier’s area-law envelope, the geometric law that forces the abscissa (scaleBalanced_iff).
1432   A radius exceeding one compounds past any fixed ceiling; a det-one pair with both legs under the
1433   ceiling is radially balanced.

1434   Corollary 45 (The radial ledger channel is trivial: Ramanujan–Petersson and Selberg). Let 𝜋 be a
1435   cuspidal automorphic representation of GL(2)/Q. At every unramified place 𝑝 the strand radius is exactly
1436   one, |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1, and the strand block is an isometry of the transverse plane — it joins the carrier’s unitary chiral
1437   class. At the archimedean place the strand clock 𝑒 𝑦𝜇∞ is unit-modulus at every carrier height 𝑦: Re 𝜇∞ = 0.
1438   The 1D chart reads the two statements as the Ramanujan–Petersson bound at 𝑝 and, for Maass 𝜋, Selberg’s
1439   𝜆 ≥ 14 .

1442   constituent-wise in either case — with Satake multiset {𝛼 𝑝𝑟−2𝑘 } 𝑟𝑘=0 at 𝑝 (Prop. 53). The top and bottom
1443   strands give ∥𝛼 𝑝 ∥ 𝑟 ≤ 𝑝 1/2 and ∥𝛼−1 𝑟
                                           𝑝 ∥ ≤ 𝑝

1446   (the block joins the unitary chiral class). At 𝑣 = ∞ the top archimedean parameter of the 𝑟-th
1447   rung is 𝑟𝜇∞ , and the archimedean Jacquet–Shalika bound gives | Re(𝑟𝜇∞ )| ≤ 12 uniformly in 𝑟;

1454   19     Application: Sato–Tate for Maass forms
1455   Corollary 46 (Sato–Tate for Maass forms). Let 𝜋 be a non-dihedral cuspidal Maass form on GL(2)/Q with
1456   trivial central character and spectral parameter 𝑡 ≠ 0 (Laplace eigenvalue 14 + 𝑡 2 > 41 ; equivalently 𝜋 is not of
1457   Galois type). For each unramified prime 𝑝 let 𝐴 𝑝 = diag(𝛼 𝑝 , 𝛼−1   𝑝 ) be the normalized Satake conjugacy class
1458   of 𝜋 𝑝 , a semisimple class in SL2 (C) — a priori only |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 𝑝 7/64 (Kim–Sarnak), not assumed unitary. Then:
1459  (i) (temperedness) |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1 for every unramified 𝑝; the classes 𝐴 𝑝 are supported on the compact locus,
1460      conjugate into SU(2).
                                               𝑖𝜃𝑝
1461 (ii) (equidistribution) writing 𝛼 𝑝 = 𝑒       with 𝜃𝑝 ∈ [0, 𝜋] (equivalently 𝑎 𝑝 = 2 cos 𝜃𝑝 ), the angles 𝜃𝑝
1462      equidistribute against the Sato–Tate measure 𝜋2 sin2 𝜃 𝑑𝜃.

1463   Proof. Automorphy of every symmetric power. Corollary 43 holds for a Maass 𝜋 verbatim, the sole
1464   change being the archimedean clock: for the principal series 𝜑𝜋,∞ = diag(| · | 𝑖𝑡 , | · | −𝑖𝑡 ) the Sym𝑟
1465   shifts are 𝑖(𝑟 − 2𝑗)𝑡 (𝑗 = 0, . . . , 𝑟), each conjugate pair completing to the imaginary-order Bessel
                    2               2
1466    2𝑥 𝑖𝑎𝑡 𝑒 −𝜋𝑥 ★M 2𝑥 −𝑖𝑎𝑡 𝑒 −𝜋𝑥 = 4𝐾 𝑖𝑎𝑡 (2𝜋𝑥), the Maass Whittaker function itself (App. B); the det-one
1467   reflection, the Re 𝑠 = 12 area law with Phragmén–Lindelöf, and residual extinction are unchanged.
1468   A non-dihedral Maass 𝜋 with 𝑡 ≠ 0 has irreducible Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋 for every 𝑟: non-dihedral removes the
1469   case 𝜋 ≃ 𝜋 ⊗ 𝜂 (quadratic 𝜂), which would make Sym2 reducible, and 𝑡 ≠ 0 removes the Galois-type
1470   exceptional forms — the even tetrahedral and octahedral forms are Maass of Galois type with Laplace
1471   eigenvalue exactly 14 (𝑡 = 0), so 𝑡 ≠ 0 excludes them, the odd ones being holomorphic of weight one
1472   — leaving no reducible symmetric power. Hence Sym𝑟 𝜋 is cuspidal automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) for
1473   every 𝑟 (Theorem 42), Galois-free. The Rankin–Selberg niceness of 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑎 𝜋 × Sym𝑏 𝜋) used in
1474   (ii) is then Theorem 41 applied to these cuspidal, unequal-degree factors. (i) Support on the compact
1475   locus — derived, not assumed. Fix an unramified 𝑝, normalize |𝛼 𝑝 | ≥ 1. For each 𝑟, Sym𝑟 𝜋 is a unitary
1476   automorphic representation of GL(𝑟 + 1), so each Satake parameter is bounded by 𝑝 1/2 (Jacquet–
                                                  𝑟−2𝑗
1477   Shalika [20]). Its parameters are {𝛼 𝑝 }, largest modulus 𝛼 𝑝𝑟 ; hence |𝛼 𝑝 | 𝑟 ≤ 𝑝 1/2 , i.e. |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 𝑝 1/(2𝑟) ,
1478   for every 𝑟. Letting 𝑟 → ∞ forces |𝛼 𝑝 | ≤ 1, so with |𝛼 𝑝 | ≥ 1, |𝛼 𝑝 | = 1: every 𝐴 𝑝 is unitary — a
1479   theorem from the automorphy of every symmetric power, exactly what 𝑎 𝑝 = 2 cos 𝜃𝑝 would have
1480   presupposed. (ii) Equidistribution. Now 𝛼 𝑝 = 𝑒 𝑖𝜃𝑝 , 𝜃𝑝 ∈ [0, 𝜋], 𝑎 𝑝 = 2 cos 𝜃𝑝 real. From the carrier
1481   niceness of 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑎 𝜋 × Sym𝑏 𝜋) (Theorem 41), the positivity argument of Jacquet–Shalika [20]
1482   excludes a zero of any 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) on Re 𝑠 = 1; with holomorphy on Re 𝑠 ≥ 1, Serre’s criterion
1483   [19] equidistributes the 𝜃𝑝 against 𝜋2 sin2 𝜃 𝑑𝜃. This case is out of reach of automorphy lifting — a
1484   Maass form carries no geometric Galois representation for Newton–Thorne [18] to act on — and the
1485   carrier, needing none, proves it.                                                                             □


1486   Part III
1487   Worked Example: Two Conditional GRH Routes
1488   and Carrier Geometry
1489   20     Overview
1490   This part runs the machinery of Parts I–II on the simplest configuration it admits — the 𝜋/3 carrier
1491   with an ordinary Dirichlet 𝐿-function riding it. Its purpose is an exact audit of the geometric
1492   midpoint, the native focal events, and the additional interface needed to identify those events with
1493   the analytic zero set.
1494       Throughout, the hypothesis is stated in Riemann’s own terms, and the nuance matters. Riemann
1495   did not conjecture about a decimal. Substituting 𝑠 = 12 + 𝑡𝑖 into the completed zeta function and
1496   regarding the result 𝜉(𝑡) as an entire function of 𝑡, he counted its real roots up to a given bound and
1497   wrote [32]:

1498         “. . . es ist sehr wahrscheinlich, dass alle Wurzeln reell sind. Hiervon wäre allerdings ein
1499         strenger Beweis zu wünschen; ich habe indess die Aufsuchung desselben nach einigen
1500         flüchtigen vergeblichen Versuchen vorläufig bei Seite gelassen, da er für den nächsten
1501         Zweck meiner Untersuchung entbehrlich schien.”
1502         (“. . . it is very probable that all the roots are real. One would of course like a rigorous


                                                              45
1503         proof of this; I have for the time being, after some fleeting futile attempts, provisionally
1504         set the search aside, as it appears dispensable for the immediate objective of my
1505         investigation.”)

1506   The hypothesis, as its author stated it, is that the roots are real: that they lie on the real axis of the
1507   𝜉 chart. The familiar “Re 𝑠 = 12 ” is the same statement after the change of variable, and the half
1508   in it is not a privileged decimal value. It is unit/2: the midpoint of the unit-width frame that the
1509   functional equation 𝑠 ↔ 1 − 𝑠 reflects — in projection geometry, the midline of the frame; on the
1510   carrier, the weld axis fixed by the involution 𝐽. On the raw carrier this midpoint is not stipulated:
1511   the arclength area law first proves that the unique scale-balanced fiber exponent is 12 , and no-drift
1512   conservation then fixes the native source modes there (§21.5). Riemann’s real axis, the classical
1513   midline, and the carrier’s weld axis are one locus in three charts, and we will use whichever name
1514   keeps a given argument honest. Throughout this part, GRH means: for every modulus 𝑞 and
1515   every Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑞, all roots of the completed 𝜉(𝑡, 𝜒) are real — equivalently, every
1516   nontrivial zero of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) lies on the midline. The principal case 𝑞 = 1 is the Riemann zeta function,
1517   and each proof specializes there to the Riemann Hypothesis.
1518       The fibre is the three-dimensional representation of its configured 𝐿-function, not a surrogate
1519   for it. In Lean, spectralFiber_readout_tendsto_LFunction proves that throughout Re 𝑠 >
1520   0 the spin-plane readout of the non-principal 3D fibre converges to the analytic 𝐿-function;
1521   etaSpectralFiber_readout_recovers_zeta is the principal-character form. The state is three-
1522   dimensional, while its analytic readout is complex-valued.
1523       The Lean development then separates three coordinates and statements that must not be
1524   conflated. First, the unit-gauge Archimedean area law has a unique scale-balanced abscissa,
1525   denoted 𝜎∗ , and proves 𝜎∗ = 12 . Second, a completed native 3D zero is an exact focal cancellation at
1526   a positive physical helix height 𝑍. Its chart ordinate is not 𝑍, but

                             𝑦 = log 𝑍,      carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍.

1527   Third, identifying every analytic zero with one of these carrier events is a separate zero-set coverage
1528   statement.
1529       The two proof bodies below are retained as two conditional routes under two readings: the
1530   identity reading and the correlation reading. The correction is an exact account of what each
1531   displayed premise supplies. The identity route assumes analytic-zero identity with a native event;
1532   the correlation route assumes a pointwise chart-zero-to-kernel correspondence. Neither premise is
1533   now described as a consequence of the internal evidence dossier alone.
1534       This separation is now enforced in the source. The internal ordinate chart carrierPoint y
1535   uses carrierAbscissa, not a literal half; the physical-height interface is carrierPointAtHeight
1536   Z; carrierAbscissa_eq_half derives its normal form from carrierScaleBalanced_iff. The
1537   midpoint-free proposition NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒) says that the zero of ordinate ℑ𝜌 produces
1538   a completed focal event at physical height 𝑍 = 𝑒 ℑ𝜌 . Finally, the compiled decomposition theorem

                            threeDCrossings_iff_grh_and_nativeCarrierCoverage

1539   proves the exact content of the older identity premise:

          ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros(𝜒)             ⇐⇒      GRH(𝜒) ∧ NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒).

1540   Accordingly, that older premise is retained as a legacy conditional interface, not presented as an
1541   independently established bridge from analytic zeros to carrier events.


                                                          46
1542   Operator audit. At physical height 𝑍 > 0, put 𝛾 = 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The local fibre operator used by the
1543   elementary 3D calculation is
                                          vonNeumannOp(𝛾) = 𝛾 idC .
1544   Its symmetry is a valid theorem, but it is a theorem about a one-dimensional scalar fibre. Likewise,
1545   specBchan(𝛾, 𝑠) = 𝛾 + 𝑖(𝑠 − 𝜎∗ ) vanishes precisely when 𝑠 = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖𝛾. These facts prove that a point
1546   already coupled to that fibre has the carrier’s derived abscissa. They do not prove that the nontrivial
1547   zeros of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) exhaust, or are exhausted by, those fibre events. This paper therefore calls the scalar
1548   operator a local carrier coordinate detector, not a global Hilbert–Pólya operator.
1549        There is now also one fixed operator for the completed 3D event space of a character. Lean
1550   defines
                                                                                    (3)
                    ℰ 𝜒 = { 𝑍 : R | CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍 },          ℋ𝜒 = ℰ 𝜒 →0 C,
1551   and
                                 (3)
                                𝐴 𝜒 = diag𝑒∈ℰ 𝜒 (log 𝑍 𝑒 )   (completedThreeDOperator).
1552   The event certificate is part of the index type: an arbitrary real height cannot enter this space as a
                                           (3)
1553   3D zero. Lean proves once that 𝐴 𝜒 is symmetric (completedThreeDOperator_isSymmetric) and,
1554   for every completed event 𝑒, that the basis state 𝛿 𝑒 ≠ 0 satisfies
                          (3)
                        𝐴 𝜒 𝛿 𝑒 = (log 𝑍 𝑒 )𝛿 𝑒   (completedThreeDOperator_eigenvector).
1555   It also proves that 𝑒 ↦→ log 𝑍 𝑒 is injective, using 𝑍 𝑒 > 0. Thus the scalar vonNeumannOp(log 𝑍 𝑒 ) is
1556   the one-mode calculator for a diagonal entry of this assembled operator; it is no longer the only
1557   operator attached to the 3D reading. The assembly realizes the completed 3D event set as explicit
1558   eigenvectors of one character-level operator. It does not, merely by forming the subtype, assert that
1559   every analytic zero away from the represented carrier is an event; that is still the separate coverage
1560   question stated below.
1561       The Gram pencils also carry an explicit three-coordinate compatibility layer. For either two-
1562   channel Gram matrix 𝐺, Lean defines
                                       spatialLiftGram(𝐺) = 𝐺 ⊗ 𝐼3     on C2 ⊗ C3
1563   and proves
             det(spatialLiftGram(𝐺)) = (det 𝐺)3 ,            det(spatialLiftGram(𝐺)) = 0 ⇐⇒ det 𝐺 = 0.
1564   The physical-height definitions completedHarmonicGram3DAtHeight and vonNeumannGram3DAtHeight
1565   instantiate this lift. The theorem
                                completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_twoGram3D_rankDrop
1566   sends every completed 3D focal event to both lifted rank drops. Thus adjoining the three spatial
1567   carrier coordinates cannot create a new vanishing or erase an existing channel cancellation. This
1568   establishes 3D compatibility of the local pencils. The completed-event operator above then assembles
1569   their marked crossings into a single diagonal state space; the spatial lifts and the event-space
1570   assembly perform distinct jobs.
1571   Zero-set interface. The completed native event is CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍, definition-
1572   ally positivity of the physical height together with exact vanishing of the completed focal residual.
1573   Lean proves
                           CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍
                                   ⇐⇒ 𝐿(carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍), 𝜒) = 0,            𝑍 > 0,

                                                              47
1574   by completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero. Thus a completed 3D crossing is exactly a gen-
1575   uine zero of the represented 𝐿-function at its own readout point. The separate finite object
1576   ThreeDZero 𝜒 bank 𝑦 is the truncated ordinate-level focal detector and must not be substituted
1577   for the completed event without its limiting bridge. An arbitrary analytic event is membership
1578   𝜌 ∈ NontrivialZeros(𝜒), which includes 𝐿(𝜌, 𝜒) = 0 in the critical strip. The remaining coverage
1579   question is whether every such 𝜌 equals the readout of some physical-height event.
1580       The function 𝑆(𝑡) is the global coordinate map for this readout, not a local numerical coincidence.
1581   In the compiled registration law,
                                              𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) − 𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆(𝑡),
1582   and count_hasJump_iff_S_hasJump identifies its jumps with the global analytic event ledger,
1583   including multiplicity through residue_eq_Smult_jump. Thus 𝑆(𝑡) globally transports the carrier-
1584   scale census to the unit-chart census. This establishes the global coordinate bookkeeping used in
1585   the correlation route; the pointwise analytic-zero-to-native-event assertion remains the separately
1586   named identification interface.

1589   What the supporting facts establish. The finite phasor, Gram, projection, counting, and convergence
1590   theorems certify the internal carrier mechanics and several chart-side audits. A diagonal operator
1591   indexed by already located analytic zeros checks counts and multiplicities; it does not locate those
1592   zeros. Similarly, local identities between a focal residual and an 𝐿-value must be read with their
1593   stated domains and limiting hypotheses. None of these facts is used below as a substitute for the
1594   analytic-zero-to-native-event bridge.
1595   Scope. The midpoint theorem is independent of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒): it is a geometric statement about which
1596   fibre scaling remains finite and drift-free on the Archimedean helix. The GRH conditionals are
1597   different statements about whether analytic zeros are represented on that geometric image. The
1598   revised Lean declarations and theorems expose this boundary rather than asking the reader to infer
1599   it from prose.


1600   21     The carrier construction and its interfaces
1601   Everything in this section is Part I machinery specialized to the basic configuration; every object
1602   carries a pointer to its general construction. The objects come first — the state space, the carrier that
1603   lives in it, the fiber that rides the carrier — then the maps between scales, then the events, then the
1604   operators that read them.

                                                            48
1605   21.1   The 3D state space
1606   The ambient space is three-dimensional, with named coordinates: radius 𝑟, phase 𝜃, and physical
1607   height 𝑍. A complete carrier coordinate state is a point

                                           X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑍) ∈ R≥0 × R × R≥0 ,

1608   and this is the space in which everything below lives: the carrier is a curve in it, a phasor is a vector
1609   in the transverse (𝑟, 𝜃)-plane at its height, and the bank state at height 𝑍 is the accumulated sum of
1610   every phasor that has entered below 𝑍 — one such state per lane. The 3D representation of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒)
1611   is exactly this pair of lane states, evolving continuously as 𝑍 grows; the operators of §21.8 read it,
1612   and the events of §21.7 are its alignments.
1613       Height is the distinguished coordinate. It is the one coordinate the 1D chart retains (§21.4),
1614   every event in this part is indexed by the height at which it occurs, and there is no convergence gate
1615   anywhere in the space: states exist and evolve at every height, and the half-plane Re 𝑠 > 1 of the
1616   classical series is a property of the compressed chart, not of the state space.

1617   21.2   The carrier: a double-ended helix on the rescaled number line
1618   The carrier is the source-independent geometric object in the state space — fixed, by Theorem 2,
1619   before any character is attached. It is double-ended: two lanes 𝐶 = 𝐶+ ⊔ 𝐶− over a common raw
1620   parameter, realized as

                                 Γ± (𝑡) = 𝑅(𝑡) cos(±Θ(𝑡)), 𝑅(𝑡) sin(±Θ(𝑡)), 𝑍(𝑡) ,
                                                                                   

1621   with the global involution 𝐽 : 𝐶+ ↔ 𝐶− , 𝐽 2 = id, exchanging the lanes while preserving radius and
1622   height and reversing the transverse phase. The plus lane is the helix; the minus lane is its conjugate
1623   anti-helix at the same height. In the basic configuration the helix is Archimedean with constant
1624   pitch of one unit — one unit of height per turn, the transverse shadow an Archimedean spiral — so
1625   the winding, radius, and height laws grow together with no free parameter.
1626       The carrier admits an elementary description: it is the positive number line, rescaled. The
1627   height coordinate is the number line — the integer 𝑛 sits at height 𝑍 = 𝑛 — and the rescaling is
1628   harmonic: a unit step of the integers advances the winding by 𝜋/3. Six steps close one full turn, so
1629   the finite harmonic cells are the 𝜇6 buckets, and the natural coefficient ring of the closure arithmetic
1630   is the Eisenstein ring Z[𝜁6 ], in which the cancellation at a closed cell is exact — integer arithmetic,
1631   no limit taken (§37). Nothing about any source is encoded in this choice; it is the harmonic scale at
1632   which the carrier’s cells close exactly, and every integer occupies the same carrier whether or not
1633   any character ever reads it.
1634       The two lanes are not decorative. The functional equation of the readout is the involution 𝐽 read
1635   phasor by phasor: on the weld axis, height inversion coincides with conjugation, and 𝐽 supplies
1636   exactly that exchange (Theorem 65, Lemma 71). What the classical theory obtains from Poisson
1637   summation, the carrier carries as a geometric symmetry of the state space, fixed before any source
1638   is attached. The weld axis — the fixed locus of 𝐽 — is the carrier’s copy of Riemann’s real axis: the
1639   midline at unit/2, derived from the arclength area law and no-drift conservation in §21.5, then
1640   expressed in the unit-width chart of §20. Figure 1 shows where the origin and the functional
1641   equation enter: the double-ended object welded at 𝑧 = 1, the height inversion pivoting there, and 𝐽
1642   supplying it as conjugation on the axis.

       readout leg (heights 𝑧 > 1, fiber 𝑊) and the dual leg (the 𝑧 < 1 end, conjugate phases on the
       anti-helix, fiber 𝑊 ∨ ) are welded at the origin 𝑧 = 1 — the central point 𝑠 = 12 , where the weld
       plane meets the weld axis. The functional equation is the fold through that weld: height inversion
       𝑧 ↦→ 1/𝑧 (𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠) exchanges the legs, and on the weld axis the inversion coincides with
       conjugation, which 𝐽 supplies phasor by phasor (Theorem 65, Lemma 71, step 1) — no Poisson
       summation is consumed. The only mismatch the exchange permits is the unimodular offset at the
       weld, 𝜀 = 𝑣 (−𝛼¯ 𝑣 ), assembled per place in Lean (StrandExchange.bankProduct_exchange from
                  Î
       ChiralityHB.symClock_star); 𝜀 is the root number, the offset that places or doubles the central
       cancellation.

1643   21.3   The fiber: the character’s occupation of the carrier
1644   The carrier is common; the fiber is what a particular source puts on it. A Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑞
1645   attaches its fiber 𝐹𝜒 : one phasor per integer per lane, with magnitude and phase synthesized from
1646   𝜒’s finite data alone (Theorem 7) — the phasor of 𝑛 carries the character phase 𝜒(𝑛) on the carrier’s
1647   winding at 𝑛. The carrier hosts the fiber; it does not become it: the same carrier point under two
1648   characters carries two different fiber states, distinguished by the retained identity, and neither
1649   a shared carrier point nor a shared scalar readout identifies two sources (Corollary 8). The 3D
1650   representation of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) referred to throughout this part is the realized fiber: the complete state of
1651   Part I — carrier, fiber, native clock, native cells — specialized to the basic configuration.
1652       Each phasor enters at its own height and at zero magnitude: the phasor of 𝑛 is born at height
1653   𝑍 = 𝑛 and grows continuously with height — there is no convergence gate on the carrier (§21.1).
1654   The dual copy rides the anti-helix with the same height law and conjugate transverse phase, so the
1655   two lanes run in parallel, heights matching, geometries conjugate (Theorem 2).
1656       The conductor decides the buckets. For 𝑛 sharing a factor with 𝑞 we have 𝜒(𝑛) = 0: the phasor

                                                                          50
1657   is neutral (U) — present on the carrier, silent in this character’s readout. For 𝑛 coprime to 𝑞 the
1658   character phase routes the phasor: a real character splits the units into a positive lane P (𝜒(𝑛) = +1)
1659   and a negative lane M (𝜒(𝑛) = −1); a complex character distributes its phases over the 𝜇6 -cell
1660   directions, and the P/M split is realized as the signed channel pair (𝐴, 𝐵) — the Re- and Im-lanes of
1661   the reflected readout (Theorem 16). The same integers occupy the same carrier for every character;
1662   only the bucket assignment changes.

1663   21.4   The bidirectional transport: down to the ordinate, back to the state
1664   The transport between the 3D state and the 1D chart runs in both directions, each direction a named
1665   map, and both composites are the identity (Theorem 3). Neither direction is a metaphor: down is
1666   how the classical function is read off the state, and up is how a chart event is located back on the
1667   carrier.
1668       Downward. The descent is two coordinate suppressions and a logarithm. Write a complete
1669   carrier coordinate state as X = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) (§21.1). The first projection forgets the radius,

                                                  Π32 (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑧) = (𝜃, 𝑧),

1670   recording the two-dimensional carrier image — in the reflected chart, the Cayley/Möbius image on
1671   the unit-circle chart (Theorem 65, item (P)). The second forgets the phase,

                                                        Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = 𝑧,

1672   leaving the height alone. The analytic chart then reads the retained height logarithmically,
                                                  log
                                              Π21 (𝜃, 𝑧) = log 𝑧 = 𝑦,

1673   and places it at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 of the strip: the abscissa supplied by the derived weld
1674   axis (§§21.2 and 21.5), the ordinate by the logarithm of the height. That is the whole downward
1675   mechanism. A three-dimensional value becomes a one-dimensional ordinate by having its radius
1676   suppressed, its phase suppressed, and its height passed through log. What is suppressed is booked,
1677   not destroyed: each projection is paired with the loss ledger 𝒟(X) = (𝑟, 𝜃) — in general: radius,
1678   angle, clock offset, adapter state, every coordinate the chosen chart makes invisible.
1679       Upward. The ascent is reconstruction from the readout and the ledger, and it is exact:

                              Rec Π(X), 𝒟(X) = X ,             Reclog 𝑦, (𝑟, 𝜃) = (𝑟, 𝜃, 𝑒 𝑦 ).
                                                                               

1680   A chart ordinate 𝑦 lifts to the carrier height 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 ; the ledger restores the radius and phase; and
1681   the lift lands on the exact state the projection left. This is a bĳection with an explicit two-sided
1682   inverse — record 𝑓 = (height, (radial, phase)) inverts by reconstruct and reconstruct inverts
1683   by record (Lean ConeProjection.record_bijective, reconstruct_record); distinct helix events
1684   write distinct ledger entries (SourceHolonomy.projection_bijective_loss_ledger). Transport
1685   with the ledger is lossless in both directions; transport without the ledger is a compression, and
1686   provably so — dropping the radial channel alone already makes the projection non-injective
1687   (ConeProjection.radial_lost, §23).
1688       The two directions do different work in this part. Downward is reading: the value of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒)
1689   at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 is the final verification of a marked event — the analytic function
1690   is consulted after the event, never used to build it (non-circularity, §20). Upward is locating: a
1691   chart ordinate 𝑦 names the carrier height 𝑒 𝑦 at which the operator reads the bank, and the two
1692   reading-hypotheses of this part are statements about precisely this lift — the 1D-primary branch

                                                              51
1693   of the weak hypothesis is the upward lift 𝛾 = ℑ𝜌 landing on an eigenstate. The classical analytic
1694   function is the downward readout without the ledger — the ledger stays on the carrier. This is why
1695   equality of readouts does not imply equality of states: two states share an ordinate whenever their
1696   heights agree, whatever their radii and phases are doing; the exact criterion is that readout plus
1697   ledger determines the state (Corollary 4).
1698       Both decisions of §20 take their teeth from this mechanism. The 1D ordinate is the logged trace
1699   of the 3D event; the eigenstate carries the coordinates the ordinate dropped. Whether an eigenvalue
1700   must be that trace or coincide with it (decision one), and whether the event or its trace is “the zero”
1701   (decision two), are questions about the two ends of the maps displayed above. Figure 2 draws the
1702   entire pipeline for 𝜒3 : the conjugate pair up to its first crossing, and the ledgered descent to the
1703   chart — with the midline surviving every stage.

1704   21.5   Midpoint provenance: geometry first, chart second
1705   The order of construction matters here. The carrier is not introduced as the vertical line Re 𝑠 = 12 .
1706   Before there is an 𝑠-plane, a zero 𝜌, or a definition of carrierPoint, the wound integer line has a
1707   cylindrical radius 𝑟𝑛 . The arclength calculation gives

                                       𝑟𝑛2
                                                                           r
                                              𝑟Δ                  𝑟𝑛           𝑟Δ
                                           −→    > 0,             √ −→            >0
                                       𝑛       𝜋                   𝑛            𝜋
1708   (windIntegerSite_radius_sq_tendsto and carrierRadius_div_sqrt_tendsto). Thus the expo-
1709   nent 𝜎 of a fiber amplitude 𝑛 −𝜎 is initially free. Define geometric admissibility by the existence of a
1710   finite positive scale limit,
                                 ScaleBalanced(𝜎)      :⇐⇒        ∃𝐿 > 0,      𝑛 −𝜎 𝑟𝑛 −→ 𝐿.
1711   The area law then proves
                                                                          1
                                         ScaleBalanced(𝜎)          ⇐⇒       𝜎=
