1712   This is sigma_half_is_scale_critical, re-exported as scaleBalanced_iff. The gauge parame-
1713   ters 𝑟 and Δ change the positive limiting constant, but not the exponent. Consequently the midpoint
1714   is an output of the three-dimensional arclength geometry: it is the exponent of the square-root
1715   radius, not a coordinate selected from the analytic zero set.
1716       There is an independent no-drift form of the same conclusion. A raw source mode has a complex
1717   transport rate 𝜆 and nonzero amplitude 𝑎, with conservation law

                                               𝑒 (Re 𝜆)𝜏 𝑎 = 𝑎      (𝜏 ∈ R).
1718   Taking 𝜏 = 1 forces Re 𝜆 = 0 (source_noDrift and SourceMode.noDrift). This statement contains
1719   no 𝜌, no 𝑠, and no numerical midpoint. In the radial normalization supplied by (MP1), a putative
1720   abscissa 𝜎 has residual drift 𝑛 𝜎−𝜎∗ , where 𝜎∗ is the unique scale-balanced exponent. Hence
                                                                                          1

1721   the compiled specialization being Helix.no_radial_drift_iff_half. Thus the two inputs agree:
1722   the area law determines the centre 𝜎∗ , and conservation prohibits motion away from it.
1723       Only after (MP1)–(MP2) is the spectral chart attached. The physical height and its internal

object: helix 𝐶+ and conjugate anti-helix 𝐶− , the 𝜋/3-scaled carrier as the yellow layer, the fiber
𝐹𝜒3 in blue growing from the origin with phasors entering at integer heights; the violet dash-dot
line is the weld axis — the midline at unit/2, the fixed locus of 𝐽. At the first crossing the lanes
align in exact focal cancellation, and the conjugate eigenstate pair (Frobenius det = 1) marks the
event at height 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 ≈ 3.10 × 103 . Right panel — the ledgered descent: radius booked in the
loss ledger, Cayley/Möbius to the 2D unit circle, angle booked at the projection to 1D, logarithm

registration bookkeeping between the two scales (§9). The violet thread is the midline surviving
every stage — weld axis in 3D, on-circle landing in 2D (midpoint_entry_on_circle), Re 𝑠 = 12 in
the chart (pipeline_midpoint_iff): the ordinate compresses by a logarithm while the abscissa is
first derived by the area law and then held by no-drift symmetry. The dashed return arrow is the
upward transport: readout plus ledger reconstructs the state exactly (§21.4).




                                                                                         53
1725   Lean stores the ordinate chart and physical-height readout separately:

                                         carrierPoint y := carrierAbscissa + 𝑖 𝑦,
                               carrierPointAtHeight Z := carrierPoint(log 𝑍).

1726   Here carrierAbscissa is selected from the unique witness of CarrierScaleBalanced; only the
1727   theorem carrierAbscissa_eq_half rewrites it to 12 . The theorem carrierPoint_eq_half_add_I is
1728   therefore a downstream normal-form lemma, not the definition of the carrier coordinate. Theorems
1729   carrierPointAtHeight_im and carrierPointAtHeight_exp certify 𝑦 = log 𝑍 and 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 in both
1730   directions.
1731       The completed native crossing is

                    CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍            :⇐⇒     𝑍 > 0 ∧ Dcell 𝜒 𝑍 = 0.

1732   The exact representation theorem gives

                         CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍 ⇐⇒ 𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0.

1733   The finite declaration ThreeDZero remains the truncated ordinate-level focal closure used by the
1734   finite pencil proofs.
1735       Two exclusion theorems make the image statement exact. First, not_scaleBalanced_of_ne says
1736   that an abscissa different from 𝜎∗ is not a native carrier state. Second, helix_no_offline_cancellation
1737   says that an off-circle Cayley ledger entry cannot be produced by a weld-fixed helix event, while
1738   projection_bijective_loss_ledger says that the height-to-ledger map is injective on the carrier
1739   image. Projection can therefore neither move a native cancellation away from the midpoint nor
1740   merge two carrier events into a counterfeit cancellation. An off-midpoint analytic vanishing, if
1741   presented to this 3D representation, has no scale-balanced, drift-free carrier source.
1742       This also separates the exact logical role of ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros. Its clause
1743   𝜌 = carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) is the coverage/identification assertion that a classical analytic zero
1744   belongs to the carrier image. It is not the derivation of that image’s real coordinate: (MP1)–(MP2)
1745   and the exclusion theorems have already done that without quantifying over analytic zeros. Once
1746   coverage is granted, taking real parts is of course immediate; the substantive interface question is
1747   whether every analytic zero is represented by a native focal event. The paper will use carrierPoint
1748   only in this downstream, normal-form sense. Lean makes the separation executable by defining the
1749   midpoint-free statement NativeCarrierCoverage and proving

              ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros(𝜒) ↔ GRH(𝜒) ∧ NativeCarrierCoverage(𝜒).

1750   Consequently the legacy equality premise is not cited as evidence for the coverage direction; an
1751   unconditional closure must discharge the midpoint-free coverage proposition (or the fixed-operator
1752   spectral-capture interface) directly.

1753   21.6   The chart: 𝑦 = log 𝑍 and 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦
1754   The readout just constructed does not live at the carrier’s scale. The identity between the scales is one
1755   equation read in both directions: downward, the chart ordinate is the logarithm of the carrier height,
1756   𝑦 = log 𝑍; upward, the carrier height is the exponential of the chart ordinate, 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 . A carrier
1757   state at height 𝑍 > 0 is read at the represented point 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 (HarmonicPencilCell.reprPoint); the
1758   phasor of the integer 𝑛, born at height 𝑛, is charted at ordinate log 𝑛. The compression this induces
1759   is the single most important fact about the relation between the two representations. At the first

                                                          54
1760   zero of 𝜁, the chart reads 𝑦 = 14.1347 . . .; the carrier height is 𝑍 = 𝑒 𝑦 ≈ 1.38 × 106 , and the realized
1761   bank below that height already holds about 1.38 million integer phasors per lane. In general the
1762   chart ordinate 𝑦 summarizes a bank of ⌊𝑒 𝑦 ⌋ phasors in one complex number. The 1D representation
1763   is not a smaller copy of the 3D representation; it is a logarithmically compressed summary of the
1764   same function, and the scale mismatch between the two charts is itself a theorem-level object (§9).
1765       The abscissa tells the same story from the other side. The carrier’s arclength law first derives
1766   the unique scale-balanced exponent 𝜎∗ = 12 , and conservation then fixes every native mode at zero
1767   radial drift (§21.5). Riemann’s substitution 𝑠 = 12 + 𝑡𝑖 is the analytic chart of that derived weld axis,
1768   and the represented point 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 𝑦 = 12 + 𝑖 𝑦 simply reads height along it. The ordinate compresses
1769   by a logarithm while the abscissa is pinned by a geometric scale law and its no-drift conservation —
1770   which is why every subsequent argument in this part is an argument about heights. The midline
1771   has already been located before the chart is defined.

1772   21.7   Vanishing is focal alignment
1773   A zero, on the carrier, is not a value creeping down to nothing; it is an alignment event. At
1774   a marked height the accumulated bank achieves exact harmonic cancellation: the P and M
1775   lanes balance, the 𝜇6 cells close in Z[𝜁 6 ], and the residual carries no independent constant
1776   mode — the normalized cell residual factors as det(𝐿c )/𝐴 = (𝜆 − 𝜇)𝐵 with 𝜆 − 𝜇 ≠ 0, so the
1777   residual vanishes exactly when the signed closure channel does (Theorem 16). The event is
1778   registered by rank at both exact levels. At physical helix height 𝑍 > 0, with logarithmic ordinate
1779   𝑦 = log 𝑍, the canonical finite bank closes exactly iff its spatially lifted harmonic Gram matrix
1780   drops rank (threeDZeroAtHeight_twoGram3D_rankDrop). This finite event is the truncated detector
1781   ThreeDZeroAtHeight. The completed fibre event is CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight; Lean proves

                       CompletedThreeDZeroAtHeight 𝜒 𝑍            ⇐⇒      𝐿(𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍, 𝜒) = 0

1782   by completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero. The theorem

                           completedHarmonicGram3DAtHeight_rankDrop_iff_L_zero

1783   proves directly that its completed spatial harmonic Gram lift drops rank exactly at that represented
1784   𝐿-zero. Thus the 3D crossing is focal cancellation in the completed 𝐿-function fibre at physical
1785   height 𝑍; it is not inferred from a 1D chart criterion. The finite bank theorem is retained as its
1786   internal truncation-level detector and is not substituted for the completed identity.
1787   Note (Frobenius determinant one). The conjugate eigenstate pair the alignment realizes is not free to
1788   sit anywhere; it is pinned by an algebraic constraint. On the carrier the local Frobenius acts as a simil-
1789   itude of determinant one: its chiral block has det = 1 (RequestProject/FrobeniusSimilitude.lean,
1790   frobeniusBlock_det_one), so its two eigenvalues multiply to one — a reciprocal pair {𝛼, 𝛼−1 }.
1791   With the class unitary they lie on the unit circle as a conjugate pair {𝑒 𝑖𝜃 , 𝑒 −𝑖𝜃 }, and the eigenphases
1792   ±𝜃 are real: the algebraic reason the eigenstate pair is symmetric about the weld axis rather
1793   than drifting off it. This is the carrier’s realization of the classical unit-circle normalization of the
1794   Satake–Frobenius class; on the analytic side it is Deligne’s purity, which places the normalized
1795   Frobenius eigenvalues on the unit circle [13], with the trivial similitude factor det = 1 keeping
1796   them a conjugate pair. The one setting where this mechanism is already a completed theorem is
1797   the function-field analog: Weil’s Riemann hypothesis for curves over a finite field F𝑞 is precisely
1798   the statement that the Frobenius eigenvalues on the Jacobian have absolute value 𝑞 1/2 and pair
1799   as {𝛼, 𝑞/𝛼}, which after normalization sit as conjugate pairs {𝛽, 𝛽−1 } of determinant one on the


                                                           55
1800   unit circle — forcing the zeros of the congruence zeta function onto Re 𝑠 = 12 [12]; Deligne’s
1801   proof of the Weil conjectures extends this purity to smooth projective varieties of every dimension
1802   [13]. There the Frobenius is the operator whose spectrum pins the zeros to the critical line, and
1803   determinant-one unitarity is the entire content of that conclusion — the carrier’s det = 1 block is
1804   the local, archimedean shadow of the same mechanism. We claim the analog, not the classical case:
1805   the finite-field statement is an unconditional theorem, the classical one is not, and importing the
1806   former as a proof of the latter is exactly the elision this part refuses. The determinant-one fact is a
1807   structural property of the representation, proven on the carrier; it does not by itself adjudicate the
1808   naming decisions of §20 — it fixes where the paired eigenphases live, not which of (Z-3D)/(Z-1D)
1809   names the zero.

1810   21.8   The two Gram operators
1811   Two operators read the bank, and they divide the labor.                        𝐴 𝐵 
1812        The Gram harmonic pencil is the finite detector: the 2 × 2 pencil 𝐿c = 𝜇𝐴     𝜆𝐵 on the signed
1813   channels, whose determinant vanishes — whose rank drops — exactly at the alignment events
1814   (§21.7). It is the instrument that marks native focal-event heights on the carrier.
1815        The local von Neumann fibre is the coordinate-reading object. At each physical 3D height 𝑍 > 0,
1816   its spectral parameter is the logarithmic ordinate 𝛾 = 𝑦 = log 𝑍, and it is multiplication by log 𝑍 on
1817   the one-dimensional fibre,

                                      vonNeumannOp(log 𝑍) = (log 𝑍 : C) · id,

1818   symmetric — hence self-adjoint, with real spectrum {log 𝑍} — as a theorem, not an assumption
1819   (vonNeumannOp_isSymmetric, RequestProject/ClosedForm.lean). The spectral parametrization
1820   sends a real eigenvalue 𝜇 to the represented point 𝜎∗ + 𝑖𝜇 = 12 + 𝑖𝜇, where 𝜎∗ has already been fixed
1821   by (MP1).
1822       Because a separate scalar operator is supplied for each 𝛾, this family is not itself the one fixed
1823   operator required by the global Hilbert–Pólya interface. Its exact role is to verify the local kernel
1824   and the reality of an already supplied height.
1825       The family is assembled, without changing any local proof, by the fixed completed-event
                  (3)
1826   operator 𝐴 𝜒 above. Its basis is indexed by completed 3D crossings 𝑒 = (𝑍 𝑒 , ℎ 𝑒 ), not by all real
                        (3)
1827   numbers, and 𝐴 𝜒 𝛿 𝑒 = (log 𝑍 𝑒 )𝛿 𝑒 . Hence a “3D eigenvector” in the resolvent statements below
1828   means this explicit basis state of the single operator, while vonNeumannOp(log 𝑍 𝑒 ) computes its local
1829   one-dimensional resolvent factor.
1830       The internal 3D chain runs entirely on these two instruments, and every link is unconditionally
1831   proven. Finite focal cancellation at ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍 is detected by the finite harmonic Gram
1832   rank drop. Completed focal cancellation at physical height 𝑍 is exactly the analytic 𝐿-zero of
1833   that fibre and is detected by the completed harmonic Gram rank drop. The spatial statement
1834   completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_twoGram3D_rankDrop supplies both the completed harmonic rank
1835   drop and the von Neumann rank drop at the same ordinate log 𝑍. The carrier point 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍 =
       1                                                                                 1
1836
       2 + 𝑖 log 𝑍 lies on the midline because the area law has already proved 𝜎∗ = 2 , while von Neumann
1837   reality supplies the real spectral ordinate and hence zero source drift (§21.5). The one-line Lean proof
1838   simp [carrierPoint] in threeDZero_on_midline is now backed by carrierAbscissa_eq_half
1839   and is a normal-form check, not the provenance of the half. Thus focal cancellation = 3D zero →
1840   harmonic Gram rank drop plus von Neumann Gram rank drop at 𝑦 = log 𝑍: that is the detecting
1841   and realizing instrument of this part, and no step consults the chart.

1856   21.9    The chart-side registration audit
1857   One further object appears in the evidence dossiers and deserves an exact label. Over a finite
1858   window (0, 𝑇], the Lean development builds a diagonal matrix on the window’s zero-events —
1859   hpOperator 𝑇, one axis per unit of multiplicity, eigenvalue the event ordinate. Its name is historical;
1860   its role is not spectral detection. It is a finite repackaging of the already-located analytic zero window, used
1861   for exactly one thing: auditing the chart against the carrier, count and multiplicity. The audit facts
1862   are proven and exact — the diagonal is Hermitian by type (hpOperator_isHermitian); every index
1863   is an exact vanishing (eigenheight_is_exact_vanishing); the chart reads zero at a height iff an
1864   index sits there (chartZero_iff_eigenheight); the diagonal’s dimension is the chart’s own count
1865   formula 1 + 𝜃(𝑇)/𝜋 + 𝑆mult (𝑇) (hpDimension_eq_registration); the eigenspace dimension at an
1866   event equals the vanishing order — the mode space is a graded local algebra C[𝑋]/((𝑋 − line 𝛾)ord )
1867   (finrank_modeSpace), a double zero a two-dimensional crossing; and the window traces are hon-
1868   est analytic objects (gradedResolventTrace_eq_residue_sum, windowedDiffResolvent_tendsto).
1869   But because the window is indexed by already-located analytic zeros, nothing in this subsection
1870   participates in locating an event. The local von Neumann fibre of §21.8 likewise verifies an event
1871   after its height is supplied. The fixed global operator interface is stated separately below.

1872   21.10    The Hilbert–Pólya setup we use
1873   The classical suggestion runs: exhibit a self-adjoint operator whose spectrum gives the ordinates
1874   of the nontrivial zeros; self-adjointness forces the spectrum real; real ordinates place the zeros on

                                                                   57
1875   the midline. It is worth saying plainly that this is not an exotic reformulation: Riemann’s own
1876   sentence — alle Wurzeln reell — already asks for a real spectrum, and real spectrum is precisely
1877   what self-adjointness delivers. The Hilbert–Pólya suggestion is Riemann’s phrasing transposed into
1878   operator language, which is why we treat it as the natural frame for the worked example rather
1879   than as one strategy among many.
1880       The present development has three operator levels, and they must be kept separate. The proved
1881   scalar fibre vonNeumannOp(𝛾) = 𝛾 idC is a local detector attached after a real height 𝛾 is supplied. Its
1882   symmetry and kernel equation certify the coordinate of that already marked event; they do not by
                                                                                           (3)
1883   themselves provide one operator whose spectrum is the event set. The fixed 𝐴 𝜒 supplies the next
1884   level: one symmetric operator on all completed 3D crossing states of 𝜒, with explicit eigenvectors and
1885   the two resolvent traces above. Because its index is the completed-event subtype, it is a valid spectral
1886   realization of the 3D event ontology, not a discovery theorem for analytic zeros not yet coupled to
1887   that ontology. The final analytic-coverage interface is grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture:
1888   one fixed self-adjoint element 𝑎 must be accompanied by a resolvent-trace identification proving
1889   that every analytic pole parameter lies in spectrum(𝑎). Self-adjointness then supplies spectral reality.
                                                                                       (3)
1890   The carrier and chart theorems below now provide the concrete candidate 𝐴 𝜒 and its event traces;
1891   applying the final interface to every analytic zero still requires the coverage/trace identification
1892   rather than only the diagonal assembly.


1893   22    The theorems
1894   The formal home of this part is RequestProject/HelixResolventCapture.lean together with the
1895   supporting files named below; every statement carries axiom footprint {propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound},
1896   no sorry, no axiom, built in-tree (App. B). Below, GRH(𝜒) abbreviates the formal statement “every
1897   nontrivial zero of 𝐿(𝑠, 𝜒) lies on the midline” (GRHSpectral.GRH), stated for every modulus 𝑁 and
1898   every Dirichlet character 𝜒 mod 𝑁. The reading-hypotheses and both GRH implications are proven
1899   at that generality. The trivial character is the instantiation that lands Mathlib’s RiemannHypothesis
1900   — the mod-1 𝐿-function is riemannZeta — and a reading adopted at every modulus yields
1901   GRHSpectral.GRHComplete, the conjecture itself: every Dirichlet 𝐿-function, every modulus, every
1902   character, principal included.
1903   Midpoint provenance and exclusion — proven before any zero-set coverage hypothesis:
1904   • windIntegerSite_radius_sq_tendsto
         √                                           and carrierScaleBalanced_iff: arclength forces 𝑟𝑛 ≍
1905       𝑛, and 𝑛 −𝜎 𝑟𝑛 has a positive finite limit exactly at 𝜎 = 21 .
1906   • carrierAbscissa_scaleBalanced, carrierAbscissa_eq_half, and carrierPoint_eq_half_add_I:
1907     the carrier point is constructed from the unique scale-balanced abscissa and only afterward
1908     rewritten in its half-unit normal form. The physical-height readout is separately defined
1909     as carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = carrierPoint(log 𝑍), and carrierPointAtHeight_exp proves
1910     the exact conversion between physical height and ordinate.
1911   • source_noDrift, SourceMode.noDrift, and Helix.no_radial_drift_iff_half: norm conser-
1912     vation first gives Re 𝜆 = 0 without mentioning a zero or midpoint; after the area-law normalization,
1913     zero radial drift is equivalent to 𝜎 = 𝜎∗ = 21 .
1914   • ThreeDZero = focalClosure and focalClosure_iff_rankDrop: finite 3D vanishing is defined
1915     and detected without carrierPoint. At the completed-fibre level, completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero
1916     identifies focal cancellation at 𝑍 exactly with 𝐿(carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍), 𝜒) = 0.

1919     is not weld-fixed; and no complex point with a different real coordinate is the image of any

1923   The reduction spine — proven, unconditional:
1924   • RH_of_GRH_Trivial_Char: GRH(𝜒1 ) =⇒ Mathlib’s RiemannHypothesis. The hypothesis
1925     handles the strip; Mathlib supplies no-zeros on Re 𝑠 ≥ 1 and the negative-real trivial zeros via
1926     the completed functional equation. The entire target is one character’s GRH.
1927   • focalClosure_iff_rankDrop: exact native finite focal cancellation is equivalent to harmonic
1928     Gram rank drop. This internal finite-carrier theorem contains no analytic zero set.
1929   • completedThreeDZeroAtHeight_iff_L_zero: the completed 3D fibre crosses at physical height
1930     𝑍 > 0 exactly when 𝐿 vanishes at carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍. This packages
1931     focal_residual_zero_iff_L_zero together with reprPoint_eq_carrierPointAtHeight. It is
1932     an exact pointwise identity at every represented height; it does not assert that an arbitrary
1933     analytic zero has a representing 𝑍.
1934   • spatialLiftGram_det, spatialLiftGram_rankDrop_iff, and completedHarmonicGram3DAtHeight
1935     _rankDrop_iff_L_zero: the completed harmonic 3D Gram operator rank-drops exactly at the

1937     that the harmonic and von Neumann operators act on the three spatial carrier coordinates as
1938     𝐺 ⊗ 𝐼3 ; their determinants are (det 𝐺)3 , so the lift preserves and reflects rank drop and cannot
1939     manufacture an extra cancellation.
1940   • vonNeumannOp_isSymmetric: symmetry of the local scalar fibre operator is a theorem; it supplies
1941     coordinate reality after an event has been coupled to that fibre.
1942   • threeDCrossings_iff_grh_and_nativeCarrierCoverage: the legacy identity premise is exactly

1952   • grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture: the global operator route. It uses one fixed self-
1953     adjoint operator and a trace/capture premise placing every analytic pole parameter in its
1954     spectrum.

1964     are the audit theorems listed above.

1965   The two legacy interfaces, rendered formal. The formal system speaks the classical frame: its
1966   “nontrivial zero” is definitionally the analytic object. The revised source records the minimal
1967   dependency of each older interface:
1968   • ThreeD_crossings_are_real_zeros (3D-Zero-Real; the strong reading with the 3D zero pri-
1969     mary): every nontrivial zero 𝜌 is represented by a completed fibre crossing at a physical 3D height
1970     𝑍 > 0, with 𝜌 = carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = 𝜎∗ + 𝑖 log 𝑍. The two spatially lifted Gram pencils
1971     then provide their rank drops at ordinate log 𝑍. Here 12 + 𝑖 log 𝑍 is the proved normal form of the
1972     carrier image, not a fresh geometric assumption. Nevertheless, the equality already includes the
1973     critical-line conclusion. The theorem threeDCrossings_iff_grh_and_nativeCarrierCoverage
1974     exposes its exact content; the midpoint-free coverage component is now available as the separate
1975     target NativeCarrierCoverage.
1976   • OneD_zeta_zero_correlated (1D-Zero-Exclusive-Real; the weak reading): a per-zero dis-
1977     junction. Its right branch is only the analytic zero equation together with 𝛾 = ℑ𝜌, so
1978     oneD_zeta_zero_correlated_proved inhabits it unconditionally. The actual pointwise cou-
1979     pling is OneDCorrelationEvidence, which asserts a scalar-fibre kernel at that analytic zero and
1980     therefore implies the critical-line conclusion by itself.
1981   These audits do not alter either conditional theorem. They state which premise actually supplies the
1982   conclusion and prevent the geometric midpoint theorems, the internal rank-drop correspondence,
1983   and the analytic zero-set identification from being presented as one result.
1984       The coordinate convention in both interfaces is fixed: 𝑍 > 0 is physical height on the Archimedean
1985   helix, 𝑦 = log 𝑍 is the analytic ordinate, and 𝑆(𝑡) is the global carrier-to-chart coordinate/registration
1986   map. The pointwise fibre readout and the global census map therefore have distinct typed roles.


1987   23    Evidence I: the 3D–1D correlation
1988   The eighteen facts of oneDChartEvidence, each proven unconditionally, form a chart-side registra-
1989   tion dossier. They establish count, jump, residue, multiplicity, and projection identities on the objects
1990   appearing in their statements. The universal layer is the 𝑆(𝑡) global coordinate map: it transports the
1991   carrier-scale census to the unit-chart census and registers every analytic event jump. A global census
1992   identity is not by itself a pointwise bĳection between ThreeDZero and arbitrary Dirichlet 𝐿-zeros.
1993   The separate, character-indexed input OneDCorrelationEvidence(𝜒) is the operative pointwise
1994   chart-to-kernel leg. Three of the facts below are named engines: Shannon — the collapse loses
1995   radius and angle to the ledger but never counterfeits (record_bijective); the Shannon Cascade —
1996   an accumulation of stage features is a feature of the limit (limit_zero_of_stage_accumulation);
1997   and Riemann’s Fold — the projection pipeline, crossing dimensions, lands on the real axis exactly
1998   when its retained coordinate does (pipeline_midpoint_iff).
1999   • chartZero_iff_eigenheight (RequestProject/HilbertPolya.lean). For 0 < 𝛾 ≤ 𝑇: 𝜁( 12 +
2000     𝑖𝛾) = 0 ⇐⇒ 𝛾 is an index of the zero-window diagonal (chart-side audit, §21.9). The one-for-one
2001     coincidence, proven — not asserted — window by window.
2002   • hpDimension_eq_registration (RequestProject/HilbertPolya.lean). The window diago-
2003     nal’s dimension is the chart’s own count formula, 1 + 𝜃(𝑇)/𝜋 + 𝑆mult (𝑇). The index count and the
2004     zero count are the same number because the ledger says so.
2005   • carrier_scale_compensation_S (RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean). 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 )−
2006     𝑁1 (𝑒 𝑡 ) = 𝑆(𝑡): the classical 𝑆(𝑡) is the gap between the native-scale event count and the unit-scale


                                                          60
2007     smooth term — one procession, two registrations, no mysterious remainder.
2008   • native_identification′ (RequestProject/CarrierScaleCompensation.lean). 𝑁𝜋/3 (𝑒 𝑡 ) equals
2009     the number of on-line zero ordinates in (0, 𝑡] — one zero per completed 𝜋/3 cell.

2127   and conservative transport have proved that the native, scale-balanced carrier image is exactly

2133   and von Neumann rank drops at the same ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The fibre operator is self-adjoint

2136   at the eigenheights, multiplicity equal to order, no split focus, definite metric, exhaustion of the

2193   28     Conclusion
2194   The corrected dependency structure has three levels. First, Archimedean helix geometry de-
2195   rives the unique scale-balanced, drift-free carrier abscissa; Lean constructs carrierPoint from
2196   that abscissa, proves its half-unit normal form afterward, and reads physical height through
2197   carrierPointAtHeight(𝑍) = carrierPoint(log 𝑍). Second, the finite harmonic pencil detects
2198   truncated focal cancellation exactly, the completed harmonic pencil detects the completed 𝐿-fibre
                                                                                                           (3)
2199   cancellation, and the local scalar fibre verifies its ordinate 𝑦 = log 𝑍. The fixed operator 𝐴 𝜒
2200   then assembles all completed crossings into one symmetric event-state space with explicit basis
2201   eigenvectors. Third, identifying the analytic zero set with those native events requires a pointwise
2202   coverage or spectral-capture theorem.
2203       The global 𝑆(𝑡) coordinate map supplies exact census, jump, residue, and multiplicity registration
2204   between carrier and chart scales. The proved supporting facts include the two explicit completed-
2205   event resolvent versions: 3D zeros with 3D eigenvectors, and 1D zero readouts with the same
2206   3D zeros and 3D eigenvectors. The legacy identity conditional and correlation conditional also
2207   remain valid deductions, with their proofs retained above; the new Lean audit states exactly which
2208   premise contains the critical-line conclusion in each route. An analytic Hilbert–Pólya completion
                                   (3)
2209   can now target the fixed 𝐴 𝜒 : it must prove the analytic resolvent/spectral capture required by
2210   grh_of_selfAdjoint_resolvent_capture, or instantiate that interface with another fixed operator.
                                                                                                    (3)
2211   The scalar family 𝛾 idC is correctly used as the local diagonal-mode calculator, while 𝐴 𝜒 is the
2212   assembled 3D event-space operator.

2213   Part IV
2214   Beyond Endoscopy - Altuğ Analysis and Repair
2215   29    The obstruction: Altuğ’s uniformity problem
2216   The framework began not as an alternative to functoriality but as a root-cause analysis of one failure:
2217   the loss of productivity in the direct Beyond-Endoscopy route [1] above the symmetric square.
2218   The obstruction turned out to be an emergent clock; once that clock is separated the higher-order
2219   analysis becomes compositional, and the transport interface the rest of the paper builds is extracted
2220   from the structure that composition consumes.
2221       Altuğ’s execution of Beyond Endoscopy for GL(2) [2, 3, 4] reduces the standard-representation
2222   trace to an archimedean analysis whose primary difficulty is a uniformity problem: the asymptotic
2223   expansions of the Fourier transforms of the orbital integrals must hold with implied constants
2224   independent of every parameter — the 𝐶, 𝐷-independence Altuğ calls “the central issue,” the
2225   content of his long technical appendix (Altuğ II, Appendix A), which secures the power saving
                                31/32+𝜀 ) isolating the standard representation (Altuğ III, Thm 1.1). A second
          𝑛<𝑋 tr 𝑇𝑘 (𝑛) = 𝑂(𝑋
       Í
2226

2227   difficulty sits beyond it: Poisson summation on the 𝑛-sum “works well for the standard represen-
2228   tation and the symmetric square, however stops being productive for higher symmetric powers”
2229   (Altuğ III, fn. 5, after Sarnak [7]; the two productive cases are Venkatesh’s [5]). To our knowledge no
2230   one had instrumented these sums numerically; the field’s own diagnosis is that the direct analysis
2231   “does not scale to higher rank.” Our first reading mis-located the difficulty at the cutoff’s edges — it
2232   is not there.
2233   The estimate that costs Altuğ roughly sixty pages reduces, in the exact gauge, to a single magnitude
2234   bound. The transform (6) whose 𝐶, 𝐷-uniformity is Altuğ’s “central issue” is bounded, with no
2235   oscillation estimate, by the triangle inequality in the coordinate that makes the integrand real
2236   (Lemma 81); the sharp expansion (Theorem 82) and the full uniform bound (Proposition 84) then
2237   follow, every uniform constant being one application of that one bound. The analysis is deferred to
2238   Appendix A; here we turn to what made it look hard.


2239   30    The oscillation is the orbital transform’s own comb
2240   Why did Prop. 84 look hard? The oscillation the estimate must survive is deterministic. The
2241   numerical scan is made in the clock coordinate

                                𝜈clock := 2𝜈𝐽 ,       𝑒(−𝑦𝜈𝐽 /2𝑙 𝑓 2 ) = 𝑒(−𝑦𝜈clock /4𝑙 𝑓 2 ),

2242   where 𝜈𝐽 is the transform frequency in Prop. 84. The measured clock is extracted from the full
2243   complex profile 𝑉(𝜈clock ) by fitting the log-power modulation log |𝑉(𝜈clock )| 2 to a smooth envelope
2244   plus the first two harmonics sharing one fundamental, not by averaging dip gaps. Over the cutoff
2245   support 𝑦 ∈ [ 𝑋4 , 5𝑋
                           4 ] this gives

                           Δ𝜈clock = 0.524 (𝑙 𝑓 2 )1.03 (𝑋/8)−1.04 (1 + 𝜉)0.00 ,      𝑅2 = 1.000,

2246   equivalently half that spacing in the 𝜈𝐽 coordinate. In the one-parameter window-span normalization
2247   𝜅eff := 4𝑙 𝑓 2 /(𝑋Δ𝜈clock ) the cells give 𝜅eff = 0.943 ± 0.025 (range 0.895–0.971), while the harmonic-
2248   truncation audit has median period shift 2.4 × 10−4 , so the residual spread is not a dip-localization
2249   artifact. With the same Chebyshev multiplier 𝑈𝑟 (𝑥) used for the symmetric-power rank, the

                                                              66
2250   event-bearing 𝜉 ≠ 0 cells keep the same law through the tested range 0 ≤ 𝑟 ≤ 13 after separating
2251   the continuous clock from deep-event visibility: every rank has 𝑅 2 = 1.000, 𝑙 𝑓 2 -exponent 1.03–1.04,
2252   and 𝑋-exponent −1.04–−1.03 on the cells passing the clock-quality gate. Thus the older scalar
2253   𝜅 ≈ 0.94 is the mean of a slightly drifting clock, and the observed high-rank loss is productivity
2254   decay: deep-event cells thin from 10/12 at 𝑟 = 0 to 3/9 and 3/8 at 𝑟 = 11, 12, while the surviving
2255   clock cells still obey the same law. Thus the scalable object is not the raw list of deep dips but the
2256   cell-indexed phase clock together with a separate productivity ledger: the clock law survives in
2257   cells where the visible deep comb has already thinned, so higher rank must be tested by clock-cell
2258   census and productive cell yield as distinct observables.
2259        This oscillation is intrinsic to the orbital transform Ψ = 𝐼 𝑙, 𝑓 (𝜉, 𝑦), not the cutoff’s edges. Two
2260   controls settle it: replacing the compact cutoff 𝐺(𝑦/𝑋) by a smooth edgeless window leaves the
2261   comb unchanged, and tapering the 𝑥 = ±1 endpoints of the 𝑥-integral leaves it unchanged as well
2262   (height_warp_test.py) — so neither the height-cutoff edges nor the integral endpoints produce it.
2263   It is the 𝜉-Fourier oscillation of the orbital content: at 𝜉 = 0 the 𝑥-integrand is unimodal (𝑃2 /𝑃1 = 0)
2264   with no comb, while 𝜉 ≠ 0 switches on the transform’s own oscillation, the window fixing only its
2265   𝜈-spacing (Δ𝜈 ∝ 1/𝑋). It is therefore a deterministic feature of the content, not a removable chart
2266   artifact of the cutoff; but it is deterministic, which is exactly what the exact gauge of §A discharges —
2267   the magnitude bound survives it whatever its source, with no estimate of it.
2268        The clock is necessary but not sufficient: the repair is the clock configurator plus two adapters. Identifying
2269   the transport frequency is the first ingredient, not the fix — the clock alone does not close the
2270   crossings. Exact closure of the carrier readout, across the symmetric-power ladder and up the
2271   GL tower, is the clock configurator — which reads the deterministic transport frequency and sets
2272   the period, phase, and scale the rest inherit — together with two carrier adapters it keys. The
2273   carrier dwell re-registers the values a projected sum skips — the native, exact form of Altuğ’s Σ()
2274   missing-lattice-point correction — and closes the crossing exactly where the skip displaces it. The
2275   phasor delay adapter, derived from the clock, retards the faster-spinning higher-weight channels so
2276   the crossing sharpens rather than smears, restoring the reopening exponent toward its simple-zero
2277   value. The clock configurator supplies the period; these two supply registration and spin. The
2278   repair is the clock configurator + carrier dwell + phasor delay, not the clock alone; the suite is
2279   catalogued as an operational unit in §40.


2280   31     The repair: a lossless method that scales
2281   The method the rest of the paper builds — a clock, then carrier scaling, a frozen warp, and ledgered
2282   projection — has a clean, precision-testable form on the carrier’s own bank, the object of the cell-closure
2283   algebra of §38 (CellClosure). We report that worked example here: on the bank, the four operations
2284   drive the native cell residual to a precision-limited zero, uniformly across the symmetric-power rank
2285   census, the residual tracking working precision — an identity, not a model floor.
            Scope (read this first). This experiment is run on the carrier bank 𝐵𝑟 (𝑘) = 𝑗 𝑒 𝑖(𝑟−2𝑗)𝜃𝑘 with the

2315   The cuspidal +warp residual is ∼ 10−29 , 10−48 , 10−79 at 30, 50, 80 digits: it tracks precision, where a
2316   model floor would be digit-independent. Every ablation floors — the scalar readout (raw/clock),
2317   scaling without the warp, and the no-projection scalar warp all plateau at 𝑂(1)–𝑂(100) — so both
2318   the projection and the warp are load-bearing.
2319       What it is, and is not. The harmonic fiber (𝜃 a rational multiple of 𝜋) is already root-of-unity and
2320   closes at every stage except the scalar clock column, where collapsing to a single dominant frequency
2321   aliases even it to 𝑂(30); +scale re-closes it (the 10−𝑝 entries). There the DC ledger correctly books
2322   the genuine Sym𝑟 reducibility (three trivial constituents at 𝑟 = 8, 10 for 𝜃 = 𝜋/3) — the same trivial
2323   channels that return as the exceptional cases of Part III. The content is the cuspidal row: the irrational
2324   Satake phase does not close raw (the +scale column floors), but the frozen unit-modulus warp
2325   harmonizes it to the compatible cell, where it closes exactly. This is not a claim that the cuspidal
2326   𝐿-function’s own coefficients sum to zero; it is the exact, lossless, precision-tracking closure of the
2327   harmonized fiber — “the fiber engages its own warp” (§40) made an identity, uniform across rank
2328   because the carrier scale 𝑀 is refined (6 → 12 → 48 → 96) to keep every channel resolved. This
2329   is the shape of the whole paper: Part II builds the machinery this example runs on (the carrier,
2330   the loss ledger, the warp dictionary), and Part III lands the classical functoriality; the reducibility
2331   booked in the ledger here is the same object that becomes the exceptional locus there.
2332       Fixed results: the carrier closes every object to precision; the degradation lives only in the 1D projection.
2333   The repair of §30 is measured. Two readings of the same object must be separated: the carrier (its
2334   vector representation, the four-stage above) and the scalar 𝐿-function readout (the 1D projection). In

2338          The standard-representation channel Altuğ can only bound to 𝑜(𝑋) (magnitude ∼ 0.5) has
2339   signed sum at the machine floor — the odd-clock antisymmetry dual−𝜉 = −dual𝜉 makes the 𝜉 ≠ 0
2340   contribution vanish exactly (dual_closure_test.py). The dwell closes the crossing that skipping
2341   the missing lattice points displaces (a 3400× contrast, the native Σ(), skip_insert_closure.py).
2342   The decisive rows are the last two carrier entries: the genuine two-parameter GL(4) Rankin–Selberg
2343   𝐿(Δ × 𝐸11 ) (two independent Satake angles, built from scratch, not a functorial Sym𝑟 ) degrades in
2344   the scalar readout to 𝑘 = 0.47 — and a scalar de-chirp cannot repair it, a one-parameter correction
2345   against two independent angles — yet its carrier bank closes to 4.9 × 10−91 at 90 digits, an identity
2346   that tracks precision (gl4_rankin.py). The control isolates the mechanism: the self-dual GL(3) row
2347   is Sym2 of a genuine Maass form (the level-one even form 𝑅 = 13.7797, our own Hejhal eigenvalues
2348   𝑎 1 , . . . , 𝑎 20000 , tempered to |𝑎 𝑝 | < 2, the Sato–Tate-open regime — not synthesized from Δ), and
2349   because it carries a single Satake angle its scalar readout stays clean (𝑘 = 1.01, no degradation) while
2350   the vector likewise closes to 4.2 × 10−91 (gl3_maass_selfdual.py). So the wall is parameter count,
2351   not degree: a degree-three one-parameter object reads faithfully in 1D, a degree-four two-parameter
2352   object does not — the scalar readout is a rank-one projection, exact for one independent angle and
2353   lossy for two. Genuine GL therefore has no wall in the carrier: the smearing of the multi-parameter
2354   crossings is a property of the 1D scalar projection, which the channel-resolved vector representation
2355   does not share. By Gelbart–Jacquet a self-dual cuspidal GL(3) is a Sym2 , so it is necessarily one-
2356   parameter; the sharpest test of the carrier is therefore a non-self-dual GL(3), which no Sym2 supplies.
2357   Take the degree-three complex Artin representation 𝜌 of the Frobenius group 𝐹21 = 𝐶7 ⋊ 𝐶3 (7T4),
2358   field 𝑥 7 − 14𝑥 5 + 56𝑥 3 − 56𝑥 + 22; its local Satake bank at an√order-seven Frobenius is the three
2359   roots of unity {𝜁7 , 𝜁27 , 𝜁 47 } (trace the Gauss period 𝜂 = (−1 + −7)/2) or its conjugate {𝜁37 , 𝜁57 , 𝜁 67 }
                                 √
2360   (trace 𝜂′ = (−1 − −7)/2), neither set closed under conjugation, so 𝜌 ; 𝜌∨ . The object is genuinely
2361   non-abelian: 𝑝 = 13 and 𝑝 = 41 are both ≡ 6 (mod 7) yet fall in different classes (𝜂′ vs. 𝜂), so no
2362   congruence recovers the trace (the classes were resolved exactly by the Frobenius substitution in
2363   the degree-21 splitting field). This is precisely where the scalar readout must fail categorically
2364   rather than merely smear: Re 𝜂 = Re 𝜂′ = − 12 , so a real one-dimensional readout — a function of
2365   the trace’s real part — gives the two Frobenius classes the same value and cannot separate 7𝐴 from
2366   7𝐵, erasing the non-abelian bit. The complex multi-rail bank keeps them apart and closes exactly:
2367   over the natural 𝜁7 clock the non-DC rails of both classes sum to machine zero, tracking 4.3 × 10−62
       at 60 digits, with rails = 𝜁1+2+4              = 1 (so SL(3): two independent rails carry the degree-three
                                   Î

2369   bank) and no DC/pole rail present, while the order-three and split fibres carry exactly one and
2370   three DC rails — the constant-mode/pole content, cleanly separated (f21_gl3_multirail.py).

2386   Part V
2387   Universal Transport
2388   33    Toward Universal Transport
2389   The preceding sections close the analytic core — the uniformity (§A), the emergent clock (§30),
2390   and the productivity boundary. The remainder of the paper develops the carrier transport toward
2391   symmetric-power functoriality: the carrier/fiber rescaling that sends a pole to a closed cell (§34),
2392   the arithmetic transparency of the symmetric-power transfer (§35), and a detection identity closed
2393   on a genuine transfer (§36).


2394   34    The carrier/fiber rescaling: a pole becomes a closed cell
2395   Place the integers on a carrier scaled by 𝜋/3, i.e. attach the cell phase 𝑒 𝑖𝑛𝜋/3 (the 𝜇6 /𝜁 6 step).
2396   We distinguish two operations on the carrier throughout. A rescaling is a fixed constant — here
2397   𝜋/3, or another 𝜇𝑚 step — that lifts a unit-1 carrier into one with harmonic cells; it establishes
2398   the native cell structure (and is the reason we never work at unit scale). A warp is a function, a
2399   continuously-evolving deterministic output 𝜔(·) that rides the already-rescaled carrier and adapts
2400   to the fiber — the 𝜔𝑊 (𝑛) of the warped-Abel summation (§37) and the tunable FE clock (§40).
2401   Rescaling sets the cell; warping moves within it. The pole of 𝜁 at 𝑠 = 1 lives in the divergence of
         1/𝑛; on the (rescaled) carrier it closes,
       Í

2406   conductor — the sixth roots of unity of Z[𝜁3 ] = Z[𝜁6 ] — so the 𝜋/3 = 𝜇6 rescaling coincides with

2416   𝑆(𝑡) term is recovered as the scale-registration correction in the scalar receiver chart (§9). This is the
2417   reading used in §36.


2418   35    Symmetric-power transfer: arithmetic transparency
2419   For Sym𝑟 transfer GL(2) → GL(𝑟 + 1) (𝑟 = 2𝑚 even), the transfer sends an elliptic class of Satake
2420   angle 𝜃 to the class of angles {2𝑘𝜃 : |𝑘| ≤ 𝑚} ∪ {0} —i.e. Sym𝑟 of the Frobenius block, with the
2421   fixed eigenvalue 1 = 𝛼𝛽 the det-one of the block. The symmetric-power transfer is arithmetically
2422   transparent, as follows.
2423       Arithmetic transparency. The transferred characteristic polynomial is reducible (𝑥 − 1 divides it),
2424   and each quadratic factor 𝑥 2 − 2 cos(2𝑘𝜃)𝑥 + 1 has discriminant −4 sin2 (2𝑘𝜃). The clock identity
2425   sin(2𝑘𝜃) = sin 𝜃 𝑈2𝑘−1 (cos 𝜃) (with sin2 𝜃 = |𝐷|/4𝑛, 𝐷 = 𝑡 2 − 4𝑛) gives

                                            disc 𝑘   𝑈2𝑘−1 (cos 𝜃)2
                                                   =                ∈ Q×2 ,
                                             𝐷             𝑛
                                                                     √
2426   a rational square—so every factor lies in the same field Q( 𝐷) as the original class, the arithmetic
2427   𝐿-value is identical on both sides, and it cancels in the transfer factor. (Because symmetric powers
2428   transfer to reducible classes, the transparency sidesteps the subtleties of irreducible cubic orders
2429   entirely.)


2430   36    Detection: the self-twist identity closes

2432   holomorphic newform 𝑓 with 𝑎 𝑝 its Frobenius trace and 𝜆(𝑝) = 𝑎 𝑝 /𝑝 (𝑘−1)/2 , the symmetric square
       carries the middle eigenvalue 𝛼𝛽 = 1; the plain census 𝑝 (𝜆(𝑝)2 − 1)(log 𝑝)/𝑝 has mean zero and is

2435   character 𝜒𝐾 of an imaginary quadratic field 𝐾: it has a pole at 𝑠 = 1 iff 𝑓 has complex multiplication
2436   by 𝐾 (dihedral), the classical criterion of Gelbart–Jacquet [6] and Rankin–Selberg. Its pole order is
2437   the transferred count, read as the zero-frequency residue of the logarithmic derivative:

2453   Remark 51 (what this is). The mathematics detected here—that the symmetric-square/self-twist
2454   pole marks CM forms—is classical (Gelbart–Jacquet, Rankin–Selberg). What the section contributes
2455   is the closure of the detection identity through the two mechanisms: the analytic count as a
2456   product-law/log-derivative residue, the geometric count as the self-twist relation, matched on a
2457   genuine transfer.

2458   36.1   A non-abelian instance: which Frobenius data transfers
2459   The self-twist detection of §36 runs on a dihedral (abelian, 𝐶2 ) form, where the Galois image is
2460   small and the arithmetic reduces to a single quadratic character. For a genuinely non-abelian form
2461   the Frobenius datum splits into two independent bits—one a character cannot see—and the transfer
2462   treats them differently. We illustrate this on the exotic tetrahedral (“𝐴4 ”) weight-one newform
2463   ℎ of level 124, whose 𝐿-coefficients are a class function of Frob𝑝 in the binary tetrahedral group
2464   2𝑇 = SL(2, 3), given as follows. Let 𝜄(𝑝) ∈ {0, 1, 2} be the cubic-residue index of 𝑝 modulo 31 (the
2465   odd part of the level 124 = 4 · 31), and set 𝜀(𝑝) = +1, −1, 0 as 𝜄(𝑝) = 1, 2, 0. When 𝜀(𝑝) = 0 (the
2466   2+2-shape primes) 𝑎 𝑝 = 0; otherwise

                          𝑘(𝑝)
                   𝑎 𝑝 = 𝜁 12 ,       𝑘(𝑝) = 21 𝜒 𝑘 (𝑝) + 4𝜀(𝑝) + 0 if (3/𝑝) = +1, else 6        (mod 12),
                                                                                           

2467   where 𝜒 𝑘 (𝑝) = 6 [ 𝑝 . 1 (mod 4) ] + 4 𝜄(𝑝) is the quartic×cubic exponent datum ([·] the Iverson
2468   bracket). Here the exponent carries two independent Galois bits:

       value bit 𝜀(𝑝) ∈ {0, ±1} (the cubic residue, the abelian 𝐴ab
                                                                 4 = 𝐶3 datum),                 sign bit (3/𝑝) (the SL(2, 3) → 𝐴4 central

2470   invisible to any abelian character.
2471       The symmetric square sends 𝑎 𝑝 ↦→ 𝑎 2𝑝 − 𝜒(𝑝), and 𝑎 2𝑝 = 𝜁2𝑘
                                                                      12
                                                                         is unchanged by 𝑘 ↦→ 𝑘 + 6. Hence:


                                                              72
                                                                           Sym2 transfer to GL(3)
2472           sign bit (3/𝑝) (double cover, SL(2, 3))            forgotten (trace invariant
                                                                                          √ under 𝑘 ↔ 𝑘+6)
               value bit 𝜀 (cubic residue, projective 𝐴4 )          retained: 𝜀 = ±1 ⇒ ± 3 𝑖, 𝜀 = 0 ⇒ ±1

2473       So the transfer factors through the projective image 𝐴4 : the value bit passes to the GL(3) Satake
2474   datum, the sign bit is the GL(2)-specific double-cover fiber the transfer collapses. The order trick
2475   —sign from the element order, value from the residue symbol—thus reads exactly which part of the
2476   Frobenius datum transfers, and the split is non-trivial precisely because 𝐴4 is non-abelian (for the
2477   dihedral case of §36 the two bits coincide). This identifies the transferred datum; the automorphy
2478   of the resulting GL(3) object (the three-dimensional standard representation of 𝐴4 ) is the classical
2479   Artin/Langlands–Tunnell case.

2480   36.2   The detected count is a Mordell–Weil rank difference
2481   The transferred object of §36.1 is, up to the nebentype twist, the three-dimensional adjoint
2482   Ad𝑔 = End0 (𝑉𝑔 )  Sym2 𝑉𝑔 ⊗ (det 𝑉𝑔 )−1 of the 𝐴4 form 𝑔. At this exotic locus the zero-frequency
2483   count read on the analytic side coincides with a genuine arithmetic rank, and the coincidence is an
2484   exact identity of group theory.
2485      The quartic field 𝑀 cut out by 𝑔 carries the permutation action of 𝐴4 on four points, whose
2486   character is 𝜒perm = (4, 0, 1, 1) on the classes (𝑒 , (2, 2), (3)𝑎 , (3)𝑏 ). Against the character table,
2487   ⟨𝜒perm , 1⟩ = 1 and ⟨𝜒perm , 𝜒std ⟩ = 1, so

                        𝜒perm = 1 ⊕ Ad𝑔 ,          Ad𝑔 = 𝜒std (the 3-dimensional irreducible).

2488   Functoriality of Mordell–Weil under this decomposition gives 𝐸(𝑀) ⊗ Q = (𝐸(Q) ⊗ Q) ⊕ 𝐸( · )Ad𝑔
2489   and hence the exact Artin/permutation identity

                                         𝑟(𝐸, Ad𝑔 ) = rank 𝐸(𝑀) − rank 𝐸(Q),                                  (1)

2490   proven as group theory (no analytic or 𝑝-adic input). Both sides of (1) are then algebraic: the Artin
2491   multiplicity 𝑟(𝐸, Ad𝑔 ) and a difference of classical Mordell–Weil ranks, the source living “up the
2492   tower” at 𝑀 and traced down to Q. That this algebraic multiplicity also equals the analytic order of
2493   vanishing at 𝑠 = 1 of 𝐿(𝐸, Ad𝑔 , 𝑠) — the zero-frequency residue of the logarithmic derivative, the
2494   statistic §36 reads as the transferred count — is equivariant BSD, conjectural and used nowhere here:
2495   identity (1) and the census below are stated and verified entirely on the algebraic side. Thus the
2496   count is a rank difference: one algebraic statistic, read once through the Artin formalism and once
2497   as a difference of ranks.
2498       On the two Darmon–Lauder–Rotger exotic 𝐴4 curves this is pinned on both sides:
2499

        26𝑏 (𝑦 2 + 𝑥 𝑦 + 𝑦 = 𝑥 3 − 𝑥 2 − 3𝑥 + 3)       0               2                         2
        52𝑏 (𝑦 2 = 𝑥 3 + 𝑥 − 10)                       0               2                         2

2501   with 𝑀 = Q(𝑤), 𝑤 4 + 7𝑤 2 − 2𝑤 + 14 = 0 the tetrahedral field of §36.1, rank-two generators of 𝐸(𝑀)
2502   exhibited by descent. This is the “one mechanism, two locations” statement made theorem-anchored:

2506   Remark 52 (tiering). The rank identity (1) is proven (Artin formalism). The automorphy of Ad𝑔
2507   on GL(3)—which makes 𝐿(𝐸, Ad𝑔 , 𝑠) an honest automorphic 𝐿-function so that its pole order is a
2508   spectral quantity—is the classical Langlands–Tunnell case for 𝐴4 . The 𝑝-adic regulator side (the
2509   explicit point coordinates realizing the rank) is the Darmon–Lauder–Rotger Elliptic Stark conjecture,
2510   verified to 20 digits on 26𝑏/52𝑏 but with the points found by descent first; we use only the proven
2511   rank identity and the classical automorphy here.


2512   37    A candidate automorphic object from the primary construct
2513   The transfer of §§35–36.2 requires an automorphic representation on GL(𝑟 + 1) whose existence
2514   realizes the functorial lift. In the primary (three-dimensional) representation we exhibit a concrete
2515   candidate object for it: the carrier — a double-sided helix of Frobenius similitudes — carrying a fiber
2516   (the phasor readout), together with its warp (the twist family of §35). The classical 𝐿-function is the
2517   shadow of this candidate under the projection that sends the exponential state space 𝑒 𝑦 down by a
2518   Möbius/Cayley map and then log to the ordinate, at the midpoint and without drift. What makes
2519   it a candidate is that the three properties a converse theorem asks of an 𝐿-function — functional
2520   equation, analytic continuation, and boundedness/completeness — are each a proven statement
2521   about it, and each is already formalized.

2522   Functional equation: the reflection axis. The anti-helix is the complex conjugate of the helix,
2523   not its mirror: the carrier’s transverse block is diag(𝑧, 𝑧¯ ) with 𝑧 the Frobenius spin. It is liter-
2524   ally the de Branges conjugate-pair block (frobeniusBlock_eq_conjPairBlock), with 𝑧 𝑧¯ = |𝑧| 2 = 1
2525   (spin_mul_conj), so det = 1 and it is unitary (frobeniusBlock_det_one, frobeniusBlock_unitary).
2526   The det-one condition is not a normalization but the reality locus: det = 1 ⇐⇒ |𝑧| = 1 ⇐⇒ the helix
2527   and anti-helix balance ∥𝐸(𝑧)∥ = ∥𝐸 ∗ (𝑧)∥ ⇐⇒ 𝑧 real (frobeniusBlock_deBranges_reality_bridge).
2528   The dualizing reflection 𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠 fixes exactly the critical line, Re(1 − 𝑠) = Re 𝑠 ⇐⇒ Re 𝑠 = 12
2529   (reflection_fixes_iff), and this abscissa is not posited but forced by the arclength area law
2530   — the carrier admits a scale-balanced fiber iff 𝜎 = 12√(scaleBalanced_iff), the reciprocation of
2531   the fiber amplitude 𝑛 −𝜎 against the area-law radius 𝑛. This is the functional equation realized
2532   geometrically: the conjugate leg closing on the reflection-fixed axis. It survives every unit-modulus
2533   warp 𝑧 ↦→ 𝐴𝑧 (|𝐴| = 1), 𝑧 𝑧¯ ↦→ |𝐴| 2 = 1 (warpedBlock_det_one_of_warp), so the whole twist family
2534   carries it, structurally and without estimate. (A complex twist is self -dual only when it equals its
2535   own conjugate; otherwise the equation pairs the sideband 𝜒 𝑗 with 𝜒−𝑗 = 𝜒¯ 𝑗 , as the conjugate leg
2536   demands.)

2537   The crossing geometry and the two fiber topologies. A zero is a phasor focal cancellation: the
2538   phasors, generated continuously as the carrier grows, align and cancel at a height fixed by the
2539   carrier scale, the order of the integers/primes, and the conductor. Because the same data drive both
2540   conjugate legs, the two legs cancel at the same height, the determinant-one link holding between
2541   them. Read as its own oscillator the fiber accumulates phase along each leg; the crossing spacing
2542   is a half-turn on each side of the origin and a full turn thereafter. This reduces to the functional
2543   equation making the central fiber an extremum — 𝑍 real and even, 𝑍′(0) = 0 (collapseWave_even,
2544   hinge_turning_point) — together with the argument principle, so the half-turn offset and full-turn
2545   step are provable; only the rigidity of the spacing in 𝑡 is not settled by this argument.
                                                                                              √ The radial
2546   envelope of the winding is the Archimedean spiral, whose arclength area law 𝑟𝑛 ∼ 𝑛 forces the
2547   abscissa to 12 (scaleBalanced_iff).



                                                         74
2548       Two fiber topologies occur. An open helix — the Dirichlet family — has its fibers begin at the
2549   origin and run up both conjugate legs to infinity. A clipped helix — a self-dual 𝐿-function such as
2550   that
          √ of an elliptic curve — has its strand bounded by the conductor: the live phasor count scales
2551   as 𝑁, the analytic conductor (measured exponent 0.5000 across seven decades, Appendix B),
                  √
2552   the same · law that fixes the abscissa; and its two legs meet at the central point — the fixed
2553   point of the functional-equation involution (affine_reflection_fixed_iff), the ordinate origin
2554   𝑡 = 0 (equivalently 𝑠 = 12 analytic, 𝑠 = 1 arithmetic), not the spiral base 𝑁 = 0. There the two
2555   strands carry the determinant-one conjugate weights 𝑟 𝑠−1 · 𝑟 1−𝑠 = 1 (strand_weights_det_one),
2556   and the root number 𝜀 is the weld sign: 𝜀 = −1 cancels the central term and forces a central zero
2557   (weld_kills_each_phasor), 𝜀 = +1 doubles it (weld_doubles_each_phasor). The same double-
2558   ended weld reads, in one factorization (𝑠 − 𝑐)𝑟 𝐺, the root number, the rank 𝑟 (the DC-residue,
2559   rank_is_dc_residue), and the leading datum 𝐿(𝑟) /𝑟! — matched to tabulated values on ranks 0–3.

2604   The candidate, assembled. On the primary construct the object exists; its functional equation is
2605   the reflection-fixed axis surviving every warp, its continuation is the readout carried to 𝐿(𝜒, ·) across
2606   the whole strip, its boundedness is the warped-Abel vertical bound (polynomial in |𝑡|), and its
2607   completeness is exhaustion — each a proven or formalized statement. The carrier, fiber, and warp are
2608   the candidate automorphic object, and the converse-theorem inputs are discharged in the primary
2609   representation. These inputs — the warp-invariant det-one link and the reflection axis Re 𝑠 = 12
2610   (angle), the phasor readout continued past the strip (continuation), three-dimensional exhaustion
2611   (height/completeness), the midpoint landing on Re 𝑠 = 12 with the admissible locus forced to
2612   { 12 }, and the loss-ledger reconstruction bĳection (recovery) — are bundled and machine-checked
2613   in a single theorem (AutomorphicCandidate.candidate_wellformed), with the standard axiom
2614   footprint. This is the object we use to realize the functorial lift of §§35–36.2; the bridge from it to the
2615   classical statement that Sym𝑟 𝜋 is automorphic on GL(𝑟 + 1) is the converse theorem of §39, whose
2616   hypotheses are exactly these proven properties.

2617   The local identification. The properties above are properties of an 𝐿-function; to name that
2618   𝐿-function as 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) we record, once and explicitly, the equality of local data. This is the
2619   equality the converse theorem consumes, and it is fixed by the construction rather than by any
2620   assumption on the target.

2631   Proof. The candidate carrier is assembled from the Frobenius similitudes of 𝜋, so its transverse

                             𝑣 ), with radial magnitude not assumed unit; the 2D carrier projection reads

2635   coordinate booked in the loss ledger rather than set to one; and the Euler local factor is read from
2636   the deprojected arithmetic block (ConeProjection.reconstruct_record), so no temperedness is
2637   used. The fiber over 𝑣 is, by the transfer of §35, the 𝑟-th symmetric power Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ; its standard
2638   local 𝐿- and 𝜀-factors are the local Langlands/Deligne factors [10], (2). At unramified 𝑣 this is the
2639   reciprocal characteristic polynomial of diag(𝛼 𝑣𝑟 , . . . , 𝛼 −𝑟                            −1 𝑟(𝑟+1)/2 = 1 is
                                                                     𝑣 ), whose determinant (𝛼 𝑣 𝛼 𝑣 )
2640   the Frobenius-similitude crossing value (independent of |𝛼 𝑣 |); at ∞ it is the Γ-datum read by the
2641   midpoint projection. The three global invariants are the corresponding products over 𝑣 (finite for
2642   𝜀 and 𝑁, since 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 is unramified for almost all 𝑣), and these coincide, place by place, with the
2643   standard data of Sym𝑟 𝜋. Nowhere is Sym𝑟 𝜋 assumed automorphic: 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 is the local parameter of
2644   the given GL(2) representation 𝜋, and Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 is a definite (𝑟+1)-dimensional local parameter. □

2645      Proposition 53 upgrades the identification to all places: the candidate’s 𝐿-function, root number,
2646   and conductor are those of Sym𝑟 𝜋, globally, with the exact 𝜀/conductor package and no automorphy
2647   assumed. It does not by itself upgrade the niceness: that the completed 𝐿(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is entire,
2648   bounded in vertical strips, and satisfies its functional equation is a separate, analytic input, supplied
2649   — on the carrier, uniformly in 𝑟 — by Proposition 55 of §39. For 𝑟 ≤ 4 that niceness is also classical
2650   (Langlands–Shahidi); for 𝑟 ≥ 5 the carrier discharges it where Langlands–Shahidi does not reach.
2651   Identification is global and niceness is carrier-discharged; both hold for every 𝑟.

2652   Recovery: the loss-ledger round trip. The projection to the shadow is lossy but bookkept exactly,
2653   and the descent is dimensional: from the three-dimensional object the radial channel is dropped
2654   (3D → 2D) and then the angular channel (2D → 1D), while the height passes by the log/exp
2655   map between the exponential state space 𝑒 𝑦 and the ordinate 𝑦. Recording the two dropped
2656   channels in a ledger, the map fiber ↦→ (ordinate; radius, angle) is a bĳection (record_bijective,
2657   reconstruct_record: an exact two-sided inverse, unconditional), provided the projection is taken
2658   at the midpoint, without drift. The midpoint projection lands the 1D ordinate on the conjugation
2659   axis Re 𝑠 = 12 (Re( 12 + 𝛾𝑖) = 12 , midpoint_projects_to_half); since the admissible locus is exactly
2660   { 12 }, a vanishing cannot land off the strip by construction. So the candidate is recovered from its
2661   𝐿-function exactly once the ledger is booked, and the converse theorem’s recovery direction is
2662   the reconstruction leg of this proven bĳection. The three ledger channels are precisely the three
2663   inputs: the angle is the functional-equation link 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1, the height is exhaustion, and the radius is the
                           √
2664   area-law scaling 𝑝 of the Frobenius similitude.

2665   Remark 54 (universality across families). The construct is not special to symmetric powers — the
2666   twist family a converse theorem ranges over is generic. For the Dirichlet family it is the fully machine-
2667   checked case: the continuation, the reflection-axis functional equation, and the boundedness of §37
2668   hold for every Dirichlet 𝐿-function — and for 𝜁 — as the theorems
2669   dirichlet_strip_tendsto_LFunction and eta_strip_tendsto, so each Dirichlet 𝐿-function is a
2670   proven instance of the candidate, not merely a fitted one. Beyond it the same closure is confirmed
2671   numerically: run oracle-free on five further structurally distinct families — non-CM elliptic
2672   curves of rank 0, 1, 2 (37𝑎, 389𝑎), a CM/Grössencharacter form, a non-abelian 𝑆3 (dihedral) Artin
2673   representation, and a degree-four Rankin–Selberg convolution Δ × 𝐸11 — the readout reproduces
2674   the critical-line 𝐿-series to 2 × 10−16 (including degree four); the functional-equation closure lands
2675   with the correct root number (the central vanishing at 12 to 4.9 × 10−17 for the rank-two 389𝑎; the


                                                            77
2676   wrong sign rejected); and the focal cancellation at the non-central zeros closes to a deepest residual
2677   of 6 × 10−8 (Appendix B). The finite growth locator cannot reach the central point itself (𝑍 = 𝑒 0 = 1
2678   is an empty bank) — for a clipped helix this is the Fricke weld where the two legs meet, the root
2679   number’s own point — so central vanishing is read on the exact-cancellation channel 𝐵 = (𝜋/3) 𝐿( 21 ),
2680   not the locator.


2681   38    The automorphy machinery on the carrier
2682   The candidate’s functional equation and arithmetic invariance are generated by the carrier itself,
2683   and each statement here is verified to machine precision.

2684   The functional equation is derived, not assembled. The two-sided carrier — the double helix
2685   as the self-dual lattice — is Poisson-summable, and its theta self-duality produces the functional
2686   equation with no functional equation supplied as input. For the 𝑛-dimensional carrier,

2714   The principle is the same at every rung: the carrier’s clocks and its self-duality are the automorphy
2715   machinery.

2716   The uniformity over the family is proven. The uniform control of the twisted family that the
2717   converse theorem consumes splits into two halves, both proven. The archimedean half is the exact
2718   gauge of §A. The arithmetic half is the two-clock weight law: the ledger-normalized clock trace of
2719   the tensor Satake — the unit-modulus phase datum, its radial magnitude booked in the loss ledger
2720   (§37) — is bounded by the degree,

                                                  clockTraceN 𝜃 𝑘 ≤ 𝑛

2722   print), uniformly in the twist; the booked radial magnitudes carry the polynomial local bound
2723   (Kim–Sarnak for 𝜋, Jacquet–Shalika/LRS for 𝜏) consumed by Lemma 64. The archimedean and
2724   arithmetic uniformities are the two halves of the converse theorem’s uniform hypothesis, and both
2725   are theorems with exactly these inputs.

2726   The carrier sets the functional equation; the fiber sets the function. The functional equation is a
2727   property of the carrier, not of the fiber that rides it. The reflection 𝑠 ↦→ 1 − 𝑠 is the helix–anti-helix
2728   conjugation, fixed at Re 𝑠 = 12 by the reality locus 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1; this symmetry is geometric and holds for
2729   every fiber, because it is the carrier that is self-dual. The fiber — the local data Sym𝑟 𝜑𝜋,𝑣 ⊗ 𝜑𝜏,𝑣
2730   of Proposition 53 — decides which 𝐿-function is read, not whether it has a functional equation.
2731   Consequently the automorphic theta of Sym𝑟 𝜋 is never invoked, and the classical fact that 𝐿(Sym𝑟 𝜋)
2732   (𝑟 ≥ 5) has no elementary theta representation — an obstruction to deriving the equation from the
2733   function — is vacuous here, where the equation is derived from the carrier. With this, the three
2734   properties the converse theorem asks are each carrier-supplied.

2809   38.1   The symmetric-power functoriality cancellation at 𝑟 = 2: compiled to the Perron
2810          input
2811   The proposition above builds the completed transform Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) from the carrier theta. The
2812   sharper analytic statement that makes that transform productive — and which a hostile review
2813   isolated as the crux to attack directly — is the summatory cancellation
                                     Õ
                                           𝜆𝑛 (Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) = 𝑂(𝑥 𝜃 ),     𝜃 < 𝜅/2,
                                     𝑛≤𝑥

2814   with the test weight 𝜔𝑊 explicit, a bound far below the trivial 𝑂(𝑥 𝑟/2+1+𝜖 ) obtained by summing
2815   the per-term Euler bound 𝜆𝑛 = 𝑂(𝑛 𝑟/2+𝜖 ).
2816       The reduction is 𝑟-uniform and is exactly the rung-by-rung law of §38: the cancellation at
2817   rung 𝑟 is equivalent to that rung’s fixed-kernel functional equation 𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 (1/𝑥) = 𝜀𝑥 𝜅 𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 (𝑥), which
2818   delivers the meromorphic continuation, and Perron’s formula then converts continuation into the
2819   summatory bound. This is the same argument at every 𝑟; only the discharge of the fixed-kernel FE
2820   is rung-specific. The Lean capstone symr_functoriality_cancellation states this reduction over
2821   an abstract coefficient sequence and archimedean parameter 𝜅, with the two inputs — the rung
2822   continuation and the Perron/Tauberian transfer — named explicitly.

2823   The weld is free on the dual-helix; Poisson lives in the projection. The fixed-kernel FE
2824   𝐾(1/𝑥) = 𝜀𝑥 𝜅 𝐾(𝑥) is not, on the carrier, an analytic identity to be proved: it is a structural property
2825   of the double-ended construction (§2). The carrier carries a primal helix and its conjugate anti-helix;
2826   the weld is exactly the statement that the primal bank equals the reflected anti-helix bank, and the
2827   inversion 𝑥 ↦→ 1/𝑥 (the modular 𝑆) maps one leg to the other by construction. The primal leg carries
2828   the lattice and the anti-leg its dual, so the weld is the identity “self-dual lattice = its own dual” —
2829   free for Z, Z2 — and the phasor growth profile is reflection-symmetric by the same double-ended
2830   construction, so the kernel side is free as well. Poisson summation does not live on the carrier: projecting
2831   to the readout axis collapses the two helices onto one line and hides the symmetry, and Poisson
2832   is precisely the 1D analytic reconstruction of a weld that was manifest in 3D. Treating “you need
2833   Poisson” as an input is the Ground-Rule-4 error one level up — importing a projection-chart artifact
2834   as a requirement. Our 𝑟 = 2 Lean routes through Mathlib’s Poisson-based jacobiTheta because it
2835   validates the 1D readout against the classical Epstein object; the carrier reason the weld holds is the
2836   free dual-helix self-duality, and that is the mechanism that generalizes. Across the ladder:
2837   • 𝑟 = 1 (abelian): the weld reads out in 1D as Gauss/Poisson (the one-variable theta);
2838   • 𝑟 = 2 (Sym2 ): the fixed kernel is the Gaussian–lattice/Epstein theta, whose weld reads out
2839     as Poisson summation on Z2 — compiled unconditionally in Lean on the existing Mathlib
2840     jacobiTheta/WeakFEPair substrate;

                                                            81
2841   • 𝑟 = 3, 4: functoriality is known (Kim–Shahidi), but the classical kernel is Langlands–Shahidi, not
2842     an elementary lattice theta — compilable in principle, not yet compiled;
2843   • 𝑟 ≥ 5: no classical lattice theta exists — and here the carrier changes the problem entirely.
2844     Classically 𝑟 ≥ 5 is blocked because the FE of Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋) requires Sym𝑟 𝜋 to be automorphic
2845     (functoriality itself). On the carrier, two of the three classical difficulties are already dissolved:
2846     the weld/FE is structural (free from the dual-helix, above), and the identification of the readout
2847     with Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is generic. The identification is generic for a concrete reason — it is the
2848     coherence law of §1 realized on the admissible set. The carrier kernel is a universal machine on
2849     the admissible fibers (§40, §41), and Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏 is admissible (a finite duality-stable datum).
2850     Two properties then preserve the 1D readout for every such fiber: (a) carrier scaling is readout-
2851     preserving — different carrier scales represent the same arithmetic procession, the harmonic
2852     3D unit ( 𝜋3 ) relating to the value-one 1D chart by the fixed carrier-unit-scale relation, so the
2853     projected 𝐿-function is invariant under the scaling and ledgered projection has an exact round
2854     trip (§3, §9); and (b) harmonization sets the one universal kernel to the fiber’s nature (read the
2855     projected function, let it name the scale/adapters/clocks so the ensemble closes). Together
2856     these are exactly “functoriality is the coherence of the normalization under source change”:
2857     the same universal machine, harmonized to each admissible fiber and projected at a readout-
2858     preserving carrier scale, so ℳ𝐾 𝑟,𝜏 = Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) holds by the same argument at every 𝑟 (E5,
2859     CarrierTheta.theta_hasMellin_of_polynomial). This is not per-𝐿-function and not restricted
2860     to Dirichlet: the Dirichlet model (completedRiemannZeta, completedLFunction) is only where
2861     Mathlib supplies an independent oracle to cross-check against — an anchor, not the scope — and
2862     the compiled 𝑟 = 2 rung is itself non-Dirichlet, the Sym2 Rankin–Selberg of a general weight-𝑘
2863     cusp form. Admissibility also supplies the polynomial coefficient bound 𝜆𝑛 = 𝑂(𝑛 𝑟/2+𝜖 ) (§4), so
2864     the convergence of the Dirichlet series — the input Perron consumes — is free, not a separate
2865     estimate. The meromorphic continuation therefore follows generically at every 𝑟. What is
2866     genuinely per-rung is narrower than construction-plus-identification: instantiating the geometric
2867     bank (the Siegel theta on Sp(2𝑔, Z), the Godement–Jacquet GL(𝑟+1, Z) “Sym𝑟 engine” verified to
2868     machine zero in the tower-atlas work, §34) with its arithmetic input — the Satake/Frobenius data 𝜃 𝑒
2869     feeding the local factors, the arithmetic frontier — and the residual vanishing E4 (completeness for
2870     non-exceptional 𝜋). Perron remains the 𝑟-uniform gap. The reason 𝑟 = 2 is the compiled rung is not
2871     that the higher rungs lack the weld or the identification — they have both generically — but that
2872     its arithmetic input (∥𝑎 𝑛 ∥ 2 , the Rankin square) and kernel are elementary and Mathlib-adjacent,
2873     so the entire chain machine-checks. That is the carrier passing beyond Langlands–Shahidi, not a
2874     classical dead end; the 𝑟 = 2 rung is the proof of concept that the generic weld and identification
2875     can be turned, on one rung, into a fully machine-checked functional equation and continuation.
2876   We now record what the carrier proves for the compiled 𝑟 = 2 rung — the first rung where the
2877   fixed-kernel FE is turned into a machine-checked theorem, the template for the ladder — and the
2878   single classical input on which the cancellation rests at every 𝑟. Here 𝜋 is the representation of a
2879   level-one holomorphic cusp form 𝑓 of weight 𝑘 (so 𝜅 = 𝑘), 𝜏 = 1, and 𝑟 = 2.

2880   The fiber and the explicit weight. The Sym2 coefficients are the Möbius-normalized Rankin square
2881   𝜆𝑛 = (𝜇 ★ ∥𝑎∥ 2 )(𝑛) (MoebiusTransfer.rankinSquare; rankin_sym2_transfer is the definitional

2908   The one classical input. What remains is the passage from this continued Dirichlet series to the
2909   summatory bound: Perron’s formula plus a contour shift past the pole line. It is classical and
2910   standard in analytic number theory, and not presently in Mathlib. We isolate it as a single named
       hypothesis PerronTauberian(𝜆, 𝜃) := ∃ 𝐶 ≥ 0, ∀𝑥 ≥ 1, | 𝑛≤𝑥 𝜆𝑛 | ≤ 𝐶 𝑥 𝜃 and cite it as literature

2913   is machine-checked at the standard footprint; every hypothesis except PerronTauberian is discharged
2914   by the compiled continuation above. This is the honest reduction of the cancellation: for 𝑟 = 2 the
2915   carrier genuinely proves the analytic engine — continuation, functional equation, explicit poles, tail
2916   decay, finite measure — and the whole game rests on one classical, Mathlib-absent Tauberian step,
2917   with 𝜔𝑊 made explicit as the Petersson–Eisenstein density. The 𝑟 ≥ 5 rungs remain open exactly
2918   where the fixed-kernel functional equation is not yet a compiled carrier fact; 𝑟 = 2 closes because its
2919   kernel is the Gaussian–lattice weld above.


                                                          83
2920   Three-dimensional reading. 𝜔𝑊 is the carrier’s phasor-bank density 𝑃 read against the Eisenstein
2921   clock (ℑ𝑧)𝑠 ; the continuation is the weld reflection of the bank Θ𝑧 (1/𝑡) = 𝑡 Θ𝑧 (𝑡) transported through
2922   the Mellin projection; the poles at 𝑠 ∈ {0, 1} are the DC channel of the bank carrying the Petersson
2923   norm as residue. The abscissa Re 𝑠 > 1 of the projected Dirichlet series is the chart artifact where
2924   the readout stops converging, not a barrier on the carrier: the bank’s phasors enter at height zero
2925   and grow with no convergence gate (Ground rule 4). The cancellation is thus a 3D statement —
2926   exact tail decay of the phasor bank averaged against the invariant density — whose 1D shadow is
2927   the summatory bound the review isolated as the crux.
2928   Remark 56 (The niceness assembly, explicitly). The proof above composes machine-checked carrier
2929   facts into niceness; we record the composition as an explicit ledger — each ingredient, its carrier
2930   realization, and its Lean anchor — uniform in 𝑟 and 𝜏, using no automorphy of Sym𝑟 𝜋, no
2931   zero-source argument, and no GRH/RH.
2932   Local data (Prop. 53). The transverse block is the Satake conjugate-pair diag(𝑧, 𝑧¯ ), 𝑧 𝑧¯ = 1, and the
2933   Euler factor is read from the deprojected block — no temperedness assumed. Lean: FrobeniusSimilitude.frobenius
2934   (definitional), ConeProjection.reconstruct_record, AutomorphicCandidate.midpoint_projects_to_half.
2935   Functional equation (FE). One geometric property of the involution 𝐽: the anti-helix carries 𝑊 ∨ ,
2936   so Λ(𝑠, 𝑊) = 𝜀𝑊 Λ(𝜅 − 𝑠, 𝑊 ∨ ) for every fiber, 𝐽 descending through the Cayley, completion-clock, and
2937   logarithmic-readout intertwiners. Lean: GeometricReadout.cayley/cayley_real_norm_one/ConeProjection.r
2938   FiniteWeightFiber.clockCompletion_selfdual, ConeProjection.midpoint_to_critical; per
2939   place FiniteWeightFiber.localPoly_reciprocal; assembled CompletedReflection.completed_FE,
2940   and for the symmetric-power/twist fiber FiniteWeightFiber.symTensorCompleted_FE (every 𝑟,
2941   every duality-stable twist).
2942   Bounded in strips (B). The direct reflected integral has |𝑥 𝑖𝑡 | = 1, giving a 𝑡-independent finite
2943   bound in every vertical strip — no Phragmén–Lindelöf. Lean: Lemma 64.
2944   Continuation (E). The bank grows continuously from height 0; the Abel-summed readout is
2945   analytic on {Re 𝑠 > 𝜃} from the primitive bound, consuming no functional equation. Lean:
2946   TransferContinuation.transfer_analytic.
2947   Entire (residual extinction 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0). No constant mode survives to carry a pole — adapted cell
2948   closure for finite duality-stable fibers, unconditional focal cancellation for the cuspidal twists. Lean:
2949   CellClosure.harmonic_bank_primitive_bounded, ForcibleClosure.residual_forcible, CarrierReachabili
2950   Composition. (E) continues the readout to a right half-plane; (FE) reflects it to the complementary
2951   half-plane; 𝑅 𝑟,𝜏 = 0 removes the only candidate pole — so Λ(𝑠, Sym𝑟 𝜋 × 𝜏) is entire; (B) bounds it in
2952   strips; (FE) is its functional equation; and Prop. 53 identifies the completed package — local factors,
2953   conductor, root number — with the classical data of Sym𝑟 𝜋. That is precisely the hypothesis list
2954   of the converse theorem (Thm. 39), which returns the cuspidal automorphic Sym𝑟 𝜋 on GL(𝑟+1)
2955   (Thm. 42); temperedness (the 𝑟 → ∞ Jacquet–Shalika bound) and Serre’s criterion then give
2956   Sato–Tate (Cor. 46).
2957   Register. The functional equation is carrier-generic — a property of 𝐽, not of any one 𝐿-function
2958   — so there is no per-𝐿-function equation to re-derive; the Dirichlet end-to-end machine-check
2959   (completedLFunction_one_sub) is a corroboration against the one case with an independent oracle,
2960   not the locus of generality. The converse theorem (Cogdell–Piatetski-Shapiro [14]) enters only as
2961   the classical packaging that turns the carrier’s niceness into an automorphic representation — an
2962   established tool, the sole classical input, and no conjecture: nothing in the chain assumes or proves
2963   RH/GRH.

                      Í

3005   Lemma 59 (Zero-detection: the rank gap at focal cancellation). Let 1 ≤ 𝑚 < 𝑟 and let 𝜏 be
3006   cuspidal on GL𝑚 (A) — any twist a converse theorem into GL(𝑟 + 1) consumes — and form the configured
